1 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Shamrock Coal Co. v. Maricle


98-SC-0664-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


5 S.W.3d 130; 1999 Ky. LEXIS 144



November 18, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL ACTION FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 98-CA-1046-OA. LESLIE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 97-CI-00015.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant coal company challenged decision of the Kentucky Court of Appeals, which denied appellant's petition for a writ prohibiting the trial court from proceeding in consolidated civil actions brought by plaintiffs, former employees, who alleged that they contracted coal workers' pneumoconiosis as a consequence of their employment.


OVERVIEW: The lower court erroneously concluded that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.690(1) did not confer exclusive jurisdiction on the Workers' Compensation Board to decide matters within the purview of the Workers' Compensation Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.012 et seq., because the case upon which it relied did not overrule the cases holding that exclusive liability cases were jurisdictional. The trial court did not have subject matter jurisdiction over plaintiffs' claims because they brought suit under the Workers' Compensation Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.012 et seq., which conferred exclusive liability to participating employers for all matters falling within the Act's purview. On the face of the complaint, appellant was entitled to protection under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.690(1). Plaintiffs could not sue under the "intentional act" exception of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.690(1) because appellant's conduct was not "willful and unprovoked physical aggression."


OUTCOME: Decision reversed because the lower court erroneously concluded that workers' compensation board did not have exclusive jurisdiction to hear plaintiffs' work-related claims and appellant was entitled to protection under exclusive liability provision of Workers' Compensation Act; the court ordered that writ of prohibition be granted.

 

2 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Dannheiser v. City of Henderson


98-SC-0474-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


4 S.W.3d 542; 1999 Ky. LEXIS 114



September 23, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 96-CA-3230-MR. HENDERSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 95-CI-470.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer was granted discretionary review of a Court of Appeals (Kentucky) decision that affirmed summary judgment for appellee city in a case involving whether the appellee's allegedly below market property sales violated Ky. Const. § 3 and 179.


OVERVIEW: Appellant developer was granted discretionary review of a decision affirming summary judgment for appellee city in appellant's suit seeking damages, declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against appellee, alleging that appellee's sale of municipal property to private companies for less than fair market value violated Ky. Const. § 3 and 179. The court affirmed appellee's summary judgment, holding that appellee's actions were not unconstitutional because they were undertaken for a valid public purpose, to enhance economic development in the area, despite the fact that the activities promoted only local economic development. Appellee's actions were not prohibited by the Kentucky Home Rule Statutes, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 82.081, et seq., because the Local Industrial Development Authority Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 154.50-301 - 154.50-346 was permissive, and did not require appellee to act pursuant to the legislation in order to pursue local economic development.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed because appellee city's actions were not unconstitutional, since they were undertaken for the valid public purpose of enhancing economic development, and because the appellee was not required to act pursuant to local development authority legislation, in order to pursue local economic development.

 

3 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Wolford


97-SC-348-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


4 S.W.3d 534; 1999 Ky. LEXIS 93



August 26, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied November 18, 1999. Released for Publication November 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 95-CA-1204, 95-CA-1254 & 95-CA-1315. PIKE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 93-CR-204.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth of Kentucky sought review of a judgment from the court of appeals, which reversed appellees' convictions of second degree manslaughter and remanded with instructions to dismiss the indictments against appellees on the grounds that the evidence supported a finding of intentional homicide and thus would not support the convictions of second degree manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and reinstated the judgments of convictions and sentences imposed by the trial court. The appellate court had reversed appellees' convictions of second degree murder on the grounds that the evidence supported only a finding of intentional homicide, and thus would not support the convictions of second degree manslaughter. Although only one appellee objected to the jury instruction on second degree murder, the appellate court reversed all three convictions because it found that it was palpable error to instruct the jury on a lesser-included offense unsupported by the evidence. The court held that the giving of an unwarranted instruction on a lesser-included offense more closely inured to defendant's benefit than his prejudice and did not rise to the level of palpable error. Further, given appellees' alibi defense, and the circumstantial evidence which did not conclusively establish appellees' states of mind at the time of the murders, it was appropriate to instruct on all degrees of homicide and leave it to the jury to sort out the facts and determine what inferences and conclusions to draw from the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an appellate judgment overturning appellees' convictions of second degree manslaughter and reinstated the judgments of convictions and sentences imposed by the trial court because given the evidence, it was appropriate to instruct the jury on all degrees of homicide and it was not irrational for the jury to convict appellees of second degree manslaughter.

 

4 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Children's Psychiatric Hosp., Inc. v. Revenue Cabinet


96-SC-1123-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


989 S.W.2d 583; 1999 Ky. LEXIS 43



April 22, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON TRANSFER FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. No. 96-CA-3343. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 93-CI-1460.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted appellant hospitals' motion to transfer the case from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) to consider the constitutionality of a state hospital tax.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hospitals challenged the constitutionality of a state hospital tax. The circuit court granted summary judgment to appellees, state officials. Appellants sought review in the appellate court, but then filed a motion to transfer the issue of the constitutionality of the legislation. The court granted appellants' motion to transfer. On review, the court stated that the legislature had the authority to define certain exemptions and that because the hospital tax was not a property tax, it did not violate Ky. Const. § 170. The court held that there was no violation, as special legislation, of Ky. Const. 59 because the legislation complied with federal guidelines. Because the classification was for a public purpose and was not arbitrary or unreasonable, it was not violative of equal protection and due process provisions. Finally, the title of one provision of the hospital tax was not unconstitutionally misleading, under Ky. Const. § 51, because it gave fair and reasonable notice of the provision. Therefore, the court affirmed the circuit court, holding that the hospital tax was constitutionally valid.


OUTCOME: The court held that a state hospital tax was constitutionally valid and affirmed a circuit court judgment that granted summary judgment to appellees because the tax complied with federal guidelines and the title of one provision gave fair and reasonable notice of the content provisions. Furthermore, the tax was not unconstitutional under equal protection and due process provisions because the classification was not arbitrary or unreasonable.

 

5 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Mills v. Commonwealth


96-SC-966-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


996 S.W.2d 473; 1999 Ky. LEXIS 51



April 22, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1172. Petition for Rehearing Denied August 26, 1999. Released for Publication August 26, 1999.
Rehearing denied by, 08/26/1999
Writ of certiorari denied Mills v. Kentucky, 528 U.S. 1164, 145 L. Ed. 2d 1088, 120 S. Ct. 1182, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1172 (2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Mills v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 150 (Ky., May 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM KNOX CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE RODERICK MESSER, JUDGE. 95-CR-98.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Knox County (Kentucky), convicting him of murder, first degree burglary, and first degree robbery and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, burglary, and robbery and sentenced to death. Defendant made several arguments on appeal, including that no exigent circumstance existed which allowed the police to make a warrantless entry into his home to effectuate his arrest, that the trial court should suppress his confession on grounds that his intoxication and injuries rendered the confession involuntary and unreliable, and that a competency hearing pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 504.100 (3) was mandatory and could not be waived by defendant. The court ruled that the allegation concerning a lack of exigent circumstances was unpreserved, but nevertheless defense counsel could have made no legitimate argument that defendant did not voluntarily consent to the search of his house. Further, the court held that the trial court erred when it failed to hold an evidentiary hearing to determine the admissibility of defendant's confession, but the error was harmless because defendant's confession was voluntary. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, concluding that it was harmless error for the trial court to allow defendant to waive the mandatory competency hearing of § 504.100 (3).


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendant and sentencing him to death was affirmed where defense counsel could have made no legitimate argument that defendant did not voluntarily consent to the search of his house, defendant did not appear to be so intoxicated or injured as to render his confession unreliable, the convictions for the three offenses did not violate double jeopardy principles, and death by electrocution was not cruel and unusual punishment.

 

6 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Bowling Green Mun. Utils v. Atmos Energy Corp.


97-SC-300-DG, 97-SC-302-DG, 97-SC-306-DG, 97-SC-312-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


989 S.W.2d 577; 1999 Ky. LEXIS 53



April 22, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended April 27, 1999. Released for Publication May 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 95-CA-1319. WARREN CIRCUIT COURT. HON. THOMAS R. LEWIS, JUDGE. (94-CI-259).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a Court of Appeals (Kentucky) decision which held that, in an action for damages from a natural gas explosion, allocation of extra peremptory challenges to plaintiffs was a violation of Ky. R. Civ. P. 47.03 and that there was insufficient evidence to justify a punitive damage award against defendant corporation. Defendant utility, defendant contractor, and defendant engineer appealed the remand for retrial against them.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendants for damages from a natural gas explosion and fire. A jury awarded plaintiffs both compensatory and punitive damages solely against defendant corporation, a gas company. The appellate court held that allocation of extra peremptory challenges to plaintiffs violated Ky. R. Civ. P. 47.03, and the evidence was insufficient for punitive damages. On remand, the appellate court directed a retrial against all defendants. On review, the court affirmed, in part, holding that allowing extra peremptory challenges was reversible error because no antagonistic interests were shown by co-parties, as required by Ky. R. Civ. P. 47.03, and because the provision was elevated to a substantive right. Although Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.184(1)(c) was held to be unconstitutional after trial, the malice standard was used in holding that there was insufficient evidence for punitive damages because plaintiffs showed no oppression, fraud, or malice, under § 411.184(2). Relitigation against three defendants was reversed because plaintiffs did not appeal the verdict. The case was remanded for retrial against defendant corporation only on liability and compensatory damages.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's decision in a damages case was affirmed, in part, because extra peremptory challenges to plaintiffs was reversible error and because evidence was insufficient for punitive damages against defendant corporation. The case was reversed, in part, because retrial against three defendants was improper since plaintiff did not appeal verdict in their favor. The case was remanded for retrial against defendant corporation only.

 

7 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Neal v. Fiscal Court


96-SC-000566-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


986 S.W.2d 907; 1999 Ky. LEXIS 24



March 25, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 96-CA-1526. HONORABLE F. KENNETH CONLIFFE, JUDGE. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT NO. 95-CI-003579.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) that held that a court resolution created a lawful means of allocating funds for the transportation of non-public elementary children consistent with Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. 158.115.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer appealed a trial court decision that a resolution created a lawful means of allocating funds for the transportation of non-public elementary school children consistent with Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 158.115. The appellate court affirmed and held that the resolution was consistent with § 158.115(2) and was constitutionally proper as a lawful method of allocating transportation subsidies. The transportation subsidies were paid directly to the individual local board of education-operated transportation system of contracted bus and vehicle companies. No funds passed into private or parochial schools. The court held that the procedure was in direct accordance with § 158.115(2), which specifically stated that the county may provide such transportation by means of local board of education-operated transportation systems, transit authorities organized and operating local governmental mass transit systems, and individual contracted buses and vehicles pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 96A. The benefit provided went directly toward the safety and welfare of elementary age school children, providing only an indirect, remote or incidental effect on the nonpublic schools.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that declared as constitutional a resolution providing funds for the transportation of non-public school children because the funds allocated flowed directly to the providers of transportation, providing only an indirect, remote, or incidental effect on the nonpublic schools. The main effect was greater protection for the safety and welfare of the children who attended the schools.

 

8 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Land v. Commonwealth


98-SC-000427-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


986 S.W.2d 440; 1999 Ky. LEXIS 13



February 18, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW FORM COURT OF APPEALS. 97-CA-001479. DAVIESS CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE GARLAND W. HOWARD, JUDGE. NO. 16980.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Daviess Circuit Court (Kentucky), which denied his motion under Ky. R. Crim. P. 60.02 to make him eligible for parole or to amend the judgment that sentenced him, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 435.090, to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole following his rape conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and sentenced to life imprisonment for one count of murder, life without the possibility of parole on each of two counts of rape, 21 years on each of two counts of shooting with the intent to kill, and 18 years for one count of armed robbery. Twenty-five years after the convictions, appellant filed a motion under Ky. R. Crim. P. 60.02 to amend the judgment or to make him eligible for parole. Appellant claimed that the sentence of life without the possibility of parole for rape imposed pursuant to former Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 435.090 was an unconstitutional sentence in violation of U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV. Appellant argued that because of the changes in sentencing laws regarding crimes of violence, and in view of the commutation of the sentences of almost all other rape offenders sentenced to life without the possibility of parole, his sentence must be deemed cruel punishment and a denial of equal protection and due process in violation of state and federal constitutions. The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which denied appellant's motion, holding that appellant's sentence was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that denied appellant's motion to make him eligible for parole or to amend the judgment that sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole for rape. Regardless of the changes in the state sentencing laws after appellant's conviction for rape, the sentence was not cruel punishment and did not deny him due process and equal protection of the law.

Kentucky Sheriffs Ass'n v. Fischer


98-SC-858-TG, 98-SC-859-TG, 98-SC-860-TG, 98-SC-861-TG, 98-SC-862-TG, 98-SC-863-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


986 S.W.2d 444; 1999 Ky. LEXIS 18



February 18, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 98-CA-2442. CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT NO. 98-CI-604.

ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 98-CA-2472. CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT NO. 98-CI-604.

ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 98-CA-2516. CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT NO. 98-CI-604.

ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 98-CA-2503. CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT NO. 98-CI-604.

ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 98-CA-2504. CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT NO. 98-CI-604.

ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 98-CA-2538. CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT NO. 98-CI-604.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public officials sought review of a judgment from the Campbell Circuit Court (Kentucky), which enjoined the enforcement of House Bill 810, 1998 Ky. Acts 610 (the bill) after holding that it was unconstitutional and that the general assembly had exceeded its legislative powers in passing the bill.


OVERVIEW: After the state general assembly determined in House Bill 810, 1998 Ky. Acts 610 (the bill) that sheriffs, county judges, county clerks, and jailers who operated full service jails had duties coextensive with the commonwealth, it added them to the category of public officers eligible to be compensated under Ky. Const. § 246's highest compensation level. Shortly thereafter, appellee attorney general filed an action for declaratory relief challenging the constitutionality of the bill's salary provisions under § 246. The appellate court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which enjoined the enforcement of the bill after finding the bill unconstitutional and holding that the general assembly had exceeded its legislative powers. The appellate court held that the general assembly did not exceed its legislative powers, but rather made a legislative finding of fact that classified certain public officials in the highest compensation category. Further, the court held that the general assembly's factual finding supported the constitutionality of the bill and did not violate the compensation limits of § 246.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that enjoined the enforcement of a house bill where the general assembly did not improperly authorize compensation for public officials in excess of the maximum compensation limits set forth in the state constitution. The general assembly did not exceed its legislative powers in passing the bill and the general assembly's factual finding supported the constitutionality of the bill.

 

10 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Shockey Tours, Inc. v. Miller Transp., Inc.


97-SC-511-DG and 97-SC-528-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


984 S.W.2d 95; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 163



December 17, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 96-CA-175-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT, CIVIL ACTION NO. 94-CI-749 & 1464. HON. ROGER CRITTENDEN, JUDGE.

ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 96-CA-175-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT, CIVIL ACTION NO. 94-CI-749 & 1464. HON. ROGER CRITTENDEN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicants sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) that reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court upholding the decision of the Department of Vehicle Registration to grant certificates of public convenience and necessity to appellants under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 281.637(4).


OVERVIEW: Appellant applicants operated chartered bus services and applied to the Department of Vehicle Registration (Department) for charter bus operations over irregular intrastate routes. Appellee protestants objected. The Department granted the requested certificates of public convenience and necessity, and the trial court affirmed following an appeal by one appellee. The Department had dismissed the other appellees for lack of standing. The appellate court reversed and held that appellant applicants did not hold a valid certificate at the time of their original application and were, thus, not entitled to the benefits of the "grandfather clause" of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 281.637(4). In affirming the judgment of the appellate court and remanding to the trial court, the court held that appellants were not included in the grandfather provisions because they did not operate a regular route or a common-carrier passenger service, and that the appellate court was not bound to follow the statutory interpretations of the Department that were erroneous. The court also ruled that based on Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 281.625(1)(b), it was error for the Department to have dismissed appellees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court that had reversed the decision to grant appellant applicants certificates of public convenience and necessity because it found that appellants were not included within the applicable grandfather clause. It also found that it had been error for the trial court to dismiss appellee protestants for lack of standing. The court remanded the matter to the trial court.

 

11 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. Kentucky Bar Ass'n


97-SC-757-KB


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


980 S.W.2d 560; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 166



December 17, 1998, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 6, 1998.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movants, commissioner of the workers' claims department and workers' compensation specialists, requested a review of an opinion of respondent, Kentucky Bar Association, which concluded that the duties assigned the non-attorney workers' compensation specialists would be duties normally performed by an attorney and therefore constituted the unauthorized practice of law.


OVERVIEW: After the legislature enacted Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.320(9), which authorized non-lawyer service representatives to represent injured workers, employers, and insurance carriers in proceedings before the Department of Workers' Claims, respondent bar association issued an advisory opinion disallowing the use of non-lawyers in any capacity as service representatives. Movants, commissioner of the workers' claims department and workers' compensation specialists, sought review of the opinion. The court affirmed the opinion in part and reversed in part, finding that most of the duties of service representatives, primarily administrative, did not constitute the practice of law, and if they did, they were properly supervised by an attorney. However, the court found that their representation of clients before the department was the unauthorized practice of law. Thus, the court declared the portion of statute that allowed such representation, § 342.320(9), unconstitutional, concluding that the legislature exceeded its authority by enacting a statute that infringed upon the power of the judicial branch to regulate the practice of law.


OUTCOME: The court held that the statute was unconstitutional because it allowed non-lawyer service representatives to represent clients before the adjudicatory board. Therefore, the court affirmed the part of respondent bar association's opinion that disallowed unsupervised representation of clients by non-lawyers, but overruled the part that disallowed the service representatives from performing lawyer-supervised administrative duties.

 

12 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Kentucky Indus. Util. Customers, Inc. v. Kentucky Utils. Co.


97-SC-1091-DG, 97-SC-1095-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


983 S.W.2d 493; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 165



December 17, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 95-CA-2487; 95-CA-2515; 95-CA-2605 and 95-CA-2687-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT CIVIL ACTION NO. 94-CI-1399.

ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 95-CA-2478; 95-CA-2515; 95-CA-2605 and 95-CA-2687-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT CIVIL ACTION NO. 94-CI-1399.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ratepayers and appellees, utilities and the Kentucky Public Service Commission, sought review of a decision of the Kentucky Court of Appeals, affirming in part and reversing in part a circuit court judgment, which found that the Environmental Surcharge Statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 278.183, was constitutional and that its retroactive application violated Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 446.080(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant ratepayers challenged a surcharge by appellee utilities, which was approved by appellee, Kentucky Public Service Commission, under the Environmental Surcharge Statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 278.183, to recover their costs for pollution control devices. The trial court found that the statute was constitutional but that retroactive application violated Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 446.080(3). The court of appeals affirmed in part and reversed in part, allowing recovery for environmental compliance projects already in existence. The court affirmed the decision upholding the constitutionality but reversed in part, disallowing recovery for costs incurred prior to the effective date of the statute. The court held that the surcharge statute was rationally related to a legitimate interest in securing a sound economy. The court held that the statute was uniformly applied and that appellants had no vested property rights in the rates they paid to support a claim of a due process violation. The court found no evidence of a legislative intent that the statute should be applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that a statute allowing appellee utilities to recover their costs for pollution control devices through an environmental surcharge on appellant ratepayers did not violate constitutional rights of due process and equal protection. Retroactive application by appellee Kentucky Public Service Commission was contrary to clear legislative intent and a violation of law.

 

13 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Yeoman v. Commonwealth Health Policy Bd.


97-SC-274-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


983 S.W.2d 459; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 140; 22 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2461



November 19, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 18, 1999. Released for Publication February 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON TRANSFER FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 96-CA-3315. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROGER CRITTENDEN, JUDGE. (94-CI-1663).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, doctors and their patients, challenged the order from the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) granting summary judgment to appellees, commonwealth and health policy board, and upholding the constitutionality of House Bill 250, which provided for wide-ranging health care reforms.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, doctors and their patients, challenged the constitutionality of House Bill 250. The bill provided wide-ranging health care reforms, including medical taxation. The trial court granted the motion for summary judgment filed by appellees, commonwealth and health policy board, upholding the constitutionality of the bill. On appeal, the court affirmed. Among its conclusions, the court found that the bill did not violate Ky. Const. § 59 because there was a valid nexus between the classification and the purpose for which the statute was drafted. The bill was not special legislation because it did not favor a special interest to the detriment of the rest of society. Moreover, the bill's provider tax was not random and arbitrary because the tax was specifically tailored to acquire federal matching funds. Using the rational basis test, the court concluded that the provider tax did not adversely affect a fundamental interest. The court found that raising revenue was not the primary purpose of the bill; therefore, Ky. Const. § 47 was not violated. There was no violation of privacy rights because data collected regarding patients' identities were shielded from public examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted summary judgment to appellees, commonwealth and health policy board, and upholding the constitutionality of legislation providing health care reforms. The court found that the bill did not favor a special interest and that purpose of the bill was the improvement of appellee commonwealth's health care system.

 

14 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Gray v. Commonwealth


97-SC-339-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


979 S.W.2d 454; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 130



October 15, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CHRISTIAN CIRCUIT COURT. HON. EDWIN M. WHITE, JUDGE. (96-CR-00493).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was charged with three counts of first-degree trafficking in a Schedule II controlled substance and of being a persistent felony offender in the second degree. He was convicted in the Christian Circuit Court (Kentucky). Appellant challenged his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that he was twice placed in jeopardy for the same offense when he was convicted of two counts of trafficking in cocaine based upon a single sale in violation of the double jeopardy prohibitions of the United States and Kentucky Constitutions. He also argued that his sentence was improperly enhanced. The court found that the second transaction that appellant was convicted of did occur on the same date as the first transaction and did involve the same type of substance, cocaine, but the second transaction occurred at a different time and resulted in the transfer of a separate quantity of cocaine. As such, the second transaction was separate and distinct and did not result in an unconstitutional prosecution. The court also found that where the prosecution split a prior felony conviction into two components, the result was an improper enhancement of appellant's conviction to both a subsequent trafficking offender and a persistent felony offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction from the trial court, but found that his sentence was improperly enhanced and remanded for matter for resentencing.

 

15 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Democratic Party v. Graham


98-SC-685-D and 98-SC-688-TG, 98-SC-687-D and 98-SC-689-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


976 S.W.2d 423; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 126



September 18, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Order Granting Motion to Vacate September 24, 1998. Order Correcting Opinion October 15, 1998. Released for Publication October 15, 1998. As Corrected October 15, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT OF APPEALS. 98-CA-2019-OA.

COURT OF APPEALS. 98-CA-1981-OA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner political contributors sought a writ of mandamus in the Kentucky Court of Appeals, to compel respondent circuit court judge to prohibit a grand jury from returning indictments against contributors unless Kentucky's Registry of Election Finance determined that there was probable cause to believe that a violation of a campaign finance law had occurred. The appellate court recommended transfer.


OVERVIEW: The trial court instructed the grand jury to proceed with its deliberations and the performance of its duties in secrecy. Contributors objected that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 121.120(5) and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 121.140(5) precluded the grand jury from proceeding until the Registry determined that there was probable cause to believe a violation had occurred. The court held that while the Registry was empowered to investigate alleged violations of campaign finance laws and to impose civil sanctions for non-criminal violations, its investigative authority was not exclusive, but was concurrent with traditional law enforcement agencies to investigate suspected criminal activity. The Registry's authority, not the Attorney General's, was limited by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 121.140(5). The Attorney General was not required to wait for the Registry to make a probable cause determination before conducting his own investigation and submitting his evidence to a properly constituted grand jury.


OUTCOME: The court denied contributors' petitions for a writ of mandamus and vacated the trial court's order granting emergency relief.

Sisters of Charity Health Sys. v. Raikes


97-SC-118-MR, 97-SC-124-MR, 97-SC-205-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


984 S.W.2d 464; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 120



September 3, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 18, 1999. Released for Publication February 18, 1999. As Corrected March 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 96-CA-2965-OA. NELSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LARRY D. RAIKES, JUDGE. 95-CI-212.

APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 96-CA-2968-OA. NELSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LARRY D. RAIKES, JUDGE. 95-CI-212.

APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 97-CA-0009-OA. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM E. McANULTY, JR., JUDGE. 94-CI-1811.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical care providers sought review, as a matter of right, of decisions of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which denied the medical care providers' petitions for a writ of prohibition to prevent appellee trial court judges from enforcing an order compelling discovery of peer review records in a medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: In three combined appeals brought by the medical care providers, the issue presented was whether the peer review privilege established by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 311.377(2) prohibited discovery of peer review records in medical malpractice suits. The court found no error in the lower courts' determination that the privilege did not extend to medical malpractice actions and further found that the privilege was limited to actions against the peer review entities, as provided in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 311.377(1). The court further determined that a decision finding a prior peer review statute unconstitutional because of a violation of the single subject provision of Ky. Const. § 51 was not in conflict because the court based its decision in the present case entirely on statutory construction rather than on constitutional grounds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decisions denying the medical care providers' petitions for writ of prohibition.

Commonwealth v. Howard


97-SC-764-TG, 98-SC-06-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


969 S.W.2d 700; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 95



June 18, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 97-CA-1994-DG. APPEAL FROM DAVIESS CIRCUIT COURT. HON. GARLAND W. HOWARD, JUDGE. CRIMINAL ACTION NO. 97-XX-03.

TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 97-CA-2452. APPEAL FROM LAUREL CIRCUIT COURT. HON. LEWIS B. HOPPER, JUDGE. CRIMINAL ACTION NO. 97-XX-04.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED CASE NO. 97-SC-764 and AFFIRMED CASE NO. 98-SC-06.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two cases were transferred from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) because they both were appeals based on whether the juvenile DUI statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §189A.010(1)(e), was constitutional. In one case, the under-21 defendant was convicted and in the other, the statute was found to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Two cases were transferred to the court because both appeals were based on the alleged unconstitutionality of the juvenile DUI statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §189A.010(1)(e). The court reversed the lower court decision that found the statute to be unconstitutional and affirmed the decision that convicted defendant of the statutory crime. The court held that because driving an automobile was not a fundamental constitutional right but a legitimately regulated privilege, and because it did not impact on a suspect class negatively, the rational basis standard would apply. The court found that the statute furthered the legitimate state purpose of preventing drunk driving accidents and was therefore constitutional. The court concluded that the statute also did not violate the Kentucky constitution because the classification provided in the statute was based on neutral, real, and substantial distinctions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the case where the juvenile DUI statute was found to be unconstitutional and affirmed the case where the under-21-year-old was found guilty of violating the statute. The court held that the statute was constitutional under the rational basis standard.

 

19 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Owens-Corning Fiberglas Corp. v. Golightly


96-SC-970-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


976 S.W.2d 409; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 97; Bankr. L. Rep. (CCH) P15,292



June 18, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Order Denying Petition for Stay of Execution August 7, 1998. Petition for Rehearing Denied October 15, 1998. Released for Publication October 15, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 95-CA-135. MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JAMES R. DANIELS, JUDGE. 92-CI-303.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a products liability action involving exposure to products containing asbestos, appellee injured party was awarded recovery from appellant manufacturer of both compensatory and punitive damages. The judgment and damages awards were affirmed by a court of appeals (Kentucky) and the manufacturer sought review.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer claimed that it was entitled to a directed verdict on the issue of punitive damages. Manufacturer also claimed that the punitive damages violated due process and that it was erroneously denied a state-of-the-art instruction. The court held that there was substantial evidence to overcome the motion for a directed verdict. The court found that the manufacturer knew of the health risks associated with its product before it was placed in the stream of commerce and that it knowingly marketed the product without warnings. The court also found that the manufacturer concealed, minimized and/or misrepresented the health risks. The court rejected the manufacturer's claim that successive punishments for the same course of conduct violated due process. The court also held that it provided actual review of punitive damages award. The court found that Ky. R. Civ. P. 59.01 provided trial court review of awards, which were upheld on appeal only if they were supported by substantial evidence. The court also found that the manufacturer waived its objection to its state-of-the art instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the punitive damages award entered against the manufacturer.

 

20 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Wilson


96-SC-1122-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


972 S.W.2d 260; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 63



April 16, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied August 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 94-CA-2200-MR. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 92-CI-240.

ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 94-CA-2200-MR. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 92-CI-240. HONORABLE MARY C. NOBLE, JUDGE. (92-CI-240).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appellee claimant's action for damages against appellant tortfeasor, claimant requested an instruction on punitive damages. The tortfeasor objected on the grounds that there was insufficient evidence under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.184 to warrant a punitive damages instruction. The trial court declared § 411.184 unconstitutional and submitted a punitive damages instruction. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) affirmed and the tortfeasor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lower courts found that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.184 violated §§ 14, 54, and 241 of the Kentucky Constitution because it altered common law rights of recovery for negligent conduct. The tortfeasor argued that the right to punitive damages was not one of the common law rights in effect at the time the constitution was in enacted and protected by §§ 14, 54, and 241, and, alternatively, that the new statute did not change the common law standard for punitive damages. The court found that although the language of the cases varied, there was little doubt that prior to 1891, the year the constitution was passed, punitive damages could be recovered in Kentucky for negligent conduct. The court also found that the element of subjective awareness of negligence required under the statute was a clear change in the common law, which only required gross negligence, conduct lacking intent or actual knowledge of the result. The court also found that the jural rights doctrine, which interpreted §§ 14, 54, and 241 to inhibited legislative abolition of rights of action for damages for death or injuries caused by negligence, was supported by the language of the constitutional provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Combs v. Commonwealth


97-SC-217-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


965 S.W.2d 161; 1998 Ky. LEXIS 33



March 19, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 95-CA-2978. MADISON CIRCUIT COURT. HON. JULIA ADAMS, JUDGE. CRIMINAL ACTION NO. 94-CR-82.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), convicting him of driving under the influence (DUI) based on his conditional plea of guilty and sentencing him to two years' probation.


OVERVIEW: Following defendant's arrest, police obtained a search warrant in order to test his blood alcohol level. The court held that the plain language of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 189A.105 prohibited compelled body searches of DUI suspects following their refusal to take a blood test, unless death or physical injury were involved. In defendant's case, there was no death or physical injury involved. The court found that the admission, therefore, of the results of the blood test was improper, but it affirmed the conviction because of the overwhelming other evidence of defendant's intoxication at the time of his arrest. The blood test evidence was merely cumulative and thus, harmless error in defendant's case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

22 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. Cabinet for Human Resources


96-SC-610-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


954 S.W.2d 317; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 127



October 30, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 96-CA-1114-D. WARREN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS R. LEWIS, JUDGE. 95-XX-53.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kentucky Court of Appeals denied discretionary review of an appeal by appellant biological father. The appeal was of the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees, a mother and the Cabinet for Human Resources. The lower courts had held that the biological father had failed to rebut the presumption contained in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 406.111. The biological father appealed, and the court granted discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: The mother of a child was subject to a divorce decree, which incorporated an acknowledgment that the child was the son of the mother's ex-husband. The acknowledgment was made even though, before the entry of the divorce decree, paternity testing had excluded the ex-husband as the child's father. The mother then sought child support from the biological father, who was determined years after the mother's divorce decree. The court found that the biological father could not assert res judicata because he was not a party to the prior divorce action. However, the court also held that the paternity issue could not be relitigated by the mother because of the doctrine of collateral estoppel, or issue preclusion. Under collateral estoppel, a person who was not a party to the former action could assert res judicata against a party to that action, so as to preclude the relitigation of an issue determined in the prior action. The prior action was the divorce decree, which was a final judgment on the merits of the case. Paternity issues were necessary issues to the dissolution action, which the mother had a full and fair opportunity to litigate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court. The action was remanded to the district court for an order dismissing the petition for summary judgment, filed by the mother and the Cabinet for Human Resources.

 

23 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Estes v. Commonwealth


96-SC-750-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


952 S.W.2d 701; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 115



October 2, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 23, 1997.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was cited under Ky. Rev. Stat. § 304.99-060 for operating an uninsured motor vehicle. Upon defendant's conditional guilty plea, the trial court sentenced him to jail and fined him. On appeal, the Nicholas Circuit Court reversed defendant's conviction. Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) that reversed the circuit court's decision and reinstated his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was not the owner of the uninsured motor vehicle. The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals that reversed the circuit court's reversal of defendant's conviction because under § 304.99-060 a non-owner, operator of a motor vehicle could not be assessed criminal penalties for driving an uninsured motor vehicle. The court found that § 304.99-060 did not designate a substantive offense, as it merely stated the penalty for the violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 304.39-080(5). Section 304.39-080 only required motor vehicle owners to provide insurance for their motor vehicles. The court concluded that the amendment of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 304.99-060, which brought motor vehicle operators into its purview, could not serve to create a substantive offense when one did not previously exist as to operators. Thus, § 304.99-060 could not apply to non-owner operators of motor vehicles.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals' decision and reinstated the circuit court's decision that dismissed defendant's conviction for operating a motor vehicle that was not insured.

Burns v. Level


95-SC-1120-DG, 96-SC-887-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


957 S.W.2d 218; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 109



October 2, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied and Opinion Modified January 22, 1998. Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 93-CA-1469, 93-CA-1470. BOONE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 90-CI-092.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist commenced an action against appellees, a company and its truck driver, which sought damages for the injuries sustained in a traffic accident. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the motorist except for the issues of damages. That matter was remanded for a new trial on the issue of damages for medical expenses. Cross-appeals of that judgment were taken by the parties.


OVERVIEW: The motorist was injured when a car was struck by a vehicle operated by the truck driver. Evidence was introduced that the motorist's medical expenses had been covered by collateral sources. A jury found in the motorist's favor and apportioned fault between the parties. It also returned a zero verdict as compensation for the motorist's medical expenses. On appeal, the court determined that introduction of the collateral source evidence was not error. In that regard, the court noted that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.188, which allowed the admissibility of such evidence, had been declared unconstitutional. However, that decision was rendered nearly two years after the parties' trial. Therefore, the trial court did not commit palpable error, which would have excused the motorist's failure to preserve that issue for appeal, when it allowed the collateral source evidence. Moreover, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189.390(6), which established the duty owed by a driver, was applicable to accidents that occurred on interstate highways. The trial court also properly directed a verdict on the motorist's claim for permanent impairment to earn money because she did not comply with Ky. R. Civ. P. 8.01(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment in part and reversed in part. That judgment was reversed with regard to its remand for a new trial on the issue of damages for medical expenses and otherwise affirmed. The trial court's verdict and judgment was affirmed in its entirety. This matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

25 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Grimes v. McAnulty


95-SC-745-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


957 S.W.2d 223; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 118



October 2, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied January 22, 1998. Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL ACTION FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 95-CA-001487.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which denied her petition for a writ of prohibition that challenged the trial court's decision to grant the commonwealth's motion for a mistrial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder and was near the end of her trial when the commonwealth moved for a mistrial. The commonwealth contended that defendant's testimony did not support her self-defense theory and that improper evidence had been admitted earlier in the trial. The trial court granted the commonwealth's motion and defendant filed an application for a writ of prohibition. The appellate court denied defendant's application and the court affirmed. The court found that a retrial was precluded if a mistrial was granted without defendant's consent and in the absence of a manifest necessity to do so, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 505.030(4). The court held that a manifest necessity existed because defendant introduced improper evidence that prejudiced the commonwealth's right to a fair trial. The court determined that defendant's testimony indicated that the shooting was an accident, but she introduced self-defense evidence. The court reasoned that these defenses were inconsistent and self-defense was improper. The court overruled Pace v. Commonwealth, 561 S.W.2d 664 (1978), which had allowed the jury to consider both accident and self-defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court, which denied defendant's application for a writ of prohibition to challenge the trial court's decision to grant the commonwealth's motion for a mistrial.

Miller v. East Ky. Beverage/Pepsico


96-SC-0516-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


951 S.W.2d 329; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 95



September 4, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 95-CA-001374. WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD NO. 93-026266.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed the decision of appellee Workers' Compensation Board. The Board had affirmed the decision by appellee, an administrative law judge, who awarded the employee 28 percent permanent partial occupational disability for a back injury from appellee employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee injured his back while unloading cases of soft drinks for the employer. The employee filed a claim for workers' compensation. The administrative law judge awarded the employee 28 percent permanent partial occupational disability. The decision was affirmed by the board and by the court of appeals. On appeal, the court affirmed the award. The court held that there was no violation of equal protection from the implementation of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 342.0011(11) under the Fourteenth Amendment to the U.S. Constitution and the Prohibition Against Arbitrary Powers, Ky. Const. § 2, because all workers were treated the same and were required to abide by the same rules. The court concluded that the workers' compensation legislation did not treat a class of persons differently from other classes, and an individual's claim of differential treatment was not sufficient to raise an equal protection challenge. The court concluded that the promulgated rules were adequate and substantial evidence supported the administrative law judge's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision affirming the award of 28 percent permanent partial occupational disability to the employee.

 

27 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Franklin County v. Malone


95-SC-0268-DG, 95-SC-0478-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


957 S.W.2d 195; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 105



September 4, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Corrected September 9, 1997. Petition for Rehearing Denied January 22, 1998. Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 93-CA-001539. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 90-CI-000571. HON. ROGER CRITTENDEN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate of deceased prisoner brought a wrongful death action against defendants, county and state, county officials, and state trooper. The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted summary judgment dismissing the action on grounds of sovereign immunity and the court of appeals reversed in part, holding that sovereign immunity in some instances had been waived. The estate and some defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner committed suicide in the restroom of the county jail while he was awaiting formal processing prior to being jailed. The estate charged the trooper and jail employees with direct negligence and the officials and government entities with direct negligence and vicarious liability. On appeal, the court held that the jailer was not liable for acts of his employees in which he was not personally involved. The jailer had no reason to know the prisoner was suicidal, and there was no evidence he violated his duty to provide a safe facility and no evidence his deputy jailers were inadequately trained, managed, and supervised. The county officials were protected by official immunity because the acts alleged to be negligent were discretionary ones. The trooper, in his arrest and search of the prisoner, was acting as an agent of the government and was entitled to immunity. The county's participation in a self-insurance fund did not constitute a waiver of sovereign immunity. The estate's complaint failed to allege a separate cause of action against any individual not acting in an official capacity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and reinstated the summary judgment of the trial court dismissing all claims.

 

28 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Revenue Cabinet v. Gillig


95-SC-1056-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


957 S.W.2d 206; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 91



September 4, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied January 22, 1998. Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 94-CA-1154. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROGER CRITTENDEN, JUDGE. (91-CI-1601).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee coal owners filed an action against appellant revenue cabinet challenging the constitutionality of an interim method of assessing the value of unmined coal. The trial court granted the cabinet summary judgment, but the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) reversed and found that the method was unconstitutional. The court granted discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: The cabinet's interim method of assessing unmined coal was based upon a self-reporting approach that used an information return form that was mailed to the owners. They argued that this method was unconstitutional because it did not consider certain individual characteristics of the property. The trial court found that the method was not arbitrary, but the appellate court reversed. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court's judgment. Under the generally accepted mass appraisal approach, the cabinet was not required to consider all factors that affected the value of unmined coal. Instead, the cabinet was only required to consider those factors to allow it to make a logical and reasonable estimate of the property's fair cash value. Because the owners failed to allege or present evidence that the method resulted in valuations that exceeded the fair cash value of their property or that the method discriminated against them or any other group, the method used by the cabinet was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the trial court's judgment that the cabinet's interim method of assessing unmined coal was constitutional.

Priestley v. Priestley


96-SC-271-DG, 96-SC-803-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


949 S.W.2d 594; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 66



June 19, 1997, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied September 4, 1997. Released for Publication September 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 93-CA-2567 and 93-CA-2436. (Woodford Circuit Court No. 92-CI-057).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult children of father (children) challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed the judgment of the trial court that appellee administratrix of father's estate (administratrix), who was also his wife, had breached her fiduciary duties with respect to her management of assets and dismissed children's claims. Administratrix contended that she should have had a directed verdict.


OVERVIEW: Father was severely disabled and suffered a fall at a hospital that added to his disability. Administratrix served as father's attorney in fact and guardian and brought an action against the hospital for medical negligence and loss of consortium. The settlement proceeds received were allocated between them. As attorney in fact and guardian, administratrix transacted several significant items of business for father and herself. The court agreed with the trial court and held that (1) children had standing because by virtue of father's intestate death, and children were his heirs at law and their rights were greater than an expectancy. (2) The absence of a judgment that declared that administratrix defaulted as a testamentary fiduciary was not a fatal flaw in children's claims because the claims were consistent with Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 395.510. And (3) administratrix was not entitled to a directed verdict because the trial court ruled on each item of her expenditures and found that those expenditures that were not necessaries pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 404.040 constituted a breach of her fiduciary duties. The court declined to decide the constitutionality of § 404.040.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court.

Summe v. Judicial Retirement & Removal Comm'n


96-SC-000034-RR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


947 S.W.2d 42; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 69

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM THE JUDICIAL RETIREMENT AND REMOVAL COMMISSION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND CONCURRED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge sought review of an order from appellee Judicial Retirement and Removal Commission (Kentucky), which found appellant to be in violation of campaign rules by depicting a paper as an independent publication when it was campaign material and for statements in a letter which constituted pre-election commitment on the issue of probation in child abuse cases.


OVERVIEW: Appellant judge challenged an order from appellee Judicial Retirement and Removal Commission which ordered appellant suspended for violations surrounding a campaign for election. On appeal, the court affirmed and modified the suspension. The court found clear and convincing evidence that appellant used a format designed to give the impression to voters that an independent organization advocating child abuse issues supported appellant in her race for circuit judge when the document was campaign material. This was a misrepresentation of fact in violation of Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 4.300. The court agreed with appellee's conclusion that nearly all of the publication's features, both individually and collectively, portrayed the publication as something other than campaign literature. The court also affirmed a finding of misconduct regarding a letter which constituted pre-election commitment on the issue of probation in child abuse cases. The court modified the judgment after a finding that it was excessive and inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellee Judicial Retirement and Removal Commission's finding of misconduct by appellant judge regarding a campaign for election but modified the punishment after a finding that the original judgment was excessive an inappropriate.

Bowling v. Commonwealth


92-SC-1035-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


942 S.W.2d 293; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 54



April 24, 1997, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 24, 1997. Certiorari Denied November 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6977.
Writ of certiorari denied Bowling v. Kentucky, 522 U.S. 986, 118 S. Ct. 451, 139 L. Ed. 2d 387, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6977 (1997)
Subsequent appeal at, Stay vacated by Bowling v. Commonwealth, 964 S.W.2d 803, 45:3 Ky. L. Summary 14, 1998 Ky. LEXIS 26 (Ky., 1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Bowling v. Commonwealth, 80 S.W.3d 405, 2002 Ky. LEXIS 52 (Ky., 2002)
Subsequent appeal at Bowling v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 143 (Ky., Sept. 18, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Bowling v. Simpson, 2010 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 93 (Ky., Oct. 21, 2010)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Bowling v. Parker, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 113022 (E.D. Ky., Apr. 2, 2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by Bowling v. Haeberlin, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 142582 (E.D. Ky., Sept. 28, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM LAUREL CIRCUIT COURT. HON. LEWIS B. HOPPER, JUDGE. NO. 89-CR-24.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of September 26, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Ky. LEXIS 99.
Bowling v. Commonwealth, 43:10 Ky. L. Summary 19, 1996 Ky. LEXIS 99 (Ky., 1996)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of the decision of the Laurel Circuit Court (Kentucky), which sentenced defendant to death on two counts of murder, and to four, 20-year terms of imprisonment on two counts of first degree robbery and two counts of first degree burglary.


OVERVIEW: Two individuals were shot and killed and appellant prisoner was sentenced for those murders to death. He was also sentenced on two counts of first-degree robbery and first-degree burglary. The court affirmed the decision in favor of appellee commonwealth and held that there was no abuse of discretion by the trial court's denial of appellant's motion for a change of venue. The record demonstrated that if the prospective jurors indicated any inability to adhere to the proper presumptions and burdens they were properly excused. Because appellant specifically denied he owned a handgun, the evidence of another shooting became admissible to rebut those claims. The court stated that the information provided to the jurors regarding the victims was not unduly prejudicial, and appellant received the death penalty because of the calculated, cold-blooded murders, not the extraneous information admitted about the victims. Because appellant's claims of jury irregularity were raised for the first time on appeal, there must have been a showing of actual prejudice, which was no the case here. The prosecutor disclosed all relevant information required. Imposition of the death penalty was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in favor of appellee commonwealth and against appellant prisoner because jurors were properly excused, evidence of another shooting was admissible to rebut appellant's claims that he did not own a handgun, and there was not showing of actual prejudice on the part of appellant in his claim of jury irregularity.

 

33 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Monsanto Co. v. Reed


95-SC-549-DG, 95-SC-561


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


950 S.W.2d 811; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 50; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,982



April 24, 1997, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 2, 1997. Petition for Rehearing Denied October 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. (93-CA-2125, 93-CA-2169, 93-CA-2224 & 93-CA-2337). (PIKE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 85-CI-1724).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant manufacturer challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) that denied its motion for summary judgment in appellee salvagers' common law negligence action for injuries from exposure to polychlorinated biphenyls manufactured by appellant. Appellant alleged that the Product Liability Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.300 et seq., barred appellees' recovery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant manufacturer's motion for summary judgment was denied in appellee salvagers' action for common law negligence for injuries from exposure to polychlorinated biphenyls (PCBs) manufactured by appellant. The court reversed finding that the action was barred because salvage of the transformers and capacitors was not foreseeable where they were not supplied to be used as junk by appellees, but for power transmission by third party power company. The court held that the Product Liability Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. § 411.300 et seq., applied regardless of whether the action was founded on strict liability in tort, negligence or breach of warranty, and that it barred recovery because the products, whether the PCBs or the transformers and capacitors, were altered and modified during the salvage process, which was an intervening cause of injury. The court declined the invitation to create a new tort claim for "spoliation of evidence" finding that evidentiary rules and "missing evidence" instructions were appropriate remedies.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant manufacturer's motion for summary judgment in appellee salvagers' common law negligence action for injuries from exposure to polychlorinated biphenyls was reversed upon a finding that the action was barred because salvage of the transformers and capacitors was not foreseeable, and alteration or modification during the salvage process was an intervening cause of injury.

Transportation Cabinet, Dep't of Highways v. G.L.G., Inc.


95-SC-1052-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


937 S.W.2d 709; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 10



January 30, 1997, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 94-CA-2316. LAUREL CIRCUIT COURT. HON. RODERICK MESSER, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 92-CI-252.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state transportation cabinet and highway department sought review of a decision by the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed a summary judgment entered in favor of appellants in an action enforcing the removal of a billboard erected by appellees, company and associated individuals.


OVERVIEW: The company erected a billboard that was prohibited by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 177.841. Appellants sought to have the billboard removed. The initial trial court found for appellants. However the judgment was overturned in an initial appeal. Upon further appeal, the court affirmed and held that the billboard fell under the exception found under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 177.860(4). The court found that the exception applied to the billboard by its clear and unambiguous language as the term highways was used in the statute's introductory paragraph. The court found that the language of the statute did not require the existence of zoning ordinances before an area could be deemed commercial or industrial. Therefore, the court found that there was a genuine issue of material fact regarding the definition of the area upon which the billboard was placed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of appellees.

Mullins v. Manning Coal Corp.


96-SC-433-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


938 S.W.2d 260; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 1



January 30, 1997, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 26, 1997. Certiorari Denied June 27, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4077.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 95-CA-524-WC. (Workers' Compensation Board No. 92-21726).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed a petition for review of the decision of the Workers' Compensation Board (board) which affirmed the administrative law judge's (ALJ) decision denying the employee retraining incentive benefits under the jurisdictional provision of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 342.316(3) (b). The appellate court (Kentucky) affirmed the board's decision. The employee challenged the appellate court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a heavy equipment operator for another out of state company for 13 years before he took a position with defendant employer. After working for the employer for approximately one year, the employee filed a workers' compensation claim, seeking income or retraining incentive benefits. The ALJ found that the employee had suffered from the disease of coal workers' pneumoconiosis. However, the court found that the employee failed to meet the jurisdictional requirements of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 342.316(3)(b) because the employee was not exposed to the disease in Kentucky. The employee was, therefore, precluded from recovering retraining incentive benefits. On appeal, the employee argued that Ky. Rev. Stat. § 342.316(3)(b) was invalid as violative of the equal protection principles set forth in both the Kentucky and United States Constitutions. He further argued that the statute violated § 14 of the Kentucky Constitution by denying him a "remedy" for his injury. The court held that the employee's constitutional arguments were unfounded. Likewise, the court held that the employee's attack of Ky. Rev. Stat. Am 342.316(3) on equal protection grounds was meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision, which affirmed the board's decision that denied the employee retraining incentive benefits.

St. Ledger v. Revenue Cabinet


94-SC-468-DG, 94-SC-875-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


942 S.W.2d 893; 1997 Ky. LEXIS 17



January 30, 1997, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended January 31, 1997. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 24, 1997, at 1997 Ky. LEXIS 45. Released for Publication May 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REMAND FROM THE UNITED STATES SUPREME COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Supreme Court vacated and remanded for reconsideration a judgment on appeal of a tax challenge filed by plaintiff taxpayers against defendants, including the Commonwealth of Kentucky, Revenue Cabinet, which addressed the constitutionality of Kentucky's Corporate Shares Tax, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.020, the Bank Deposits Tax, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.030, and the Exemption Statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 136.030(1).


OVERVIEW: The United States Supreme Court vacated and remanded for reconsideration the state supreme court's judgment, which held, in part, that the state's Exemption Statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 136.030(1), did not violate the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. On remand, the court reversed, holding that § 136.030(1) did violate the Commerce Clause. The court also held that the Kentucky Corporate Shares Tax, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.020, was not severable from § 136.030(1) because any severance of the two provisions by the court would violate the separation of powers doctrine. Thus, the court held that § 132.020 was also invalid. The court further held that the taxpayers were entitled to a refund under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590(2) of taxes paid under the invalid provisions for two years prior to the filing of a refund application. The court denied the taxpayers' claim for costs and attorney's fees, holding that the reliance of the Commonwealth of Kentucky, Revenue Cabinet on prior caselaw was substantially justified.


OUTCOME: The court reversed its prior judgment. The court declined to address the invalidity of the Bank Deposits Tax. The parties conceded that the Exemption Statute violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. The court held that it could not sever the Corporate Shares Tax from the Exemption Statute; therefore, the Corporate Shares Tax was also invalid.

Reis v. Campbell County Bd. of Educ.


95-SC-656-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


938 S.W.2d 880; 1996 Ky. LEXIS 130



December 19, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 94-CA-353-MR. CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. HON. LEONARD L. KOPOWSKI, JUDGE. (93-CI-927).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee board of education filed a petition for a declaratory judgment challenging the constitutionality of Ken. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 161.790(8) and requesting that it be granted the right to appeal a tribunal's decision on appellant teacher's termination. A Kentucky court of appeals held that the school board had the right to appeal the tribunal's decision. The teacher appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board of education terminated the teacher's employment. A tribunal determined that the teacher's employment should not have been terminated. The board filed a petition challenging the constitutionality of Ken. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 161.790(8), which granted a teacher the right to appeal a tribunal's decision to the circuit court but which was silent concerning the board's right to appeal, and requesting that it be allowed to appeal the tribunal's decision on the teacher's termination. The circuit court dismissed the petition. The court of appeals held that the school board had the right to appeal the tribunal's decision. On appeal, the teacher contended that the court of appeals circumvented the clear language of § 161.790(8). The court held (1) since the tribunal was not an agent of the board, the board was not barred from appealing the tribunal's decision, (2) because the board requested judicial review based on the arbitrariness of the tribunal's decision, the board had to be allowed to seek judicial review in the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals, which held that the school board had the right to appeal the tribunal's decision concerning the employee's termination.
