Eastern Ky. Resources v. Arnett


95-SC-827-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


934 S.W.2d 270; 1996 Ky. LEXIS 118



November 21, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 93-CA-2162. CLARK CIRCUIT COURT NO. 92-CI-252. HON. JAMES S. CHENAULT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant partnership challenged a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which upheld the judgment of the circuit court finding that an agreement entered into between the partnership and the Magoffin County Fiscal Court (fiscal court) for the disposal of solid waste in a privately-owned landfill was a franchise or privilege granted in violation of the advertisement and public bidding requirements of Ky. Const. §164.


OVERVIEW: The fiscal court contracted with the partnership for disposal of solid waste. The partnership was granted the right to operate a landfill in the county and to collect the garbage of the county free of charge; the partnership agreed to pay a royalty to the county for garbage accepted from outside the county. A representative of an environmental group and some of its individual members attacked the contract and contended that it was a franchise that required advertisement and public bidding pursuant to Ky. Const. § 164. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the group. It held that the facts that an exclusivity provision were deleted and that the landfill was operated on private property did not avoid the fact that the partnership had been granted preferential rights and privileges that were not available to the public at large to engage in activities that the partnership could not do without a grant from the government. The appellate court upheld the judgment, and on appeal of that decision the court affirmed. The court held that waste disposal was a government responsibility and that advertisement and public bidding of a contract for the service was constitutionally required.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmance of the trial court holding that solid waste disposal was a public function and that the contract rights for such disposal required a franchise.

Commonwealth v. Halsell


95-SC-846-TG, 95-SC-951-MR, 95-CS-913-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


934 S.W.2d 552; 1996 Ky. LEXIS 119



November 21, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended November 26, 1996. Released for Publication December 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 95-CA-2554-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM E. MCANULTY, JUDGE. 94-CR-3038.

APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM E. MCANULTY, JUDGE. 95-CR-512.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED NO. 95-SC-846-TG, AFFIRMED NO. 95-SC-951-MR, and AFFIRMED NO. 95-SC-913-MR


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged in the district court's juvenile sessions for committing felonies involving the use of a firearm, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 635.020(4)(1994). The Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) dismissed the indictment against defendant one for the district court's failure to conduct a transfer hearing, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 640.010. The state appealed. Defendants two and three pleaded guilty in the circuit court, then appealed.


OVERVIEW: Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 635.020(4)(1994) required that a child over 14 years of age charged with a felony involving the use of a firearm to face trial in the circuit court as an adult. Ky. Const. § 112(5) stated that the circuit courts had original jurisdiction of all claims not vested in another court. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 610.010(1)(a) gave the district courts, unless otherwise exempted, exclusive jurisdiction over minors. Defendants claimed that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 640.010(2)(b) required the district court to examine seven factors before transferring a juvenile felony firearm case to the circuit court. The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 635.020(4) did otherwise exempt minors accused of felony firearm from the district courts' exclusive jurisdiction. Section 635.020(4) did not conflict with Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 640.010(2). Whether it was determined at a preliminary hearing, § 640.010(2), or prior to an adjudicatory hearing, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 635.020(1), once the district court had reasonable cause to believe a juvenile committed a felony firearm offense under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 635.020(4), jurisdiction vested in the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the indictment against defendant one and reinstated the indictment. The court affirmed the judgments against defendants two and three.

Haight v. Commonwealth


94-SC-288-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


938 S.W.2d 243; 1996 Ky. LEXIS 125



November 21, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 3, 1997. Petition for Rehearing Denied March 3, 1997. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4990.
Writ of certiorari denied Haight v. Kentucky, 522 U.S. 837, 118 S. Ct. 110, 139 L. Ed. 2d 63, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4990 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at Haight v. Commonwealth, 2000 Ky. LEXIS 69 (Ky., June 15, 2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at Haight v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 136 (Ky., Aug. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HON. BENJAMIN F. SHOBE, SPECIAL JUDGE. INDICTMENT NO. 85-CR-32.
Haight v. Williamson, 833 S.W.2d 821, 1992 Ky. LEXIS 80 (Ky., 1992)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with various offenses including murder. He was convicted and was sentenced to death by the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky). That conviction was reversed because he was misled into believing that there was a commitment to impose a sentence other than death. The court then denied defendant's writ to enforce the original plea agreement. Defendant appealed on this and other grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed two persons during a robbery. He was convicted after a jury trial and was sentenced to death. Because he had previously raised numerous appeals, the court held that the law of the case doctrine applied and it refused to address issues that were raised in the previous appeals. The court further held that the additional grounds raised on the current appeal were meritless. It was not error nor an abuse of discretion for the trial court to find that defendant was not prejudiced by a juror who had read an article about the case. The trial court's failure to give a specific jury instruction regarding mitigating factors was not error in light of the evidence and counsel's argument. Any error in the instruction regarding the burden of proof of his extreme emotional disturbance defense was harmless. Defendant's history of violent conduct was properly placed before the jury and there was no error in the introduction of past criminal convictions that became final after the commission of the instant offense. Finally, the death sentence was supported by findings of aggravating factors and it was not excessive or disproportionate to the penalty imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the imposition of the death sentence.

93-SC-000828

Subsequent appeal at Foley v. Commonwealth, 2003 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 32 (Ky., Aug. 21, 2003)
Related proceeding at Foley v. Commonwealth, 306 S.W.3d 28, 2010 Ky. LEXIS 53 (Ky., 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at Foley v. Commonwealth, 425 S.W.3d 880, 2014 Ky. LEXIS 103 (Ky., 2014)

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM LAUREL CIRCUIT COURT. THE HON. RODERICK MESSER, JUDGE, DIVISION TWO. INDICTMENT NO. 91-CR-180.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Laurel Circuit Court (Kentucky), which imposed two death sentences after defendant was convicted for two murders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for the murders of two people. The trial court imposed two death sentences, and defendant sought review. The court held that, in order for a change of venue to have been granted there must have been a showing that: (1) there had been prejudicial news coverage; (2) it occurred prior to trial; and (3) the effect of such coverage was reasonably likely to prevent a fair trial. The court held that the trial court had properly excused those jurors that had prejudiced defendant. The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.05592, which required a jury to recommend whether the sentences were to run concurrently or consecutively, was inapplicable to capital cases. The court held that the trial court properly admitted evidence that defendant's family had attempted to suppress a witness' testimony. The court affirmed the judgment and sentence of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of two counts of capital murder. The court held that the trial court had not abused its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a change of venue and that the trial court had properly excused those jurors that had prejudiced defendant. The court held that evidence that defendant's family had attempted to suppress a witness' testimony was admissible.

Brown v. Commonwealth


94-SC-804-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


934 S.W.2d 242; 1996 Ky. LEXIS 97



September 26, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 19, 1996. Petition for Rehearing Denied December 19, 1996. As Modified December 19, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS J. KNOPF, JUDGE. 93-CR-1255.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which found defendant guilty but mentally ill of the murders of his father and brother, and guilty but mentally ill of the first-degree assaults of his mother and sister.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found defendant guilty but mentally ill (GBMI) of the murders of his father and brother, and GBMI of the first-degree assaults of his mother and sister. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that it had not been unreasonable for a juror to find that defendant was not insane at the time of the incident. The court concluded that while the jury instructions might not have contained the precise language sought by defendant, counsel was free to argue the preponderance burden to the jury. The court found that the jury had been instructed that it must return a not guilty by reason of insanity verdict, and not compromise by returning a GBMI verdict. The court found that in looking at the trial as a whole, there was nothing in prosecutor's statement during his closing argument that deserved reversal. The court found that photographs of the victims were relevant and probative evidence of the circumstances of the crime. The court held that defendant's right to a speedy trial had not been violated. The court cautioned that the decision did not put to rest the issues of the constitutionality of the GBMI statute and the instructions to be given to the jury in a GBMI case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court finding defendant guilty but mentally ill (GBMI) of the murders of his father and brother, and GBMI of the first-degree assaults of his mother and sister, and the court cautioned, however, that the decision did not put to rest the issues of the constitutionality of the GBMI statute and the content of the jury instructions given in a GBMI case.

Lewis by Lewis v. West Am. Ins. Co.


95-SC-751-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


927 S.W.2d 829; 1996 Ky. LEXIS 86



August 29, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 19, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 94-CA-1158. CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. HON. LEONARD L. KOPOWSKI, JUDGE. NO. 93-CI-1019.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured minor challenged the order of the Kentucky Court of Appeals, which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee insurer, upholding the validity of the family exclusion clause.


OVERVIEW: The child was a passenger in a vehicle owned and operated by her mother that was involved in a collision. The mother was killed. The child suffered serious and permanent injuries including brain damage. The insurer's policy included a family exclusion specifically limiting liability coverage available for bodily injury to the named insured or any family member of the named insured to the minimum liability insurance coverage statutorily required. Thus, the policy limited coverage to the $ 25,000 statutory minimum where the injured person was the named insured or a member of a named insured's family, regardless of who was driving. The court reversed, finding that household exclusions were invalid as against public policy. The court found that the possibility of collusion by a few was not a valid reason to deny benefits to an entire class of innocent victims, preventing them from receiving adequate financial protection. The court found that this exclusion was particularly disturbing because this class of victims was the one most frequently exposed to the potential negligence of the named insured, as typical family relations required family members to ride together.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, holding that family exclusions to liability insurance policies were invalid and unenforceable. The summary judgment entered against the injured child was set aside and the matter remanded.

Flying J Travel Plaza v. Transportation Cabinet, Dep't of Highways


95-SC-388-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


928 S.W.2d 344; 1996 Ky. LEXIS 41



April 25, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied August 29, 1996, Opinion Modified August 29, 1996, Released for Publication August 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 93-CA-1133-MR. BOONE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 90-CI-674. HON. JOSEPH BAMBERGER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant plaza corporation challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed a judgment of injunction by the trial court, holding that the content of the information presented on the travel plaza's on-premises sign violated Kentucky law. Appellee Commonwealth of Kentucky, Transportation Cabinet, Department of Highways (Cabinet) argued to uphold the injunction ordering a modification of the message or removal of the sign.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that the only question was the content of the message on the sign. The court examined whether the statutes and regulations imposed an unconstitutional restriction on both commercial and noncommercial free speech. The court also examined whether the Cabinet had failed to demonstrate that less restrictive measures were not available to accomplish a legitimate interest. The court concluded that the Cabinet failed to demonstrate a reasonable connection between the means provided by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 177.863(4)(a) and 603 Ky. Admin. Regs. 3:010, § 3(1)(h) and the ends of highway safety and aesthetics. Consequently, the court found that the statute and regulation were not narrowly tailored to achieve the desired objectives of the law and regulation. Therefore, the court held that the statute and the regulation were unconstitutional restrictions on the commercial free speech of the travel plaza. The court additionally held that the restrictions in question were also unconstitutional as an impermissible limitation on content-based noncommercial speech.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that the travel plaza's sign violated state law, and the court dissolved the injunction issued by the trial court.

Department of Educ. v. Risner


95-SC-458-T


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


913 S.W.2d 327; 1996 Ky. LEXIS 2



January 18, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 8, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 95-CA-1316. FLOYD CIRCUIT COURT. HON. JOHN D. CAUDILL, JUDGE. (95-CI-055).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Kentucky Department of Education sought review of an order of the Floyd Circuit Court (Kentucky), which issued a temporary injunction to enjoin the removal of appellee parent members of the school based council from their respective councils pending the outcome of the petition challenging the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 160.345(2)(a) brought by the parent members and appellee Floyd County Board of Education.


OVERVIEW: Appellees brought an action challenging the constitutionality of § 160.345(2)(a). The trial court issued a temporary injunction to enjoin the removal of the parent members from their respective councils pending the outcome of the constitutional challenge and subsequently found § 160.345(2)(a) unconstitutional as a violation of the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV after applying strict scrutiny. Upon appeal by the Kentucky Department of Education the court reversed the order finding no such violation. The court held that the constitutionality of the statute should have been analyzed using the rational basis test as parents were not a suspect class not was sitting on a school based council (SBC), a constitutionally protected fundamental right. The court held that the restriction in § 160.345(2)(a) directly addressed the appearance of nepotism within the SBC and was thus clearly rationally related to the legitimate goal of the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which found that the statute expressly prohibiting school district employees or their spouses from serving as a parent member on a school based council was unconstitutional.

Fryrear v. Parker


94-SC-539-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


920 S.W.2d 519; 1996 Ky. LEXIS 1



January 18, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Sloan v. Kentucky, 14 Fed. Appx. 366, 2001 U.S. App. LEXIS 14063 (6th Cir. Ky., 2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at Fryrear v. Commonwealth, 2014 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 707 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 5, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 94-CA-66. LYON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 93-CI-48.
Fryrear v. Commonwealth, 507 S.W.2d 144, 1974 Ky. LEXIS 664 (Ky., 1974)
McDonald v. Commonwealth, 569 S.W.2d 134, 1978 Ky. LEXIS 379 (Ky., 1978)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who had been convicted of rape and sentenced to life without parole, appealed the order of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed a trial court decision that had granted their petition for writ of habeas corpus under Ky. Rev. Stat. § 419.020 and had ordered that defendants' sentences be commuted to life. Defendants contended that their continued incarceration without the right to apply for parole was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Following the convictions of the seven defendants, an amendment to the state penal code eliminated the phrase "without parole" from the applicable life sentence for rape. Defendants contended that the appellate court erred in holding that a writ of habeas corpus was not the correct procedure for defendants to apply for the right of parole. On appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court's order. The court held that the writ of habeas corpus was not the correct procedure for defendants to seek relief because they were not being unlawfully detained. The court found that the balancing of interests, including the rights of victims to be present at defendants' requested hearing, favored returning the matter to the county where the cause originated. The court stated that the correct procedure was for defendants to seek relief from judgment under Ky. R. Crim. P. 60.02. The court noted that Ky. R. Crim. P. 60.02(e) and (f) permitted relief from judgment based on equitable or extraordinary grounds. An application for relief under Ky. R. Crim. P. 60.02 should have been deemed timely if it was made expeditiously after the opinion of the court was made final.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's order reversing the decision that had granted defendants' petition for writ of habeas corpus and had ordered that defendants' sentences be commuted to life.

 

47 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Associated Indus. v. Commonwealth


95-SC-53-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


912 S.W.2d 947; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 147



December 21, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 11, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. NO. 93-CI-2006. (Transfer From Court of Appeals No. 95-CA-119).

ON TRANSFER FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 95-CA-119. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HON. WILLIAM GRAHAM, JUDGE. (93-CI-2006).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant legislative corporation sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which declared that the legislative and executive codes challenged by appellant were constitutional. Appellant initiated declaratory judgment action against appellees, state, attorney general, and associated individual, and contended that the provisions were vague or overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Appellant legislative corporation initiated declaratory judgment against appellees, state, attorney general, and associated individuals, and contended that various legislative and executive codes were unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The trial court declared that the provisions were constitutional, and appellant sought review. The court held that the trial court correctly declined to address appellant's issue that asserted that the fines and criminal penalties, which could have been imposed under the provisions, violated U.S. Const. amend. I rights of association and petition because appellant failed to assert an actual and justiciable controversy pending before the trial court. The court determined that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 6.811(9) and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 11A.236(1) were neither overly broad nor violative of appellant's freedom of association under Ky. Const. § 1 or U.S. Const. amend. I. The court held that under the strict scrutiny test, although legislative rights burdened the exercise of fundamental rights, such rights may yield where there was a subordinately compelling governmental interest. The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which declared that legislative and executive provisions challenged by appellant legislative corporation against appellees, state, attorney general, and associated individuals, were constitutional. The court held that the provisions were not violative of U.S. Const. amend. I and Ky. Const. § 1 because the rights of association and petition could have yielded to a compelling governmental interest.

 

48 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Transportation Cabinet v. Cassity


94-SC-894-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


912 S.W.2d 48; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 149



December 21, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 11, 1996. As Corrected March 26, 1996. Certiorari Denied May 20, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 3285.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 93-CA-001130. PIKE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE BAYARD V. COLLIER, JUDGE. (88-CI-667).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Transportation Cabinet of the Commonwealth of Kentucky (cabinet) challenged a decision from the Court of Appeals of Kentucky, which determined that the cabinet's procedure for enforcing Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 138.990 was unconstitutional. An enforcement officer had issued citations for statutory violations to appellee litigant and immediately impounded his tractor and trailer. The litigant filed an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The litigant filed his § 1983 action to recover damages suffered as a result of the loss of his equipment. The litigant was cited for not having a Kentucky motor fuel user's license (KYU), which subjected the vehicle to mandatory impoundment pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 138.990(15). The officer had to receive authority from a superior officer before impounding the vehicle. The issue before the court was whether the transportation department's procedure for enforcement of § 138.990 resulted in a deprivation of procedural due process and was therefore unconstitutional. The cabinet asserted there was no due process violation because the litigant had an opportunity for a hearing concerning his KYU revocation. The court reversed, holding that: (1) the motor carrier usage tax was collected through the issuance of a KYU; (2) the litigant had an opportunity for a hearing to challenge the revocation of his license for nonpayment of usage taxes; (3) although the litigant's interest in his vehicle was significant, it was counter balanced with the state's compelling interest in collecting tax revenues; and (4) the litigant's federal and state due process protections were satisfied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's determination that the cabinet's procedure impoundment of motor vehicles for lack of a KYU was unconstitutional. The court remanded for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

49 of 908 DOCUMENTS


State Bd. of Elections v. Fischer


95-SC-849-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


910 S.W.2d 245; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 135



November 22, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 95-CA-2534. (CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT NO. 91-CI-1400).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state board of election (board) and secretary of state, challenged an order of the Campbell Circuit Court (Kentucky), whereby it denied their motion to amend its permanent injunction. Said injunction prohibited the conduct of any election pursuant to the district boundaries set forth in Chapter 5 of the Kentucky Revised Statutes after January 3, 1995.


OVERVIEW: The trial court, interpreting the court's past ruling, issued a permanent injunction prohibiting the conduct of any election pursuant to the district boundaries set forth in Chapter 5 of the Kentucky Revised Statutes after January 3, 1995. The particular controversy arose upon the August 3, 1995 resignation of a state representative. By virtue of the trial court's injunction, the board was prohibited from conducting special elections to fill that or any other vacancy in the state legislature. The board sought amendment of the permanent injunction to permit a special election to fill the representative's vacancy. The trial court declined to modify its injunction. The court affirmed. The court's past ruling declared the 1991 Legislative Reapportionment Act unconstitutional. Upon the court's determination that such was unconstitutional, there was no legal theory whereby it or any portion of it could be used to establish a district for the purpose of filling a vacancy. It was the responsibility of the state legislature to remedy the problems associated with the voided districts, including the potential for death or resignation, not the court's responsibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision not to amend its permanent injunction prohibiting the conduct of any election pursuant to the district boundaries set forth in Chapter 5 of the Kentucky Revised Statutes after January 3, 1995.

 

50 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. Oberle-Jordre Co.


95-SC-136-WC, 95-SC-174-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


910 S.W.2d 241; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 141



November 22, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NOS. 94-CA-84-WC, 93-CA-2964-WC, 94-CA-42-WC & 94-CA-211-WC (Workers' Compensation Board Nos. 90-40415 & 90-35304). APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NOS. 94-CA-211-WC, 93-CA-2964-WC, 94-CA-42-WC, & 94-CA-84-WC (Workers' Compensation Board Nos. 90-35304 & 90-40415).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widows challenged decisions from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed the decision of the Workers' Compensation Board. The widows' claims for benefits due to their husbands' deaths from asbestos-related diseases were denied, and their cases were dismissed. The widows questioned the constitutionality of the five-year statute of repose. Cross-appellants, employer and Special Fund, also challenged the decisions.


OVERVIEW: The widows argued that they were not seeking a continuation of benefits but were proceeding under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.750, which they claimed allowed for an independent cause of action for their husbands' deaths not subject to the limitations period. The Workers' Compensation Board concluded that the widows' claims were not derivative of their deceased husbands' causes of action and that they had an independent cause of action, concluding that a cause under § 342.750 did not accrue until the worker's death and was not otherwise affected by any limitations period which would have applied had the worker filed a claim during his lifetime. On review, the court disagreed, asserting that the widows did not effectively counter the fact that there was no constitutional impediment to the repose provision. The court found that there was no concomitant right to seek workers' compensation benefits, and that the widows' claims were not merely barred by the three-year statute of limitations in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.316(3), but they were extinguished by the five-year statute of repose; it was not simply a matter of competing limitations periods. The appellate decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision. There was no constitutional impediment to repose provisions in the workers' compensation scheme. The employer and Special Fund were entitled to rely on rights contained in the state repose provision freeing them from any liability for compensation after the passage of five years from the employee's exposure.

Jones v. Board of Trustees


94-SC-487-TG; 94-SC-493-TG; and 94-SC-840-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


910 S.W.2d 710; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 131; 19 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2196



November 22, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. NO. 93-CI-00597. Hon. William L. Graham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Board of Trustees for the Kentucky Employee Retirement System (retirement system) brought an action, seeking declaratory relief against appellants, governor and general assembly, concerning actions taken to control the state's contribution to the retirement system. The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted summary judgment in favor of the retirement system. The governor and the general assembly sought review.


OVERVIEW: The retirement system sought to increase the state's contribution to the system by including it in its budget request. Valuing the system's assets to reflect market value, as opposed to book value, the governor declined to follow the retirement system's recommendations and acted through the general assembly to maintain the state's contribution rates of the previous year. The retirement system filed an action for declaratory relief in the trial court arguing that the governor and the general assembly usurped the retirement system's authority by enacting legislation that differed from its recommendations. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the retirement system. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the governor and the general assembly were not immune in this type of action; and (2) the action of the governor and the general assembly in maintaining the previous rate of the state contribution did not violate the laws and did not impair the pension rights of state employees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the state retirement system and remanded the cause for entry of judgment in favor of the governor and the general assembly.

Hoy v. Kentucky Indus. Revitalization Auth.


94-SC-949-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


907 S.W.2d 766; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 125



October 19, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 94-CA-2700-MR. (Franklin Circuit Court No. 93-CI-1201).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the judgment of the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellees, Kentucky Industrial Revitalization Authority (KIRA) and electric company, in the attorney's action to obtain information through the Open Records Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 61.870 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The electric company filed an application with KIRA pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 154.26-010 for investment tax credits to support the renovation of its laundry machine manufacturing facility. Pursuant to § 154.26-080(5), an analysis of the company's operations was undertaken by an accounting firm and a confidential report was supplied to KIRA. The attorney, representing the electric company's competitor, made a request for the electric company's completed application and the full report prepared by the accounting firm. KIRA denied the attorney's request. After exhausting the administrative remedies, the parties appeared before the trial court for a decision on the attorney's application. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying the attorney any relief. The attorney was prohibited from receiving the application and accounting report under the Open Records Act because the information was exempted from disclosure under the Act. The court found that it did not take a degree in finance to recognize that the information concerning the inner workings of the company were generally recognized as confidential and proprietary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the attorney the relief he sought under the Open Records Act.

 

53 of 908 DOCUMENTS


St. Ledger v. Commonwealth


94-SC-468-DG, 94-SC-875-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


912 S.W.2d 34; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 128



October 19, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 92-CA-2688-MR & 92-CA-2689-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT (90-CI-6075).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART AND AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers filed an action against appellees, commonwealth, revenue cabinet and secretary, contending that the ad valorem taxes and exemptions under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.030 were unconstitutional. The trial court held that the exemption statute in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.030(1) was unenforceable. The Circuit Court of Appeals (Kentucky) reversed and held the statute was enforceable and valid. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: Kentucky had an ad valorem tax statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.020. Under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.030(1) certain in-state bank deposits were taxed at a rate lower than out-of-state deposits. Under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 136.030(1)(a), an exemption statute, shareholders who held stock in corporations that paid taxes to the commonwealth on at least 75 percent of its total property irrespective of location, did not pay taxes on their shares. Two taxpayers brought suit alleging constitutional violations. The trial court entered judgement for them, but the appellate court reversed. It held that the statutes passed constitutional muster. On appeal, the court held that the lowered ad valorem tax for in-state bank deposits violated the commerce clause. The tax interfered with interstate commerce and directly affected the decision-making of a depositor. It held that the exemption statute for the tax on corporate shares was facially discriminatory and violated the commerce clause. But it was proven to advance a legitimate local purpose, the elimination of double taxation, that could not be adequately served by reasonable nondiscriminatory alternatives and was upheld as valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgement that the bank tax did not violate the commerce clause. It affirmed the appellate court's judgement that the exemption statute did not violate the commerce clause. It held that the overall ad valorem statutory scheme was constitutionally valid.

 

54 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Edmonds v. Commonwealth


94-SC-376-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


906 S.W.2d 343; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 113



September 21, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 12, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. CRIMINAL ACTION NO. 93-CR-816-6. HON. JAMES E. KELLER, JUDGE.
Brooks v. Commonwealth, 905 S.W.2d 861, 42:10 Ky. L. Summary 22, 1995 Ky. LEXIS 104 (Ky., 1995)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Fayette County Circuit Court (Kentucky) for first-degree trafficking in a controlled substance and criminal syndicate, challenging an informant's in-court identification, admission of a videotape, and denial of a directed verdict, and alleging insufficiency of the evidence, double jeopardy, and improper jury instruction. Defendant also alleged a statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that in-court identification of defendant by an informant was proper. The court held that as there was no objection at trial to a videotape being shown to the jury, any alleged error was not properly preserved for appellate review under Ky. R. Crim. P. 9.22. The court held that the probative value of the videotape outweighed any prejudicial effect. The court found that it was not reversible error for the trial judge to have refused to grant a directed verdict of acquittal, as the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant established, maintained, or facilitated drug trafficking activities in which a crime group engaged on a continuing basis. The trial judge correctly overruled a motion objecting to the jury being instructed on both trafficking in a controlled substance and criminal syndicate as a violation of double jeopardy principles, as the count of cocaine trafficking was not a "lesser-included offense" of the crime of criminal syndicate. The court found that the fact that defendant was possibly not as involved with the crime group as other members did not render Ky. Rev. Stat. § 506.120 unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction for first-degree trafficking in a controlled substance and criminal syndicate, and affirmed the judgment that defendant was a first-degree persistent felony offender.

Dishman v. Commonwealth


94-SC-392-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


906 S.W.2d 335; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 114



September 21, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 12, 1995.
Decision reached on appeal by Smith v. Commonwealth, 905 S.W.2d 865, 42:10 Ky. L. Summary 42, 1995 Ky. LEXIS 115 (Ky., 1995)
Subsequent appeal at Dishman v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 600 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. CRIMINAL ACTION NO. 93-CR-816-5. HON. JAMES E. KELLER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment based on a jury verdict in the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky). The defendant was convicted of trafficking in a controlled substance in the first degree, for which she was sentenced to 10 years in prison, and of criminal syndicate, for which she was sentenced to 20 years, both sentences were to be served consecutively for a total of 30 years.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was among 11 other persons that were indicted on various charges including trafficking in controlled substances, criminal syndicate, welfare fraud, failure to file state income tax, and persistent felony offender charges. The defendant and four others were tried at the same time. The court affirmed and held that: (1) the trial court properly exercised its discretion in denying the defendant's motions for continuance and for directed verdict of acquittal; (2) pursuant to Ky. R. Crim. P. 6.20, there was no prejudice regarding the failure to separate her trial from the trial of her co-defendants; (3) there was no double jeopardy violation because the crime of trafficking in a controlled substance and the crime of criminal syndicate each required proof of facts that the other did not, and were not a factually single offense or part of a single criminal episode; (4) whether Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 506.120 was unconstitutionally vague when compared to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1402 was not properly preserved for appellate review as required by Ky. R. Crim. P. 9.22; and (5) the jury instructions were correct and sufficient evidence was presented to support the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction against the defendant for the crimes of criminal syndicate and trafficking in a controlled substance in the first degree.

Foster v. Overstreet


93-SC-385-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


905 S.W.2d 504; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 98



August 24, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ORIGINAL ACTZON IN COURT OF APPEALS. 93-CA-1231-OA (Fayette Circuit Court No 86-CR-332).



DISPOSITION: Denied


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner's request for a writ of mandamus was transferred from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky). Petitioner complained of respondent trial judge's refusal to recuse herself from the retrial of the sentencing phase of petitioner's capital murder case.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge denied petitioner's motion to recuse alleging that her impartiality could reasonably be questioned. Petitioner requested a writ of mandamus in the appellate court and requested the petition be transferred to the court. The court denied the petition. The court noted that mandamus was an extreme remedy which was only available when it was the only appropriate remedy available. The court found that petitioner could file a motion under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26A.020(1) to request that the Chief Justice determine whether to designate a special judge or she could appeal from an adverse sentencing decision. The court held that a decision by one justice under § 26A.020(1) did not deny petitioner's constitutional right of appeal to the entire Supreme Court. The court did find § 26A.020(1) to be an unconstitutional encroachment by the legislature on the power of the judiciary to make rules but extended it comity. The court held that the procedure afforded by § 26A.020(1) was adequate.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for a writ of mandamus.

Kentucky Cent. Life Ins. Co. v. Stephens


94-SC-742-TG, 94-SC-743-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


897 S.W.2d 583; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 60



May 11, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 94-CA-2074. (Franklin Circuit Court No. 93-CI-196).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company sought review of the order of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which upheld a ruling in appellee insurance commissioner's favor that approved the sale of the insurer's assets and ordered its liquidation. The insurer sought reversal, arguing that the order did not comply with state rehabilitation and liquidation laws and was in contravention of the insurer's constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: After an insurer became insolvent, the insurance commissioner sought a reorganization or reinsurance plan. After he failed to procure an infusion of cash, the commissioner obtained an order of sale and liquidation. The insurer sought reversal of the order, arguing that no genuine effort was made to rehabilitate its company. The court found that this argument lacked strength in view of the commissioner's efforts to procure infusions of cash and his consideration of alternative plans of self-rehabilitation. The court found that the trial court based its order on substantial evidence, and further attempts to rehabilitate the insurer would substantially increase the risk of loss to policyholders and creditors, and would be futile. The insurer argued that the trial court approved an arbitrary taking of its property without permitting it meaningful opportunity to defend itself and without permitting just compensation, as was constitutionally mandated. The court held that no violation of the insurer's substantive or procedural due process rights occurred because the commissioner was within the scope of power afforded to him by the insurance laws when he sought the order of liquidation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order directing the sale and liquidation of the insurance company. The court held that the insurance commissioner was within his statutory rights when he sought liquidation because the interest of the public required the order of liquidation, and the means were reasonably necessary and not unduly oppressive upon the insurer.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant shareholders filed suit against appellee, insurance commissioner, challenging the insurance commissioner's liquidation of an insurance company. OVERVIEW: The insurance commissioner placed an insurance company into rehabilitation/liquidation proceedings. The record demonstrated that the insurance company was insolvent. Vaughn v. Knopf


94-SC-150-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


895 S.W.2d 566; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 49



March 23, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 92-CA-236. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. (HONORABLE WILLIAM S. COOPER). (91-CI-4915).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sheriff sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) that affirmed the decision of the trial court that held Ky. Rev. Stat. § 64.345(2) and (5) was unconstitutional in that it violated Ky. Const. §§ 27, 28 regarding the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: The county sheriff filed an action in the trial court seeking a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. 64.345(2) and (5), which directed the chief circuit judge of counties containing cities of the first class and urban county governments to approve certain budget elements of the sheriff department. The trial court held that § 64.345(2) and (5) was unconstitutional because it was a delegation of discretionary authority that constituted an unreasonable interference with the function of the judicial department. The appeals court agreed with the trial court result but held that the delegation was improper since it contained "inadequate standards" by which the judge should make the decision. On appeal, the court affirmed both the trial and appeals court decisions. The court held that § 64.345(2) and (5) violated Ky. Const. §§ 27, 28 because it mandated that a judicial officer perform what was clearly a function of the executive branch of government. The court rejected the sheriff's argument that the court had routinely held that delegations from one branch to another branch were generally acceptable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appeals court and trial court that held that the statute directing a judge to approve county sheriff budgets was unconstitutional as a violation of the separation of powers doctrine.

 

60 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Stephens v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


93-SC-919-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


894 S.W.2d 624; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 7



January 19, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 20, 1995. Rehearing Denied April 20, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 92-CA-2000. (Franklin Circuit Court No. 89-CI-1426).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Kentucky state insurance agencies and official, requested review of a decision of the Kentucky Court of Appeals regarding the constitutionality of amendments to the Kentucky Fair Access to Insurance Requirements (FAIR) Plan Statutes, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 304.35-010 et seq., in an action brought by appellee insurer.


OVERVIEW: The insurer challenged the constitutionality of amendments to the Kentucky FAIR plan that mandated statutorily that insurers authorized to write property or casualty insurance on a direct basis be a member of the FAIR plan. Before the amendment, only insurers authorized to write property insurance, homeowner and farm owner policies were required to be members, as the Plan pertained only to property insurance coverage. The court found that the plan did not violate either federal or state equal protection standards. This was a highly economic regulation that did not rise to the same level of scrutiny involved in freedoms guaranteed by the Bill of Rights. There was no demonstration by the insurer that the plan constituted a hostile and oppressive scheme against it or any particular class. The insurer had the possibility of adjusting its premium rates charged to regular customers to recoup some or all of the assessment that the plan might require them to pay. The court reversed, holding that the plan was constitutional and did not impose such a classification as to include persons within the class who were not rationally related to the goal of the legislation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, finding that appellants' FAIR Plan, as amended, was constitutional and did not impose on the insurer such a classification as to include persons within the class who were not rationally related to the goal of the legislation. This issue of prejudgment interest was remanded to the trial court for a determination.

 

61 of 908 DOCUMENTS


O'Bryan v. Hedgespeth


93-SC-963-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


892 S.W.2d 571; 1995 Ky. LEXIS 10



January 19, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 92-CA-734. DAVIESS CIRCUIT COURT. HON. JOSEPH H. McKINLEY, JUDGE. NO. 90-CI-641.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured filed a personal injury action against appellee driver. The injured filed a pretrial motion in limine to exclude evidence of collateral source payments, alleging that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.188 was unconstitutional. The trial court denied the injured's motion and the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) affirmed. The injured appealed.


OVERVIEW: The injured alleged that § 411.188, which stated that collateral source payments to a plaintiff who sought to recover damages in contract or tort were admissible evidence, was unconstitutional because it violated the "subject/title" clause of the Kentucky Constitution and it violated the separation of powers clauses of the Kentucky Constitution found in Ky. Const. §§ 27, 28 and 116. The court found that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.188 did not violate the "subject/title" clause of the Kentucky Constitution. The court found that § 411.188 did violate the separation of powers clauses because the judiciary was responsible for deciding when evidence was relevant to an issue of fact, not the legislature. The court further determined that the statute was not entitled to judicial comity. It was not unconstitutionally adopted, but it unconstitutional in operation. Section 411.188 encouraged the jury to disregard the injured's evidence as to the medical bills incurred and to temper the verdict with the irrelevant consideration of what payments he received from other sources. The court also determined that § 411.188 was an unconstitutional limitation on damages in violation of Ky. Const. § 54.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court was reversed. The judgment of the trial court was vacated, and the case is remanded for a new trial on damages in conformity. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.188 was unconstitutional and Edwards v. Land, 851 S.W.2d 484 (1992) was overruled.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to challenge the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189.270, appellant state requested review of the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirming that the authorized fee was not a tax.


OVERVIEW: The trucking company contended that the amount that authorized for a weight-axle-over-dimensional vehicles upon motor carriers was a fee and the amount charged was excessive. In the alternative the trucking company contended that the permit amount was an unconstitutional tax. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the permit amount was a fee because it was an amount for exercising the privilege of operating an overweight or an over-dimensional vehicle on Kentucky's highways. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding that the statute authorizing a permit fee for weight-axle-over-dimensional vehicles was constitutional and that the fee was reasonable.

 

63 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Botkin v. Commonwealth


92-SC-657-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


890 S.W.2d 292; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 141



December 22, 1994, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 12, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 92-CA-1116. FLEMING CIRCUIT COURT. HON. RICHARD LEWIS HINTON, JUDGE. NO. 91-XX-003.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of September 1, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Ky. LEXIS 93.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the judgment of the Fleming District Court (Kentucky), which convicted them of violating Ky. Rev. Stat. § 189A.010(1)(a) by operating a motor vehicle when their blood alcohol content was 0.10 or more. Upon appeal to the Fleming Circuit Court, their judgments were affirmed. The Kentucky Court of Appeals denied discretionary review and defendants sought further discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: Ky. Rev. Stat. § 189.010(1)(a) was the new per se subsection added to the driving under the influence statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. § 189A.010(1). Defendants received enhanced sentences upon a finding of two prior alcohol related motor vehicle convictions. The issue was whether defendants could have been assessed a greater punishment than that provided for a first time offender because of previous offenses that were related in nature, but different in character. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court determined that defendants did not receive a greater punishment than the law annexed to the crime when they committed it. The court explained that defendants were punished as the law provided at the time when their present offenses were committed, but because of their status as prior offenders, the crime they presently committed was subject to a greater penalty than it would have been otherwise. The court concluded that the ex post facto clauses were not implicated because defendants were not being punished for crimes committed prior to the effective date of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions of driving while under the influence.

Kuprion v. Fitzgerald


94-SC-334-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


888 S.W.2d 679; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 135



November 23, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended November 28, 1994. Released for Publication December 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS NO. 93-CA-2760-OA. JEFFERSON FAMILY COURT 93-FD-1244.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant spouse sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) that denied a writ of mandamus challenging the constitutionality of the family court. Appellant sought to have the family court declared unconstitutional and requested that her case be transferred to a division of the regular circuit court.


OVERVIEW: Appellant spouse filed a petition for the dissolution of marriage with the circuit court and the matter was assigned to the family court to be heard by a specially appointed judge. Appellant contended that the family court was unconstitutional and the circuit court denied her request to have her case reassigned to a regular division of the circuit court. The appellate court denied appellant's writ of mandamus and the court affirmed the decision. The court held that the creation of the family court project was not unconstitutional. The chief justice of the supreme court did not create a new court, as proscribed by the Kentucky Constitution. The chief justice had authority to assign qualified judges to the family court project on a temporary basis, and his order that the judge shall serve until further order of the court did not exceed that authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court that denied appellant spouse's writ of mandamus challenging the constitutionality of the family court. The court held that the creation of the family court as part of the circuit court and the chief justice's appointment of judges to it was not unconstitutional.

 

65 of 908 DOCUMENTS


George v. Commonwealth


93-SC-550-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


885 S.W.2d 938; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 116



October 27, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LEWIS G. PAISLEY, JUDGE. 93-CR-91



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) for first-degree rape. The trial court permitted defendant's 11-year-old daughter, a nonvictim witness, to testify outside of defendant's presence by closed circuit television under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 421.350 and denied defendant's motion for mistrial after one juror who realized she was related to the victim was dismissed and another was allowed to remain on the jury.


OVERVIEW: The child witness's therapist testified that her main concern was how the family would relate after the child witness testified and that the child witness expressed anxiety, but was not fearful, and could testify in defendant's presence. The court held that the trial court committed reversible error and abused its discretion by allowing the child witness to testify via closed circuit television because Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 421.350(3) only applied to child victims. The court held that the statutory language was plain and that exceptions that were not made could not be read as such. In addition, even if § 421.350(3) applied to witnesses, the state made an inadequate showing of necessity, and the trial court did not find a "compelling need." The court held that the trial court did not commit reversible error by allowing a juror who was related to the victim to remain on the jury where the juror did not know he was the victim's third cousin until she mentioned her mother's name during her testimony, there was no evidence of a close relationship or a relationship certain that created a presumption of prejudice, and the defendant did not object at the time of disclosure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for first-degree rape and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

66 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Pillersdorf v. Department of Pub. Advocacy


92-SC-449-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


890 S.W.2d 616; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 125



October 27, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 16, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 90-CA-1302-MR. KNOTT CIRCUIT COURT NO. 87-CR-17



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorneys were appointed by a trial court, which then directed appellee, Department for Public Advocacy (DPA), to compensate the attorneys at the statutory hourly rates with no limitation on the legal fees and expenses. The trial court ordered payment to the attorneys. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) reversed and held that the trial court failed to make findings of fact sufficient to sustain the order. The attorneys appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court held that the trial court simply did not have the prerogative to intrude as it did into the appointment or assignment process of the DPA. There was at least a legitimate dispute as to whether "good cause" to substitute counsel existed, as Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 31.130 required. The court affirmed. The trial court failed to find good cause to appoint substitute counsel, the condition precedent to the vesting of DPA's statutory authority under § 31.130 to comply with its order. It then penalized DPA for not complying, and appointed the attorneys in contravention of the statute. The amount of compensation for attorneys who provide services under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 31.065(2) is predetermined because DPA staff attorneys are on salary. If the unusual circumstance arose whereby a trial judge was forced to look outside the statute to appoint counsel, the maximum terms of state compensation and the procedure by which it was procured were also dictated by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 31.070. DPA would still review compensation claims submitted by judge-appointed counsel and approve or deny them. The decision of the DPA in all matters of fee and expense compensation were final.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order and remanded to the DPA for a determination of reasonable state compensation to the attorneys in accordance with DPA guidelines and the statutes.

Wilson v. Kentucky Transp. Cabinet


93-SC-360-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


884 S.W.2d 641; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 108



September 29, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 93-CA-1202. (Franklin Circuit Court No. 90-CI-1557)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged an order from the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which dismissed a declaratory judgment action against appellees, state transportation cabinet and the state turnpike authority. The declaratory action was brought to determine the constitutional validity of revenue bonds enacted by the state general assembly.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought the declaratory action for the court to determine the constitutional validity of revenue bonds enacted by the state general assembly for the improvement of roads. The lower court dismissed the action. The court affirmed its dismissal. The court determined that the bonds were constitutional and did not represent a debt of the state because neither the full faith and credit nor the taxing authority of the state was pledged to the payment of the principal or interest of the bonds. Further, neither the state nor the authority was obligated to pay the bond issue or the serial lease or from other revenues of the system. Further, the court stated that serial leases automatically renewable, unless cancelled, did not create a long-term obligation and therefore were not legal debts within the meaning of the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, which dismissed a declaratory judgment action against the state transportation cabinet and the state turnpike authority.

Commonwealth v. Lavit


92-SC-450-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


882 S.W.2d 678; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 82



September 1, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 89-CA-2360. WASHINGTON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 87-CR-010



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed the trial court's award of attorney fees granted pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. § 31.170(4) and which held that the attorneys were entitled to the full amount that they requested, which was above the statute's limit, because the defense of any capital murder case was "ipso facto" a "special circumstance" within the meaning of § 31.170(4).


OVERVIEW: The attorneys were retained as defense counsel in a capital murder case. The trial court approved their request that they be appointed as public defenders so that the attorneys could be more fully compensated. After successfully defending the suspect, the attorneys submitted their fee, which the trial court approved although it surpassed the statutory maximum. The state public defender's association (association), however, refused payment. Thereafter, the trial court ordered the association to pay each attorney the maximum allowed under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 31.170(4). The court affirmed the appellate court's reversal and award of attorney fees that surpassed the statutory maximum because the services rendered by the attorneys clearly required a finding that special circumstances existed to warrant a higher total attorney fee as a matter of law. The trial court's judgement in failing to award more than the statutory cap was inconsistent with its finding that the attorneys' legal services and expenses were necessary, fair, and reasonable. Furthermore, it rendered the "special circumstances" exception meaningless and deprived the attorneys of their property without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision, which awarded the attorneys the full amount of attorney fees that they requested although such fees surpassed the statutory maximum.

Fiscal Court v. Brady


93-SC-723-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


885 S.W.2d 681; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 88



September 1, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 23, 1994. Released for Publication November 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 93-CA-2013. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HON. GEOFFREY P. MORRIS, JUDGE. NO. 92-CI-6724



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Fiscal Court of Jefferson County, Kentucky, sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which rendered judgment in favor of appellee taxpayers in the taxpayers' action challenging the legality of grants made from county tax revenues by direct payment to certain privately-owned schools.


OVERVIEW: A group of taxpayers filed suit against the Fiscal Court of Jefferson County, Kentucky to challenge grants being made from county tax revenues by direct payment to specified privately-owned schools, designated as school transportation subsidies. The taxpayers alleged that the payments exceeded the statutory authority of the Fiscal Court as specified in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 158.115 and 67.080 and violated the Kentucky Constitution. The circuit court ruled in favor of the taxpayers and ordered the Fiscal Court to stop providing direct aid to nonpublic schools. On appeal, the court affirmed and explained that, when payment was made directly to a nonpublic school, Ky. Const. § 184, which provided that public money could not be expended for education other than in common schools without a vote of the people, was violated. Moreover, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 158.115 contemplated transportation furnished by the Fiscal Court to all pupils equally, not selectively to some pupils and not others, and it did not contemplate direct payment to the general funds of private institutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court holding that the fiscal court's grants to private schools as transportation subsidies violated Kentucky law.

Revenue Cabinet v. Gossum

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, revenue cabinet and current and former members, sought review of the decision of the Marshall Circuit Court (Kentucky), which held that tax refunds for taxes paid under an unconstitutional statute might be available under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590 only for the two years preceding the year in which the litigation was commenced, in favor of appellee class. The class filed a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: Before it was amended, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 141.021 exempted state retirement annuities from state income tax, but exempted federal retirement annuities only up to $ 4,000. After the United States Supreme Court found a similar statute unconstitutional, the class, composed of federal retirees, sought refunds of taxes paid on federal retirement benefits received during the five-year period preceding the Supreme Court's decision. The circuit court held that two year limitations period of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590 had a rational basis and that refunds were only available for the two years preceding the litigation's commencement. The court reversed the part of the circuit court's decision restricting the refund period and held that the general assembly was clear that taxes paid under an unconstitutional statute should be refunded, provided that the refund application was made within two years from the date payment was made. The court affirmed the circuit court's decision in all other respects and held that the shorter two year limitations period of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590(2) had a rational basis and that the class was not entitled to attorneys' fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the circuit court's decision that held that refunds were available only for the two years preceding the year in which the class commenced the litigation. The circuit court's decision was affirmed in all other respects.

72 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Bussell v. Commonwealth


92-SC-74-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


882 S.W.2d 111; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 51



April 21, 1994, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 29, 1994. Released for Publication September 29, 1994.
Writ of certiorari denied Bussell v. Kentucky, 513 U.S. 1174, 115 S. Ct. 1154, 130 L. Ed. 2d 1111, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 1395 (1995)
Related proceeding at Commonwealth v. Bussell, 226 S.W.3d 96, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 133 (Ky., 2007)
Decision reached on appeal by Russell v. Commonwealth, 2011 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 65 (Ky., Aug. 25, 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the Christian Circuit Court (Kentucky) judgment of conviction for murder and robbery and the death sentence imposed. He asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion for recusal, in permitting testimony to elicit sympathy for the victim, in instructing the jury that it could "recommend" a life sentence; and in denying his motion for a directed verdict.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of murder and robbery and he was sentenced to death. He sought review, alleging that the trial judge erred in denying his motion for recusal, in allowing testimony that elicited sympathy for the victim, in instructing the jury that it could "recommend" a life sentence, and in denying a directed verdict. The court affirmed. It held that the recusal motion presented nothing new that the trial judge would have learned through his prior representation of defendant, which would have rendered him biased. The release of information as to defendant's competency was not confidential and could readily have been learned from public record in the case. Testimony from the victim's family and the prosecutor's reminder to the jury during the penalty phase closing argument that the victim had relatives did not deny defendant a fair trial. Certain background information was relevant to understanding the crime. The court disapproved of using the word "recommend" in instructing the jury on sentencing in capital cases, but concluded that defendant had waived the issue and that the use of the word had not been unduly prejudicial. Ample evidence supported the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction for murder and robbery. There was no reason for the trial judge to have recused himself. Certain background information about the victim was relevant to an understanding of the nature of the crime. The erroneous use of the word "recommended" in the jury's sentencing instruction was not unduly prejudicial. Sufficient evidence supported the denial of the directed verdict motion.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth appealed a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed defendant's disorderly conduct conviction under Ken. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 525.060 (1984). The commonwealth claimed that the content of defendant's speech was not in issue, and that substantial evidence supported the jury's verdict.

Rev. Stat. Ann. § 525.060(1)(b) and (d). The court noted that it was not the content of her speech that was criminalized, but the fact that she had been unreasonably loud and had created a physically offensive condition without legitimate purpose.

Campbell v. Brewer


93-SC-170-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


884 S.W.2d 638; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 23



March 24, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 91-CA-2780. (Wolfe Circuit Court No. 91-CI-052)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed a decision of the Wolfe Circuit Court (Kentucky) enjoining appellees, who included the county beverage control administrator and petition signers, from holding county-wide precinct elections on whether or not prohibition should be reinstated. The appellate court ruled that the circuit court's reliance on Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 242.030(5) was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after Wolfe County voted to abolish prohibition, petitions were circulated to decide the issue on a precinct-by-precinct basis for every precinct in the county. Appellants sought to enjoin the elections, claiming that they violated the three-year waiting period prescribed by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 242.030(5). The circuit court found for appellants but the appellate court reversed. On subsequent appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court. The court noted that because the votes in each precinct would be counted separately and would determine the outcome for that precinct only, without reference to the results in other precincts, there was no violation of § 242.030(5). The territories in the second election (precincts) was not the same as the territory in the first election (county). The court also said that if its application of such statutes was wrong, it was up to the Legislature to correct the law.


OUTCOME: The court found for appellees and affirmed the appellate court.

 

75 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Revenue Cabinet v. Smith


93-SC-946-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


875 S.W.2d 873; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 34



March 24, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 23, 1994. Petition for Rehearing Denied June 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 93-CA-002840. (Franklin Circuit Court No. 93-CI-000959)



DISPOSITION: REVERSING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a state medical association and related parties, commenced an action alleging that the enactment of a health care provider tax on physicians, codified at Ky. Rev. Stat. §§ 142.201-142.259, 216.270-216.287, was unconstitutional. The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) determined that the tax violated Ky. Const. § 59 (15). Defendants, the state and affected state agencies, appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under the bill, a two percent of gross revenue tax was imposed on physicians' services, whether or not they participated in the state's medicaid program, and the tax proceeds were utilized to obtain federal matching money to support the program. The issue before the court was whether the state's general assembly lacked the ability to define the class of providers being taxed. The court reversed, holding that the health care provider tax as applied to physicians was constitutional. The court found that there was a rational basis for the classification: (1) because the state statute was designed to meet the federal statute which provided and enumerated the specific requirements as to the class of health care providers that might be taxed in order to qualify for federal matching funds; and (2) both groups of health care providers, those participating in the medicaid program and those not participating therein, might receive immediate and direct results of a fund that paid fees for treatment of the indigent. Thus, the tax on physicians' revenues did not violate Ky. Const. § 59 prohibiting special legislation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment.

Canler v. Commonwealth


93-SC-049-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


870 S.W.2d 219; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 3



January 31, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 91-CA-2443. (Logan Circuit Court No. 90-CR-084)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART AND REVERSING IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order by the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed a determination by the trial court suppressing defendant's confession of child abuse during a polygraph examination. Defendant also appealed a determination by the lower appellate court that the child abuse statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 508.100, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with criminal child abuse in the first degree in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 508.100. Prior to a polygraph examination, defendant signed a waiver encompassing his Miranda rights. Defendant then confessed, after questioning by the examiner, that he abused the child. Defendant moved to suppress the statement. Defendant also sought a ruling that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 508.100 was unconstitutional. The trial court suppressed the statement but upheld the constitutionality of the statute. The lower appellate court reversed as to the trial court's order suppressing defendant's confession. Defendant appealed. The court reversed the lower appellate court's order permitting the confession to be admitted at trial, holding that the prosecution did not prove by at least a preponderance of the evidence that defendant's confession during the polygraph examination was voluntary. An involuntary statement could not be used at trial under any circumstances. However, the court upheld the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 508.100, holding that it was sufficiently clear to apprise ordinary sensible persons of the types of acts that it sanctioned.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower appellate court upholding the constitutionality of the child abuse statute. The court reversed the order of the lower appellate court permitting the admission of defendant's confession of child abuse.
