Kentucky Harlan Coal Co. v. Holmes


92-SC-1073-WC, 93-SC-027-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


872 S.W.2d 446; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 6



January 31, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied Aril 21, 1994. Released for Publication April 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 91-CA-2644. W.C.B. NO. 89-29834.

ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 91-CA-2586. W.C.B. NO. 90-02661.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, coal company, commonwealth, and employer, challenged an order of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which upheld the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.732(1)(d), relied upon by appellees, employees, special fund, administrative law judge, and board, for the approval of benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, coal company, commonwealth, and employer, challenged the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.732(1)(d), which provides income benefits for occupational pneumoconiosis. The appeals court upheld the constitutionality of § 342.732(1)(d). On appeal, the court affirmed the constitutionality of the statute, ruling that it equally applied to all coal workers who had contracted pneumoconiosis. The court held that the legislature had provided a natural reason for classifying them separately from workers in other industries with the same illness. The court concluded that the different treatment was not arbitrary or unfair to either group. The court ruled that § 342.732 and the classifications created were rationally related to a legitimate state objective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the constitutionality of the statute, ruling that it applied equally to appellees, employees, who had contracted pneumoconiosis. The court held that the different legislative treatment of appellees was not arbitrary or unfair, but rationally related to a legitimate state objective.

 

78 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth Revenue Cabinet v. Cope


93-SC-056-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


875 S.W.2d 87; 1994 Ky. LEXIS 15



January 31, 1994, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1994. Released for Publication May 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON TRANSFER FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 93-CA-0176. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 91-CI-1676 AND 90-CI-1302



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth sought review of a judgment from the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), in favor of appellees, private pensioners, in the private pensioners' action that sought declaratory and injunctive relief for being subjected to the collection of an unconstitutional income tax.


OVERVIEW: A state law exempted federal, state, and local government retirees from payment of income taxes on their pension benefits. The law originally only exempted state and local government retirees, but in order to comply with 4 U.S.C.S. § 111, which prohibited states to discriminate against federal retirees, federal retirees were also exempted from the income tax on pension benefits. The trial court found that there was not a sufficient basis for the classification and held the exemption applicable to all pension benefit recipients. On appeal the court found that the state statute was not arbitrary and without a permissible legislative purpose. The court found that the statute was enacted in furtherance of what the legislature determined to be a proper public purpose, providing an additional benefit to government employees who were generally paid less than their counterparts in the private sector. The mere expansion of the class to include federal retirees did not invalidate the proper classification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the private pensioners and dismissed their claims.

 

79 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Hendricks v. Commonwealth


92-SC-662-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


865 S.W.2d 332; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 154



November 24, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 92-CA-1351. CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT NOS. 91-X-29 AND 91-X-30.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed defendants' convictions for nude dancing.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were found guilty of nude dancing in violation of a city ordinance. The lower court affirmed the convictions. Defendants appealed and argued that the city ordinance did not apply to a private club; was an unreasonable exercise of police power; and was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court affirmed defendants' convictions because it found that the club was a public club and a place of public accommodation. The court held that the ordinance was not an unreasonable exercise of police power because it did not attempt to regulate activity in a private place. The ordinance was not overbroad since it bore a reasonable relationship to its stated purpose. The court determined that the ordinance did not operate beyond the occasion or necessity of the particular situation and therefore did not violate the First Amendment. The ordinance only required a slight amount of clothing, and did not prohibit dancing but rather public nudity. The court concluded that the ordinance was not vague because it defined the criminal offense of appearing nude in public with sufficient clarity that any reasonable and ordinary person could understand what conduct was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for violation of a city ordinance prohibiting public nudity.

 

80 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Arch on N. Fork v. Campbell


No. 93-SC-250-WC, No. 93-SC-262-WC


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


865 S.W.2d 312; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 167



November 24, 1993, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 92-CA-152-WC. (Workers' Compensation Board of No. 90-11722)



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an employer and a special fund, sought review of a decision of the court of appeals (Kentucky), which reversed a lower court decision in an action brought by appellee claimant. The appeal concerned the claimant's claim for benefits due to coal workers' pneumoconiosis.


OVERVIEW: Claimant had been employed in the coal industry for 13 years, wherein his duties involved driving a coal truck and operating heavy equipment at his employer's surface mine. The appeal concerned his claim for benefits due to coal workers' pneumoconiosis. The Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) reviewed the medical evidence and concluded that the claimant had contracted category 1 pneumoconiosis which resulted from his exposure to coal dust. Benefits were therefore awarded pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.732(1)(a). The claimant argued that the ALJ was without authority to ignore his FEV1 values, regardless of whether they were related to his exposure to coal dust, and was required to award a total disability benefit pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.732(1)(c). On appeal, the court found that the ALJ determined that the claimant's depressed FEV1 values were caused by asthma and that claimant had not shown that his depressed FVC values were caused by pneumoconiosis. The court held that the claimant had failed to meet his burden on appeal to show that the evidence in his favor was so overwhelming that a finding in his favor was compelled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and reinstated the award made by the ALJ.

Kraus v. Kentucky State Senate


92-SC-960-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


872 S.W.2d 433; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 169



November 24, 1993, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified March 24, 1994. Rehearing Denied March 24, 1994. Released for Publication March 24, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 91-CA-1864-MR. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 90-CI-1613



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nominee sought review of a judgment from the Kentucky Court of Appeals, which rejected his constitutional challenge to the authority of the Kentucky State Senate to exercise approval power over the employment of workers' compensation judges pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.230(3).


OVERVIEW: The Kentucky Senate rejected the nominee's selection as an administrative law judge by the workers' compensation board. He filed a declaration of rights action seeking to have § 342.230(3) declared unconstitutional and requesting damages and appointment to the position. The court held that the senate had the inherent power to advise and consent on executive branch appointments of inferior state officers; hence, the statute did not violate Ky. Const. §§ 27 and 28.The court held that the nominee had standing to sue under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.045, which provided that any person whose rights were affected by statute or who was concerned with any title to office could apply for and secure a declaration of rights if an actual controversy existed. The court noted that members of the General Assembly were not immune from declaratory judgment relief simply because they were acting in their official capacities. Ky. Const. § 43, however, provided legislative immunity from suits concerning speech or debate, and the court held that this provision extended to voting on executive appointments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate decision that upheld the constitutionality of the selection process.

Bowling v. Commonwealth


91-SC-45-MR, 91-SC-75-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


873 S.W.2d 175; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 127



September 30, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 24, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ky. LEXIS 26. As Modified March 24, 1994. Released for Publication March 24, 1994.
Modified and rehearing denied by Bowling v. Commonwealth, 1994 Ky. LEXIS 26 (Ky., Mar. 24, 1994)
Writ of certiorari denied Bowling v. Kentucky, 513 U.S. 862, 115 S. Ct. 176, 130 L. Ed. 2d 112, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 6204 (1994)
Decision reached on appeal by In re Bowling, 2005 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 14 (Ky., Apr. 21, 2005)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Bowling v. Commonwealth, 2012 Ky. LEXIS 76 (Ky., May 24, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HON. GEORGE BARKER, JUDGE. CRIMINAL ACTION NO. 90-CR-363



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fayette County Circuit Court (Kentucky) convicted defendant of the intentional murders of a husband and wife and of fourth-degree assault of the couple's two-year-old son. The defendant was sentenced to death for the murders. The defendant appealed his conviction for the murders and his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. One of the defendant's primary contentions on appeal was that the trial court erred in failing to instruct on extreme emotional disturbance and first degree manslaughter and in failing to direct the jury to fully consider mitigating evidence in the guilt and penalty phases. The court stated that: (1) there was no evidence that the defendant was overcome on the morning of the murders and that he acted as a result of anything other than an evil purpose; (2) the jury was instructed to consider mitigating factors which they found relevant and there was no requirement to provide instructions regarding extreme emotional disturbance, mental disease or defect, and intoxication; and (3) a jury instruction on unanimous findings on mitigation was not required. Defendant also contended that in a double murder in which the only aggravating circumstance was intentional multiple murders, the imposition of the death penalty for either killing violated constitutional guarantees against double jeopardy. The court stated that there were two murders and two sentences and the defendant was not punished for the same offense twice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

Commonwealth v. Welch


92-SC-490-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


864 S.W.2d 280; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 128



September 30, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 21, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 90-CA-1189. APPEAL FROM BOYD CIRCUIT COURT. HON. CHARLES STOCKDALE SINNETTE, JUDGE. INDICTMENT NO. 90-CR-0006



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother was charged with criminal abuse in the second degree, possession of a narcotic, and possession of drug paraphernalia. The mother was found guilty of all charges. The court of appeals vacated the mother's conviction for criminal drug abuse, and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother was convicted of criminal abuse in the second degree for using controlled substances while she was pregnant. Her child was born addicted to a controlled substance. The appellate court determined that a fetus was not a person under the Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 508.110. Furthermore, the appellate court found that such a reading violated the legislative intent. The State argued that this conclusion was incorrect because the baby was born alive and the effects of past criminal activity caused the baby to suffer postpartum from neonatal abstinence syndrome. The court examined the legislative history of § 508.110 and other statutes that punished pregnant women using controlled substances. The court determined that the appellate court correctly determined that mother's conduct was not covered under the wording of § 508.110.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision that vacated the mother's conviction for criminal abuse in the second degree.

 

84 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Ward v. Harding


88-SC-825-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


860 S.W.2d 280; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 101



July 15, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1993. Released for Publication September 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 85-CA-514 and 85-CA-857. JOHNSON CIRCUIT COURT NO. 82-CI-501



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surface owners sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed the judgment in favor of surface owners and instead determined that appellee mineral owners held the dominant estate and were entitled to use the surface in any manner necessary or convenient for recovery of the minerals.


OVERVIEW: As an initial matter, the court noted that the dispositive issue on appeal was whether broad form deed mineral owners were permitted by virtue of that instrument alone, to engage in surface mining. The court then held that as it was neither fair nor just to deny damages for surface destruction, it was neither fair nor just to permit surface mining contrary to the wishes of surface owners and beyond the contemplation of the original parties to the instrument. Thus, as the court found that the conveyance of minerals by broad form deed did not include the right to strip mine, it overruled the portions of Buchanan v. Watson, 290 S.W.2d 40 (1956), which so presumed a right. The court therefore held that mineral owners had a common law right to remove their coal in accordance with the instrument of severance and the manner contemplated therein, but were without any protected right to retain benefits claimed by virtue of previous caselaw. The court concluded by noting that as mineral owners' entitlement to remove minerals in accordance with the instrument of acquisition was unaffected by Ky. Const. § 19(2), there was no violation of the Fifth or Fourteenth Amendments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment under review and ordered the reinstatement of the judgment enjoining mineral owners from entering upon the property of surface owners for the purpose of surface, strip, or auger mining.

DeGrella v. Elston


92-SC-756-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


858 S.W.2d 698; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 103



July 15, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 5, 1993.  [**1]


PRIOR HISTORY: ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 92-CA-2173. APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HON. JOSEPH H. ECKERT, JUDGE. NO. 92-CI-1099



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian challenged the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which held that appellees, mother and legal guardian, had the right to direct the attending physician and the nursing home where daughter resided to disconnect the feeding tube that was maintaining her existence and let her die.


OVERVIEW: Appellee mother's daughter sustained severe brain damage for which medical treatment was of no benefit, and she lived in a persistent vegetative state. The trial court held that appellees, mother and legal guardian, had the right to direct daughter's attending physician and the nursing home to disconnect the feeding tube that was maintaining her existence and let her die. Appellant guardian ad litem challenges the legality of the decision, and the court affirmed. The court concluded that the trial court found by clear and convincing evidence that the proof sustained the allegations of the complaint, both as to the medical facts regarding the daughter's condition and prognosis and as to her choice as she expressed it to family members on different occasions and in different contexts. The court found that the daughter specifically stated, as the subject came up in conversation on various occasions, that if she were ever faced with a devastating injury or illness incapacitating her to such an extent, she would want her treatment terminated rather than having her life prolonged by artificial means.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment concluding that appellees, mother and legal guardian, had the right to direct daughter's attending physician and the nursing home to disconnect the feeding tube that was maintaining her existence and let her die. The court concluded that clear and convincing evidence established that she did not wish to be in a persistent vegetative state because of her statements, medical facts, and prognosis.

Regency Pheasant Run v. Karem


93-SC-130-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


860 S.W.2d 755; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 96



July 1, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL ACTION IN THE COURT OF APPEALS. 93-CA-0376



DISPOSITION: DENYING THE ISSUANCE OF A WRIT OF PROHIBITION


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of prohibition to prohibit the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) in an underlying case from entering a judgment rendered by respondent special circuit judge who was temporarily assigned to preside over nine cases on the day that the underlying case was tried. Petitioner argued that the respondent was not authorized to serve as a judge pro tempore because he was a practicing attorney.


OVERVIEW: Before he retired as a judge, respondent presided over a 12-day bench trial in which petitioner was defendant in a lawsuit regarding notes owed by petitioner in a real estate deal. Before an opinion was rendered in the underlying case, respondent retired as a judge. Thereafter, he entered the private practice of law. About two months after his retirement, respondent was temporarily assigned by the chief judge of the trial court to serve as a special circuit judge under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26A.020 and Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 1.040 over nine cases on a certain day. On that day, respondent rendered an opinion in the underlying case against petitioner. The court denied the writ of prohibition and held that the judgment rendered by respondent was not void under the Ky. Const. and that respondent was acting under a constitutionally valid appointment. As such, the court held that Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 4.300, Canons 2, 2(A) were not violated by respondent. The court further noted that respondent was not required to comply with Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 4.300, Canon 5(F) pursuant to Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 4.300, Canon 7 and, thus, was allowed to practice law while acting as a judge pro tempore.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of prohibition.

Capital Area Right to Life v. Downtown Frankfort


92-SC-347-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


862 S.W.2d 297; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 97



July 1, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 28, 1993. Released for Publication October 28, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 90-CA-2564. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HON. SQUIRE N. WILLIAMS, JR., JUDGE. 90-CI-1636



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advocacy group attacked the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), affirming the trial court's denial of injunctive relief and grant of summary judgment to appellees, non-profit corporation and president. The advocacy group filed suit against the non-profit corporation and its president, seeking relief under the Kentucky Declaratory Judgment Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 418, and the Federal Civil Rights Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Upon weighing the circumstances of the case in the aggregate, the court held that the non-profit corporation qualified as a state actor. There were many factors that pointed to this conclusion. The non-profit corporation was incorporated as a private, non-profit corporation, but its purpose was to bring about "revitalization" of the city's downtown. This was a function it took over from the city to the extent of carrying out the "Main Street Program," which was operated under the patronage and guidance of an agency of state government under the Education and Humanities Cabinet. The non-profit corporation's principal funding was from monies received from that state agency, from the city, and from the county fiscal court. The court concluded that in conducting the "Great Pumpkin Festival" and setting policy as to what individuals, groups, or organizations could maintain booths at the festival, the activities of the non-profit corporation and its president constituted state action. The court further held that the restriction did not abridge the advocacy group's constitutional right to free speech, declaring that such restriction was a reasonable limitation on time, place, and manner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court in favor of the non-profit corporation and its president.

Appalachian Regional Health Care v. Johnson


92-SC-1049-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


862 S.W.2d 868; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 75



May 27, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1993. Released for Publication September 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 92-CA-2288



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a doctor, hospital, and health care corporation, challenged an order of the Court Of Appeals (Kentucky), denying a writ of prohibition in plaintiff patient's negligence action arising from an operation the doctor negligently performed. The doctor and hospital had tried to prevent disclosure of peer review documents containing information regarding the doctor's performance by invoking the protection of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 311.377(2).


OVERVIEW: The doctor and hospital wanted to avoid having to produce peer review records from disciplinary proceedings in Kentucky that related to the doctor's performance. The patient had discovered that the doctor had had his clinical privileges revoked by a New York hospital, and he was later denied admission to practice in both South Carolina and Kentucky. Kentucky only granted him a probationary license on appeal because the hospital said it was willing to take responsibility for closely supervising him. The trial court allowed discovery of the documents, finding that § 311.377(2) did not provide a privilege against the discovery of peer review documents in a medical negligence action brought by a patient against a doctor and his hospital. The appeals court affirmed, noting that the trial court's order contained measures to maintain confidentiality of the records. Even if the interlocutory order was erroneous, the extraordinary remedy here sought was not a substitute for the appellate process and could not be invoked. The court concurred, as defendants had not demonstrated that they would suffer irreparable harm, nor had they shown that the remedy of appeal was inadequate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the the opinion of the appeals court, which denied the writ of prohibition and ordered that the discovery go forward and the documents be produced.

Thomas v. Commonwealth


88-SC-375-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


864 S.W.2d 252; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 77



May 27, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1993. Released for Publication September 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM KNOTT CIRCUIT COURT. HON. PHILIP R. MORGAN, JUDGE. INDICTMENT NO. 87-CR-002



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of wanton murder and first-degree burglary and sentenced to death and to 18 years' imprisonment as entered by the Knott Circuit Court (Kentucky). On automatic appeal, defendant assigned 34 errors.


OVERVIEW: During voir dire, the lower court overruled defendant's challenges of prospective jurors for cause. Three jurors indicated that they were predisposed to imposing the death penalty. Two of the potential jurors indicated that they were affected by pretrial publicity in the case, one of whom also was related by marriage to the prosecutor. One potential juror was related by marriage to the victim. He was not challenged for cause and sat as the foreman of the jury. On appeal, the court determined that the lower court erred in overruling defendant's challenges for cause. The lower court's questions to the prospective jurors did not serve to rehabilitate the jurors in the instances where they initially showed bias and they should have been excused as not qualified. A family relationship, whether by blood or by marriage, between a juror and the judge, prosecutor, or victim, disqualified the juror and was grounds for reversal. The court found that the jury's verdict was unreliable because they were told about the automatic appeal defendant received when sentenced to death and did not apprehend that their decision was final.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The grounds for challenging the jurors for cause were so substantial that the lower court's failure to sustain challenges was an abuse of discretion.

Fischer v. State Bd. of Elections


92-SC-354-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


847 S.W.2d 718; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 52



February 18, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 11, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM AN ORIGINAL ACTION IN THE COURT OF APPEALS. 92-CA-679-OA



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant voter brought an action against defendant election officials, challenging the constitutionality of reapportionment legislation. The election officials brought this original proceeding in the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), seeking a writ of prohibition. The court of appeals granted the writ, which prohibited the trial court from adjudicating the voter's lawsuit. The voter appealed from the grant of the writ.


OVERVIEW: The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 452.405(2) allowed the voter to challenge the constitutionality of a statute in the venue in which he was alleged to have been injured. The county in which the alleged injury occurred controlled the issue of venue, rather than the county where the redistricting statute was adopted. Though the legislative enactment of the General Assembly occurred in Franklin County, the effect of the redistricting lines was felt in Campbell County, where the voter was a resident and taxpayer. Accordingly, the court held, he should be allowed to bring his challenge within the venue of the Campbell Circuit Court. The court held that the parties would not be irreparably harmed by defending the suit in Campbell County, and there was an adequate remedy by way of appeal. Therefore, the grant of a writ of prohibition and an injunction against the trial judge was clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the writ of prohibition and injunction and remanded the case to the original trial court for further proceedings.

 

92 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Raines


91-SC-653-CL


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


847 S.W.2d 724; 1993 Ky. LEXIS 51



February 18, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 11, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON DISTRICT COURT. HON. THOMAS B. MERRILL, JUDGE. NO. 90-TO-61465A


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Commonwealth of Kentucky (commonwealth) appealed an order from the Jefferson District Court (Kentucky), which denied the commonwealth's motion for a mandatory pretrial suspension of defendant's motor vehicle license pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.200. The district court had declared § 189A.200 was unconstitutional and violative of due process and the separation of powers doctrine of the Kentucky constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with driving under the influence. The commonwealth filed a motion to suspend defendant's license. The district court denied the motion and held § 189.200 was unconstitutional. The commonwealth appealed. On appeal, the court certified the law. The court found § 189A.200(1)(b) was violative of the Fourteenth Amendment and § 59 of the Kentucky constitution because it contained an arbitrary age classification. The court applied a three-factor test in order to decide if the rest of § 189A.200 was constitutional. The court held the suspension of a driver's license by the commonwealth implicated a property interest protectable under due process. The court found although the interest in possessing a driver's license was high, the state had a compelling interest in removing drunk drivers from highways. The court found the risk of an erroneous deprivation was low. The court held it was paramount that defendant could have sought judicial review of the suspension within 30 days. The court found nothing appeared in Kentucky's constitution that gave the executive branch the exclusive authority to control the issuance, possession, use and revocation of drivers' licenses.


OUTCOME: The court certified the law with regard to the constitutionality of pretrial license provisions.

 

93 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Waggoner v. Waggoner


91-SC-440-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


846 S.W.2d 704; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 189



December 17, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 18, 1993. Released for Publication March 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. 89-CA-1464. CARTER CIRCUIT COURT. HON. SAMUEL C. LONG, JUDGE. (88-CI-165)



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had denied appellee husband's motion to alter, vacate, or amend a dissolution decree, and directed the trial court to allow discovery of the wife's mandatory contributions to a teachers' retirement system (TRS), in the course of a dissolution proceeding.


OVERVIEW: In dissolution of marriage case, the husband sought to discover the mandatory contributions made by his wife, a teacher, to the TRS. The trial court found that, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 161.700(2), the contributions were nonmarital property and not subject to discovery and later overruled the husband's motion to alter, vacate, or amend a subsequent dissolution decree. The court of appeals reversed and ordered the trial court to allow discovery. On review, the court reversed and affirmed the trial court, finding that although § 161.700(2) set teachers up as a special class, the provision did not violate § 59 of the Kentucky Constitution when the statute was applied equally to all and because a distinctive and natural reason supported the classification. The TRS was enacted to provide retirement benefits to state teachers who were not covered by the social security system and the purpose behind § 161.700(1) was to protect teachers by insulating their retirement allowances from attachment during the division of marital property. Further, the statute did not violate the husband's rights under the Equal Protection Clause and its retrospective application was not improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals, which reversed the trial court's denial of the husband's motion to alter, vacate, or amend a dissolution decree and directed the trial court to allow the husband to discovery the wife's mandatory contributions to a teachers' retirement system, was reversed, in a dissolution of marriage proceeding.

 

94 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Sanders v. Commonwealth


90-SC-954-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


844 S.W.2d 391; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 171



November 19, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 18, 1993. Released for Publication February 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM DAVIESS CIRCUIT COURT. HON. ROBERT M. SHORT, JUDGE, DIVISION 2. CRIMINAL ACTION NO. 90-CR-036



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the Daviess Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted him of rape, sodomy, robbery, burglary, and assault and which imposed consecutive sentences of imprisonment with an enhancement for being a persistent felony offender. Appellant contended that identifications should have been suppressed and that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 439.3401 was unconstitutional in the sentence imposed for violent offenders.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of rape, sodomy, robbery, burglary, and assault, and consecutive sentences of imprisonment with an enhancement for being a persistent felony offender were imposed, as well as a concurrent sentence for a misdemeanor. Appellant sought review and the court affirmed. The court held that photographic identification of appellant was properly admitted where the victim had ample time to observe appellant, and denial of appellant's motion to suppress was proper. The court further held that his sentencing was proper, based upon the court's interpretation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 439.3401(3), which provided sentence enhancement for violent offenders. The court held that the increase in imprisonment time during which parole was not available to 50 percent on the sentence imposed was constitutional where it was interpreted to allow the increase only to the maximum amount of 12 years, as contained in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 439.3401(2). The court held that appellant's other contentions lacked merit and affirmed the convictions and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for rape, sodomy, robbery, burglary, and assault and affirmed the imposition of sentences of imprisonment, together with enhancements due to appellant's violent offender status. The court held the enhancement statute did not violate due process or equal protection where the increase in imprisonment time without parole was allowed up to a maximum amount, as contained in another section of the statute.

 

95 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Meyers v. Chapman Printing Co.


92-SC-396-TG, 92-SC-397-TG, 92-SC-398-TG, 92-SC-399-TG and 92-SC-400-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


840 S.W.2d 814; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 151; 60 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 336



October 22, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified December 17, 1992. Released for Publication December 17, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NOS. 89-CA-2463, 90-CA-1261, 89-CA-2423, 90-CA-1660, 86-CI-281. APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HON. GEORGE E. BARKER, JUDGE. NO. 86-CI-281



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee and defendant employer challenged a decision of the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky), which found in the employee's favor on her sexual harassment claim under the Kentucky Civil Rights Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 344.010 et seq., and awarded her attorneys' fees, but did not find in her favor regarding her claim of gender-based discrimination. The case was transferred to the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The employee alleged that she was subjected to inappropriate sexual comments by her employer. The employee was discharged. The employee alleged that she was subjected to inappropriate sexual comments by her employer. After she was discharged, she brought an action under the Kentucky Civil Rights Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 344.010 et seq., seeking damages. The supreme court held that 1) the employee's claim for damages for emotional distress were not preempted by workers' compensation laws, because such only preempted common law tort claims, not statutory ones, 2) the employee was entitled to a trial by jury under the act, 3) the evidence supported the inference that the employer used abusive and intimidating conduct of a sexual nature, which supported the employee's harassment claim, 4) the jury instruction on her claim of gender-based discrimination was not error, even though it used the language but for regarding the causation aspect, because such language did not require a finding such discrimination as a sole cause, but only as a substantial factor, and 5) the attorneys' fees awarded were not an abuse of discretion by the lower court, seeking damages.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the decision in favor of the employee on her sexual harassment claim as well as the award of attorneys' fees, and there was no error regarding the decision in the employer's favor on the employee's claim of gender-based discrimination.

 

96 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Sommers v. Commonwealth


89-SC-882-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


843 S.W.2d 879; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 137



September 24, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 17, 1992.
Post-conviction relief denied at Sommers v. Commonwealth, 2006 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 334 (Ky. Ct. App., July 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM McCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HON. J. W. "BILL" GRAVES, JUDGE. 88-CR-247



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his murder convictions and prison sentence from the McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky). He appealed as a matter of right and claimed that the trial judge abused his discretion when he denied defendant's motions of recusation and for the funding of consultants and/or witnesses, and argued that he was prejudiced during both the guilt/innocence and penalty phases of his trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted a number of alleged procedural errors on the part of the trial judge. The court examined the trial record and determined that: 1.) Under the circumstances it was reasonable for the defense to question the trial judge's impartiality, and denial of the motion of recusation constituted an abuse of discretion; 2.) Defendant was provided competent expert psychiatric and social worker assistance, which he used in his trial, and he failed to establish that further expert assistance was "reasonably necessary" for his defense; and 3.) Defendant, who was subject to enhanced penalties for a subsequent offense, was entitled to suppression of evidence of the earlier conviction, because the record showed that he was not present when his counsel entered a guilty plea on his behalf. Accordingly, the court ruled that the law of the case was that evidence of the misdemeanor must be suppressed upon proper motion in the event of a second sentencing phase.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction, vacated the sentence, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

97 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Wasson


90-SC-558-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


842 S.W.2d 487; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 140



September 24, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 2, 1993. Released for Publication January 21, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 90-CA-1483. FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HON. CHARLES M. TACKETT, JUDGE. NO. 86-XX-048



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with solicitation to engage in deviate sexual intercourse in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 510.100 and 506.030. The trial court held that the statute violated defendant's right to privacy and dismissed the action. The Commonwealth appealed to the Fayette County Circuit Court, which affirmed. The Commonwealth appealed once more and the action was transferred from the Kentucky Court of Appeals.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after he invited an undercover police officer back to his home for sex. He was charged under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 510.100, which punishes deviate sexual intercourse with another person of the same sex. The court held that the statute violated the protections of privacy and equal protection under the Ky. Constitution. The court noted that the protections under the state constitution exceeded those of the federal constitution. Further, an evaluation of state case law revealed a long history recognizing the rights of the individual to be free from government constraint and included the right to live without unwarranted interference by the public. Unlike the federal constitution that limited protection to certain classes, no class of persons could be discriminated against under the Kentucky Constitution. All were entitled to equal treatment unless there was a substantial governmental interest, a rational basis, for different treatment. The court looked to the evidence compiled by the defendant and found that there was no rational basis to discriminate against homosexuals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the charges against defendant.

 

98 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Philpot v. Patton


92-SC-261-I


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


837 S.W.2d 491; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 142



September 24, 1992, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 92-CA-763. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. 91-C8-466. HON. ROGER CRITTENDEN, JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant senators sought a declaration that Ky. Sen. R. 48 violated Ky. Const. § 46 and an order to require appellee colleagues to consider legislation that the senators attempted to introduce. The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) held that the senators were not entitled to the relief and the senators appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a judgment in the colleagues' favor in the senators' action for a declaration that Ky. Sen. R. 48 violated Ky. Const. § 46 and for an order to require the consideration of the legislation that the senators tried to introduce. The court dismissed the action without prejudice. The court reasoned that the controversy was moot because the legislative session in which Ky. Sen. R. 48 was enacted and in which the senators introduced the legislation had adjourned, and that it was less than certain that Rule 48 was going to be reenacted in the next legislative session or that the senators were going to introduce bills that were similar to those that were buried in committee. The court also held that, due to the provisions of Ky. Const. § 46, a rule that allowed a committee's final meeting to occur without reporting a bill would have been subject to a judicial challenge.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the action brought by the senators, finding that the controversy was moot.

 

99 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Nichols v. Commonwealth


90-SC-838-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


839 S.W.2d 263; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 143



September 24, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 89-CA-1394. GREENUP CIRCUIT COURT NO. 88-CR-109. HON. JAMES W. LYON, SR. JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment and sentence of the Greenup Circuit Court (Kentucky), which sentenced him to a total of ten years as a result of his guilty plea to eleven counts of burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant reached a plea agreement whereby he pled guilty to eleven counts of burglary and the prosecution recommended a sentence of five years on each of the eleven counts to run concurrently. Before rendering the sentence the circuit court withdrew the sentence, set the matter for trial, and advised the prosecution to contact the victims. Cases for the three victims who did not agree with the prosecution's recommendation were sent to a jury. The jury recommended five year concurrent sentences to run concurrently with the other eight counts. The circuit court, however, ordered the sentences to run concurrently with each other but consecutively to the other for a total of ten years. Defendant argued that the judge should have recused himself because the sentence was motivated by his desire to please the jailer who was one of the victims. The court found that the language of the judge did not provide a basis for personal bias and that he was concerned about the views of all of the victims who each had a right to make an impact statement. He did not err in not recusing himself. Further, he was not bound by the recommendation of the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence as imposed by the circuit court.

 

100 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Board of Educ. v. Paul


91-SC-725-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


846 S.W.2d 675; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 116



September 3, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 18, 1993. Released for Publication March 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 89-CA-604. (Kenton Circuit Court No. 88-CI-999)



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movants, Board of Education of Kenton County and superintendent, sought review from the order of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed the summary judgment against the respondent administrator.


OVERVIEW: The administrator, a high school assistant principal, was to be removed from his administrative position and reassigned as a classroom teacher. He filed suit against the movants and alleged that his reassignment and demotion was unconstitutional and arbitrary and did not comply with the statutory requirements of the Kentucky Teacher Tenure Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 161.765(2). The movants filed a motion for summary judgment, which the trial court granted on the grounds that the administrator was not entitled to a hearing because he had not completed three years of administrative service and had be properly notified of the demotion. The appellate court reversed. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court and held that the administrator had not completed three years of administrative service. The words "not less than seven school months within a school year" implied that the service be for more than seven months, so long as it was not less than seven months.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the court of appeals and reinstated the summary judgment in favor of the movants.

 

101 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Chapman v. Gorman


91-SC-654-TG, 91-SC-659-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


839 S.W.2d 232; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 124



September 3, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 19, 1992. Released for Publication November 19, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. NO. 91-CI-14. COURT OF APPEALS NO. 91-CA-1824-MR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs elected school board members (members) and their relatives (relatives) brought suit against the defendant attorney general, challenging the validity of anti-nepotism statutes, Ken. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 160.180(2)(I) and 160.380(2)(f). The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) upheld the constitutionality of the challenged provision and dismissed the members and the relatives complaint. The members and relatives appealed.


OVERVIEW: The members and relatives argued that Ken. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 160.180(2)(I) and 160.380(2)(f) violated their First Amendment rights, violated their rights expressed under the Equal Protection Clause, were overbroad, denied procedural and substantive due process, and infringed upon familial rights of school employees. Initially, the court determined that no fundamental rights were involved because no such status was given to candidacy. The court also found that the statutes did not significantly injure the voters' First Amendment rights. Furthermore, removing nepotism served a legitimate state interest, while imposing only incidental burdens on the members, the relatives, and voters. Furthermore, the court determined that the Equal Protection Clause was not violated, because the members and the relatives were not members of a suspect class. The court also found that the statute was not overbroad and did not infringe upon any familial rights of school employees. Therefore, the court upheld the constitutionality of §§ 160.180(2)(I) and 160.380(2)(f).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the attorney general.

Kentucky Utilities Co. v. South East Coal Co.


91-SC-357-DG, 91-SC-609-DG, 91-SC-610-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


836 S.W.2d 407; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 131



August 25, 1992, Entered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. NOS. 89-CA-002574, 89-CA-002575, 89-CA-002591, and 90-CA-000068. (Fayette Circuit Court No. 84-CI-001703)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent company moved for intermediate relief, for recusal of the Justices of the Supreme Court of Kentucky, and for disqualification of a special justice.


OVERVIEW: A special justice was appointed to hear a matter along with the other justices of the state supreme court. After the pending matter was heard, the company moved for recusal of the entire state supreme court panel from hearing the motion for disqualification of the special justice and disqualification of the special justice. The company argued that the appointment of the special justice was in violation of Ky. Const. § 110 and the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court denied both motions. The court determined that there was no reason for recusal of the panel and that the special justice had been appointed pursuant to a valid statute and in accordance with the provisions of the Kentucky Constitution. The court further held that the company had no due process right to retroactively challenge the appointment, by such a valid procedure, and made no allegation of a personal, substantial or pecuniary interest in the case on the part of the special justice to merit his recusal from sitting in the action.


OUTCOME: The motions for recusal and disqualification were denied.

 

103 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Keel v. St. Elizabeth Medical Center


90-SC-689-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


842 S.W.2d 860; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 82



June 4, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 16, 1992. Released for Publication September 16, 1992. As Modified September 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS 89-CA-2002 (Kenton Circuit Court No. 86-CI-890) .



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of a judgment entered in the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant hospital in plaintiff's action that claimed defendant had performed a medical procedure on him without his informed consent. The issue on appeal was whether expert testimony was required to support plaintiff's claim.


OVERVIEW: Patient who developed thrombophlebitis at site of contrast dye injection sought damages for alleged injury. The court held that expert evidence was not required in all instances where lack of informed consent was asserted. The court found it was significant that hospital offered patient no information about any possible hazards of the procedure, but at the same time admitted that it routinely questioned every patient about to undergo a dye injection as to whether patient had any previous reactions to contrast materials. The court concluded that a failure to adequately inform a patient need not be established by expert testimony where the failure was so apparent that laymen could easily recognize or infer it from evidence within the realm of common knowledge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

104 of 908 DOCUMENTS


State Bd. for Elementary & Secondary Educ. v. Howard


91-SC-606-TG, 91-SC-643-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


834 S.W.2d 657; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 85



June 4, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS NO. FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT #90-CI-1145.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state school board and research commission, sought review of a decision from the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee school employees in a declaratory judgment action to challenge the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 161.164 and 161.990. The statutes prohibited the school employees' involvement in political campaigns for the election of local school board members.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, it was asserted that the statutes were constitutional and enforceable because they were essential to the state's educational reform so that the state school system would operate in a constitutionally efficient manner required by Ky. Const. § 183. Thus, it was argued that the statutes were constitutional, and the accompanying injunctive relief restraining their enforcement should be overturned. The crucial element on review was the balancing of compelling state interests against the interests of citizens in participating in the political process. The court then found that a person of ordinary intelligence would not have been able to identify the conduct prohibited under the word "activities" in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 161.164(1). Thus, that portion of the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it did not give school employees a fair notice of the standard of conduct to which they were to be held accountable. The court nonetheless held that the remaining portions of the statutes were neither overbroad or impermissibly vague. Accordingly, the court reversed to the extent the statutes did not contain the proscribed term "activities," and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment under review insofar as it held that all provisions of the challenged statutes were unconstitutional, holding that only the word "activities" was unnecessarily and facially broad and vague. The court overruled the order enjoining the enforcement of the balance of the statutes and remanded the matter.

Williams v. Hillview


91-SC-342-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


831 S.W.2d 181; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 86



June 4, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS 89-CA-1428-MR. BULLITT CIRCUIT COURT NO. 87-CI-580. HON. ATHOL LEE TAYLOR, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, voters and landowners, sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed a summary judgment in favor of appellees, city and attorney general, in the voters' and landowners' declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The voters and landowners challenged an annexation ordinance adopted by the city. The circuit court, in a declaratory judgment action, granted summary judgment in favor of the city and attorney general. The court of appeals affirmed the summary judgment, ruling that the failure of 50 percent of the registered voters or landowners to protest the annexation was dispositive. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and held that the lower courts failed to address the issues of validity, sufficiency, and constitutionality of the annexation ordinances. The court ruled that the demonstrators had a right to contest the annexation ordinance, to prove that the description was inaccurate, it was improperly adopted without notice under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 61.825, and whether it was constitutional. The court remanded to the circuit court for an application of the rules of summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the court of appeals affirming the summary judgment in favor of the city and attorney general. The court remanded to the circuit court for an application of the summary judgment rules.

 

106 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Florence v. Owen Electric Coop., Inc.


90-SC-785-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


832 S.W.2d 876; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 72



May 14, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM BOONE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SAM NEACE, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION No. 89-CI-388.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city, franchisee and company, challenged the decision of the Boone Circuit Court (Kentucky), which held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 278.016, 278.017, 278.018, 96.538, 81A.490 and 279.110(5) were not rendered unconstitutional by Ky. Const. §§ 163 and 164 in appellants' declaratory judgment action against appellee corporation regarding utility services within the city's new annexed boundaries.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed a declaratory judgment action seeking to have several statutes rendered unconstitutional and to declare that the parties' franchise agreement gives the company the exclusive right to serve all utility customers within the city's newly annexed boundaries. The trial court held that the statutes were not unconstitutional and provided that the corporation had the exclusive right to provide retail service to all electric consuming facilities located within its certified territory, including those portions of its certified territory located within the boundaries of the city. The court concluded that the city's franchise power under Ky. Const. §§ 163 and 164 did not include the right to authorize the company to provide electrical service in the annexed territory, thereby overriding the statutory provision which regulated electric service areas. The court found that municipalities had only the right to grant street franchises. The court found no language which discerned that either §§ 163 or 164 indicated that the state had been deprived of the right to exercise police power and the right to implement control of rates and services of the utilities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment which held that certain utility service statutes were not unconstitutional and which held that the corporation had the exclusive right to provide retail serve to all electric consuming facilities located within its certified territory.

 

107 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Speers v. Commonwealth


91-SC-038-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


828 S.W.2d 638; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 59



April 9, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 90-CA-364. MADISON CIRCUIT COURT. 90-XX-001. MADISON DISTRICT COURT. 89-T-513, 89-T-789, AND 89-T-652



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were arrested for speeding and for DUI. After a motion to suppress the admission of blood tests was denied, the defendants entered conditional guilty pleas to DUI. On appeal, their convictions were first affirmed by the Court of Appeals (Kentucky). Defendants appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The court found that paramedics and phlebotomists were qualified medical technicians pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189.520(6). Therefore, they were authorized to draw blood samples for the purpose of testing to determine the blood alcohol level of a DUI suspect. The court determined that where actual consent was given there was no need to address the issue of implied consent under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 186.565(1). The court also held that consent had been freely and voluntarily given and that there was no evidence of coercion. Further, the court found that the state could seize without a warrant evanescent evidence which was likely to disappear before a warrant could be obtained, such as blood samples. The court found that the blood test results were clearly admissible at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions.

 

108 of 908 DOCUMENTS


King v. King


90-SC-495-DG, 90-SC-502-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


828 S.W.2d 630; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 44



March 12, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1992. Released for Publication June 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 89-CA-000207. (Boyle Circuit Court No. 88-CI-000282)



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant grandfather appealed the decision of the Kentucky Court of Appeals, which reversed the trial court decision allowing him visitation with respondent parents' child, his granddaughter, against their wishes.


OVERVIEW: Respondent parents opposed the visitation of their child with the movant paternal grandfather. Grandfather had almost daily contact with child for the 16 months she lived with her parents on his farm. Grandfather ordered them out because he thought his son drank too much and did not do enough work, and the parents thought grandfather was overbearing and intrusive. After they were asked to leave, grandfather requested that he be allowed to see the child. This request was denied. The trial court referred all of the parties for evaluation, mediation and recommendation. After receiving the report, the trial court granted visitation. The appellate court reversed. The court held that the grandparent visitation statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. § 405.021 was constitutional and the trial court did not err in finding that the best interest of the child would be served by allowing the grandfather visitation. The court felt that if a grandparent was physically, mentally and morally fit, then a grandchild would ordinarily benefit from contact with the grandparent and these considerations by the state did not go too far in intruding into the fundamental rights of the parents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court decision and reinstated the trial court decision allowing the grandfather visitation with the child.

 

109 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Stoker v. Commonwealth


89-SC-763-MR, 89-SC-764-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


828 S.W.2d 619; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 45



March 12, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1992. Released for Publication June 4, 1992.
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Stoker v. Watson, 184 Fed. Appx. 496, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 14294 (6th Cir.) (6th Cir. Ky., 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Stoker v. Commonwealth, 2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 41 (Ky. Ct. App., Mar. 27, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: HARDIN CIRCUIT COURT. HON. HUGH ROARK, JUDGE. INDICTMENT NO. 88-CR-142, NO. 89-CR-004



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART/REVERSING IN PART AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action filed by the Commonwealth, defendants appealed a judgment of the Hardin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted and sentenced them for first-degree sodomy, first-degree criminal abuse, first-degree sexual abuse, first-degree rape, and terroristic threatening.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth asserted that defendants tied up a neighbor girl and the female defendant's three daughters, taped their mouths, made them watch pornographic films and perform oral sex, and anally sodomized and raped them. At the time of trial, the female defendant's conviction for murdering her husband was on appeal. At trial, two of the daughters testified that defendants told them that if they did not do as told, they would kill them like they did their father. The court affirmed the trial court's convictions and sentences. Admitting defendants' statements to the girls was proper because it was a nonhearsay use of extrajudicial statements. Objection to the Commonwealth's cross-examination of the male defendant on the murder of the female defendant's husband was properly overruled because his counsel opened the door to the issue on direct examination. Conflicting physician testimony on physical signs of sexual abuse was sufficient to support the rape and sodomy convictions because it was consistent with the girls' testimony of slight penetration. The court remanded the action because a jury instruction on concurrent and consecutive sentencing was meant for only two offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences. The court reversed that part of the judgment that ordered the sentences to run consecutively. The court remanded to enter sentences that ran concurrently.

 

110 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Corey


92-SC-85-TG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


826 S.W.2d 319; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 46



March 12, 1992, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 24, 1992.
Post-conviction relief denied at Moore-Baker v. Commonwealth, 2012 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 508 (Ky. Ct. App., July 27, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 92-CA-000222. (Jefferson Circuit Court No. 91-CR-1421)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth sought review of an interlocutory order of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which directed that defendants be allowed to enter Alford pleas on all counts.


OVERVIEW: Prior to trial and not in response to any plea negotiations between the commonwealth and defendants, the trial court sua sponte entered an order directing that defendants be allowed to enter Alford pleas to all counts. The trial court further proposed that if death or life without parole was required at the sentencing phase, defendants would be allowed to withdraw their pleas of guilty and proceed to trial by jury. On appeal of the order by the commonwealth, the court reversed. The trial court's order was outside the limitations placed upon it prior to receipt of evidence and return of a verdict. Without consent of the commonwealth, a trial court could not amend or reduce to a lower degree the charge brought against a defendant and it was not the prerogative of the court to choose what the accusation would be. A plea agreement was required to be between a defendant and the commonwealth's attorney.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that directed that defendants be allowed to enter Alford pleas on all counts.

 

111 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Commonwealth


91-SC-270-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


830 S.W.2d 877; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 47



March 12, 1992, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 25, 1992. Released for Publication June 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 89-CA-2684-MR. PULASKI CIRCUIT COURT. HON. DANIEL J. VENTERS, JUDGE. 89-CR-127



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed appellant's conviction for second-degree manslaughter of a baby who was delivered and died after appellant's car collided with another vehicle driven by a pregnant woman. Appellant contended that the baby was not a person under Ky. Rev. Stat. § 507.040 and that the statute was void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: While appellant was driving under the influence of alcohol, he collided with another vehicle driven by a pregnant woman. The baby was delivered after the accident and died 15 hours later from prenatal injuries sustained in the accident. Appellant pled guilty to second-degree manslaughter. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the baby was a person to which Ky. Rev. Stat. § 507.040, the second-degree manslaughter statute, applied. The court found that defendant could not rely on caselaw in which the court had held that a criminal assault upon a pregnant mother, causing the death of a fetus, could not support a murder conviction. The court found that the critical difference in defendant's case was that the baby was born alive and died subsequently. The court rejected appellant's argument that some intentional or reckless act subsequent to the child's birth was required in order to sustain a conviction for criminal homicide. The court also held that the void-for-vagueness doctrine did not apply to § 507.040 because the conduct prohibited by the statute was clear.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for second-degree manslaughter. The court held that the baby who was killed was considered a person under the manslaughter statute because she was born alive and died 15 hours later. The court also held that the statute was not void for vagueness because it was clear in the conduct that it prohibited.

 

112 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Boone v. Commonwealth


90-SC-235-MR


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


821 S.W.2d 813; 1992 Ky. LEXIS 7



January 16, 1992, Rendered*1


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HON. J.W. "BILL" GRAVES, JUDGE. 87-CR-150



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence for first-degree sodomy and first-degree sexual abuse entered after a second sentencing hearing by the McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky) on the ground that the trial court committed reversible error. Defendant further argued that upon remand for a third sentencing hearing, the new jury should only hear evidence as to those matters specifically itemized in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055(2)(a), (b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree sodomy and first-degree sexual abuse. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions but set aside the sentence. On remand, the trial court imposed a second sentence. Defendant appealed, alleging that the trial court committed reversible error during the second hearing. The state conceded the error. The court vacated the second sentence and remanded for a third sentencing hearing. Defendant argued that the new jury should only be allowed to hear evidence as to those matters specifically set forth in § 532.055(2)(a),(b). The court rejected such argument, holding that § 532.055(2)(a),(b) was drafted to cover the normal bifurcated trial where the guilt and punishment phases followed in close proximity. Because in defendant's case a later punishment phase was needed due to reversible error committed only in that phase, the jury had to be informed of what transpired in the guilt phase in order to avoid imposing a sentence in a vacuum. The court then outlined issues for a punishment phase jury to consider in addition to those items listed in § 532.055(2)(a),(b), including jury instructions at the guilt phase and the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order imposing sentence on defendant during the second sentencing hearing and remanded to the trial court for resentencing as to defendant's convictions for first-degree sodomy and first-degree sexual assault, pursuant to the procedures outlined in the court's opinion.

Miles v. Dawson


90-SC-605-DG, 91-SC-007-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


830 S.W.2d 368; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 191



December 19, 1991, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. 88-CA-2743-MR. JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT 86-CI-9083. HON. JOSEPH E. ECKERT, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSING, VACATING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner filed an appeal from the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed the decision of the trial court in denying the landowner the right to repurchase previously condemned property pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 416.670.


OVERVIEW: The landowner previously owned a 15-acre tract of land that was condemned by appellee state for use in improving a road. She was compensated for the land, and title was conveyed to the state. There was a change in the state's plans and only 69 percent of the acreage was actually used. The landowner wanted to repurchase the unused portion of the property which was adjacent to her other property. The state refused, and stated that it intended to convey the unused portion to a church as part of an agreed settlement in another condemnation case which involved the church. The landowner sought a declaration of rights and the trial court dismissed the action by summary judgment without opinion. The appeals court affirmed, and the landowner challenged the decision. The court reversed the decision and held that the denial of the repurchase request was based entirely on the theory of convenience to the state in settling other litigation with a church. The court concluded that mere convenience was not a sufficient justification for the condemning authority to act as a land broker for private interests.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court, which affirmed the decision of the trial court in denying the landowner the right to repurchase previously condemned property.

 

114 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Caretenders, Inc. v. Commonwealth


90-SC-000813-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


821 S.W.2d 83; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 192



December 19, 1991, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released For Publication January 9, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 89-CA-1432-MR. (Nelson Circuit Court No. 88-CR-000013)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a home health care corporation, appealed a judgment of the Kentucky Court of Appeals, which affirmed its conviction of violations of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 209.990(2). The trial court found that defendant and its agents knowingly and willfully neglected an adult patient, which caused her mental and/or physical injury or permanent disability. The trial court acquitted defendant's agents named in the indictment.


OVERVIEW: The patient's family contracted with defendant to provide home health care services on a live-in basis. The patient developed serious bedsores and showed signs of poor hygiene and nutrition. The commonwealth indicted defendant and three of its nurses who took care of the patient. The court affirmed. The court found that defendant provided services for the patient and was a caretaker as defined by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 209.020(6). As a result, defendant was subject to liability under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 209.020(2). The court found that defendant's agents included the nurses named in the indictment and the live-in aides who were not named. The court held that because the majority of the patient's care was provided by the live-in aides, there was no inconsistency in the verdict, which found the corporate defendant guilty and acquitted the nurses. The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 290.990(2) and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 209.020 were not unconstitutionally vague and overbroad because they provided adequate warning to ordinary persons of the prohibited conduct and were sufficient guides to discourage arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appeals court which affirmed defendant's conviction of knowing and willful neglect of an adult patient.

 

115 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Puckett v. Miller


90-SC-662-DG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


821 S.W.2d 791; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 194



December 19, 1991, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released For Publication January 9, 1992. As Amended January 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. NO. 89-CA-1735-MR. (FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT NO. 84-CI-392)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART AND REVERSING IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff officers brought an action for a declaratory judgment challenging six regulations, alleging that the regulations violated Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 85.015 and 61.310(4), and the Fourteenth Amendment to the Constitution of the United States. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) found no violation. The officers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The regulations at issue restricted the rights of the officers to engage in off-duty employment. The officers argued that the statutes guaranteed the officers the right to engage in any endeavor enjoyed by all other citizens of the city in which they resided. The court noted the general rule that the rights of public employees could have been abridged in the interest of preventing conflicts with official duties. The court reasoned that the prevention of conflicts of interest and promoting community respect for police officers was at the heart of the regulations adopted. Therefore, the regulations prohibiting employment in establishments engaged primarily in the sale of alcoholic beverages and employment on behalf of individuals with reputations for involvement in criminal activity. The regulations also survived the officer's constitutional challenge because the police department had a rational basis for the regulations related to a legitimate objective. However, the regulation requiring the approval of the Chief of Police of off-duty employment was a grant of arbitrary power and was invalidated by the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the regulations with the exception of the regulation that required the Chief of Police to approve of off-duty employment.
