Barrett v. Reynolds


No. 90-SC-656-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


817 S.W.2d 439; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 146



September 26, 1991, Rendered


NOTICE:  [**1] Released For Publication November 21, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 21, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from Court of Appeals; No. 89-CA-000536; (Owsley Circuit Court No. 87-CI-027).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING THE COURT OF APPEALS' OPINION


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) affirmed the judgments of the trial court for appellee taxpayers and awarded them costs and fees in their action for declaratory and injunctive relief under KY. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.040 against appellants, state and its employees, alleging that the property valuation methods used in the assessment of their property taxes were unconstitutional. The state and its employees appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1986, the revenue department ordered the property valuation administrator to increase property values based on its latest appraisal study. Due to an earlier fire, which destroyed the maps of the area, the affected area was being remapped and only the newly mapped areas were assessed with the increase. The taxpayers filed suit for declaratory and injunctive relief under KY. Rev. Stat. Ann. §418.040, alleging that the method of valuation of the property was unconstitutional. The trial court entered judgment in the taxpayers' favor and the appellate court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed, adopting the appellate court's opinion, which found that the property valuation administrator used an impermissible mathematical formula in her valuation of the property. The court found that the taxpayers had not been required to exhaust their administrative remedies before bringing suit and that the suit was not barred by the two-year statute of limitations found in KY. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590(6). The court also found that by taxing only some property, the state violated KY. Const. §§ 171-174, which required a uniform and equitable tax rate for all classes of property in the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the affirmance of the trial court's judgments, which found that the method of property valuation was unconstitutional and awarded the taxpayers costs and attorney's fees.

Kentucky Ass'n of Realtors, Inc. v. Musselman


Nos. 90-SC-664-TG, 90-SC-665-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


817 S.W.2d 213; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 109



August 29, 1991, Rendered


NOTICE:  [**1] Released For Publication November 21, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal form Jefferson Circuit Court; Hon. Olga S. Peers, Judge; No. 89-CI-5160.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon a transfer to the court, appellants, realtor association and attorney general, sought review of a judgment by the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which declared unconstitutional so much of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 324.281 that required the governor to appoint to the real estate commission real estate agents from the list supplied by the association.


OVERVIEW: Appellee real estate agent sought to have a portion of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 324.281 declared unconstitutional. The trial court entered judgment on the pleadings declaring unconstitutional so much of § 324.281 as required the governor to appoint agents from the list supplied by the association. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court held that § 324.281 did not violate the state constitution. The court found that § 324.281 limited the power of the governor to appoint two names on a list provided by the association, but it neither limited appointees to members of the association nor compelled the governor to appoint someone on the list. The court reasoned that § 324.281 did not give the general assembly a voice in the selection of the committee members for the real estate commission but only provided a method of selection with reasonable criteria to generate commission members qualified for the position through the participation of the association.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which declared part of the real estate appointment statute unconstitutional.

Snodgrass v. Commonwealth

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order by the Daviess Circuit Court (Kentucky), which denied defendant's motion for continuance the morning of trial and convicted defendant of sodomy and other acts of sexual misconduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sodomy and other acts of sexual misconduct. Defendant was provided with a public defender. The afternoon before trial, defendant advised the public defender that he wished to retain private counsel. The morning of trial, the public defender filed a motion for continuance for defendant to employ private counsel. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied the motion for continuance because of four previous continuances by agreement of counsel. The court held that the public defender effectively and competently assisted defendant during trial. The court also held that matters that concerned parole eligibility should not be explored until the penalty phase of the bifurcated trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denial of defendant's motion for continuance the morning of trial.

Brown v. Commonwealth


No. 90-SC-111-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


818 S.W.2d 600; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 75



June 6, 1991, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 19, 1991. Released for Publication December 19, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from Court of Appeals; No. 89-CA-000225; Jefferson Circuit Court No. 88-CR-001544.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed a judgment of a trial court that found defendant guilty of theft by deception and gave defendant a sentence of two and one-half years on that charge. A jury then found defendant guilty of being a persistent felony offender in the first degree (PFOI), convicted on two prior nonviolent property-related offenses, and fixed the sentence at 10 years.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the 10 year sentence on the PFOI conviction was so grossly disproportionate to the theft by deception crime that it was manifestly unfair and constituted cruel and inhuman punishment in violation of the federal and state constitutions. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that a test was satisfied in that: (1) the 10 year sentence for repeated property-related offenses fit the gravity and harshness of the offense where the sentence was 10 years less than the 20 year maximum allowed under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.080(6)(b); (2) defendant's sentence was similar to sentences imposed on other persistent nonviolent, property-related felony offenders in the commonwealth under § 532.080(6)(b); and (3) a sentence in a case in another jurisdiction imposed for the same crime was squarely on point. Further, the court, in a case where the facts were nearly identical to the present facts, had addressed the same constitutional issue and concluded that the sentence in the present case was not manifestly unfair or unconstitutional. Last, no alternative sentencing plan applied where the court found § 532.080(7) controlling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of a court of appeals, which affirmed a judgment of the trial court that found defendant guilty of theft by deception. Defendant's 2 1/2 year sentence was enhanced to 10 years on a conviction as a persistent felony offender in the first degree.

Williams v. Commonwealth


No. 89-SC-323-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


810 S.W.2d 511; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 77



June 6, 1991, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 27, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from McCracken Circuit Court; Honorable James R. Daniels, Judge; No. 88-CR-222.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART/REVERSING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted him of first-degree rape, first-degree robbery, and first-degree burglary. Defendant was sentenced to 20 years in prison on each count, with the sentences to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed and raped an elderly woman. Police obtained a fingerprint from a soap box he had handled, which proved to be a match with his fingerprint card. The victim identified defendant from mug shot photograph books. Both the mug shot photograph and fingerprint card were introduced into evidence at the trial after defendant testified. Defendant contended that they prejudiced him by allowing the jury to infer that he had a criminal history. The court held that: (1) the Commonwealth needed to utilize the mug shot to confirm the victim's identification of defendant, but concealed all identifying information; (2) following the introduction of the mug shot into evidence, the court admonished the jury as to its limited relevance; and, (3) the trial court committed no prejudicial error with regard to the introduction of the mug shot and fingerprint card. However, the court found prejudicial error in the trial court's prevention of defendant from introducing his prior misdemeanor convictions because, under the Kentucky Truth in Sentencing statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. § 532.055, either party should have been permitted to introduce such evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's convictions of defendant for first-degree rape, first-degree robbery, and first-degree burglary; however, it vacated his sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing.

Perkins v. Northeastern Log Homes


No. 90-SC-738-CL


Supreme Court of Kentucky


808 S.W.2d 809; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 44; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,000



 May 9, 1991, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from United States District Court, Western District of Kentucky; Eugene E. Siler, Jr., Judge; Civil Action No. C8-90-0564LS.



DISPOSITION: CERTIFICATION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners filed a product liability action against appellees, log home kit seller, preservative designer, and manufacturer. The United States District Court for the Western District of Kentucky certified the following questions: 1) whether Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.135 violated Ky. Const. §§ 14, 54, 59, and/or 241; and 2) whether Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.135 applied to latent disease cases and when the limitations statute commenced.


OVERVIEW: A homeowner discovered that she had non-Hodgkin's lymphoma in 1986, several years after constructing her log home. The disease allegedly was caused by her continued exposure to chemicals contained in the wood preservative used in the logs. The homeowners challenged the constitutionality of § 413.135, which protected builders and others engaged in the design, planning, supervision, inspection, or construction of any improvement to real property from suit for damages, personal injury or wrongful death, five years after the substantial completion of such improvement. The court held that the statute was constitutionally defective as special legislation and violative of Ky. Const. §§ 14, 54, and 241. The court ruled that the statute could not bar the homeowners' action and deny constitutionally protected rights in Kentucky. The court specifically overruled Carney v. Moody, 646 S.W.2d 40 (1983), Fireman's Fund Ins. v. Government Emp. Ins., 635 S.W.2d 475 (1982), and Brown v. Neel, 798 S.W.2d 690 (1990). Under the discovery rule, an action accrued when the homeowner discovered that not only was she injured but that the injury may have been caused by another's conduct.


OUTCOME: The court held that the applicable Kentucky statute of repose violated the Kentucky Constitution, and that in latent disease cases, causes of action accrued when the plaintiff knew or should have discovered that she was injured and that her injury may have been caused by the conduct of defendant.

 

122 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Hacker v. Baesler


No. 89-SC-979-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


812 S.W.2d 706; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 45



May 9, 1991, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified August 29, 1991. Rehearing Denied August 29, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ky. LEXIS 130. Released for Publication August 29, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Review from Court of Appeals; 88-CA-2152-MR; Fayette Circuit Court No. 87-CI-1311.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), that affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which upheld appellee city mayor's veto of appellee city counsel's adoption of a proposed zoning amendment submitted by the landowners. The landowners argued that the city counsel's adoption of the zoning amendment was not subject to the mayor's veto.


OVERVIEW: The landowners sought an amendment to the local zoning plan from the zoning commission; although denied, the city counsel reversed the commission and adopted the proposed amendment. This action was in turn vetoed by appellee city mayor. Both the circuit court and the intermediate appellate court ruled against the landowners who argued the mayor did not have such veto power. On review the court held the city charter, giving the mayor the right to veto proposed ordinances, did not apply. A rezoning ordinance was not a general law subject to executive veto, but an adjudicatory decision that affected individual property rights. As such, it was subject to due process and judicial review and had to be based on substantial evidence. The court held that once a proponent of a zoning amendment prevailed before the local legislative body pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 100.211(1), the state constitution did not permit a peremptory mayoral veto. The court held that the veto power was inconsistent with constitutional guarantees of due process and equal protection, and that no local charter could grant mayoral power forbidden by the state constitution and state statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court and remanded the matter to the circuit court for entry of a new judgment. The court held that the state's constitution and statutes did not permit the city mayor to veto the adoption of the landowners' proposed zoning amendment because the process was not a legislative action subject to executive veto, but an adjudicatory action entitled to constitutional protection.

Louisville v. Louisville Professional Firefighters Assn., Local Union No. 345


No. 89-SC-441-D


Supreme Court of Kentucky


813 S.W.2d 804; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 47; 138 L.R.R.M. 2816



May 9, 1991, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 26, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From Court of Appeals; 88-CA-1208; Jefferson Circuit Court; Hon. Martin E. Johnstone, Judge; 87-CI-4911.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed the judgment of the lower court, dismissed the city's claim against appellee union, and remanded the issue of whether the city committed an unfair labor practice to the State Labor Relations Board (board).


OVERVIEW: The city challenged the constitutionality of Kans. Rev. Stat. ch. 345 and argued that it was not barred under the doctrines of res judicata and waiver from raising the issue of the applicability of chapter 345. The city also argued that the board acted arbitrarily and capriciously. The court found that the parties and the subject matter in the present action and a previous circuit court action were the same. The subject matter in both actions from the viewpoint of the union was whether the city had committed an unfair labor practice by its unilateral implementation of a third shift in the schedule of the arson squad. The only change in the two cases was the position of the city. Despite the dismissal of a claim without prejudice, the litigation was barred under the principles of res judicata and collateral estoppel because it made a final resolution of the question whether chapter 345 applied to the parties' dispute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the claims of the city as barred.

Nucor Corp. v. General Electric Co.


Nos. 89-SC-802-DG, 90-SC-208-DG, 90-SC-209-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


812 S.W.2d 136; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 54



May 9, 1991, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 29, 1991. Rehearing Denied August 29, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Review from Court of Appeals; Nos. 87-CA-809 and 87-CA-810; Jefferson Circuit Court No. 79-CI-1275.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART/REVERSING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, contractor, supplier and manufacturer, sought review of a decision from the Kentucky Court of Appeals reversing a trial court decision and reinstating a jury award of prejudgment interest on appellee corporation's claims for negligence, breach of warranty and strict liability in tort for a defective product; and appellee cross-appealed the decision striking the award made under the breach of contract theory.


OVERVIEW: Appellee corporation filed suit against appellants, contractor, supplier and manufacturer, alleging theories of liability in negligence, breach of warranty and strict liability in tort for defective joist girders that caused the collapse of a roof in one of appellee's warehouse. The court reversed the appellate court's decision and affirmed the trial court's conclusion that the responsibility for deciding whether to award prejudgment interest was one for the court and not the jury. The court concluded appellee could not collect a jury award of some $ 1.5 million in prejudgment interest because the trial court had concluded that appellee did not assert a claim for prejudgment interest until late in the trial, had refused appellant's settlement offers, and reasoned the ten-year delay in the case was not attributable to appellants. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting the pleadings to be amended to assert a breach of contract claim after the breach of warranty claim was barred by a four-year statute of limitations. The court found the amendment was necessary under Ky. R. Civ. P. 15.02 to cause the pleadings to conform to the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court and held the responsibility for deciding whether to award prejudgment interest was one for the court and not the jury. The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting the pleadings to be amended to assert a breach of contract claim in order to conform with the proof and the decision striking the award under the breach of contract claim was reversed.

Calvert Invest., Inc. v. Louisville & Jefferson County Metro. Sewer Dist.


Nos. 90-SC-191-DG, 90-SC-198-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


805 S.W.2d 133; 1991 Ky. LEXIS 17



March 14, 1991, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Review from Court of Appeals; No. 88-CA-2295; Jefferson Circuit Court No. 87-CI-10070. On Review from Court of Appeals; No. 88-CA-2295; Jefferson Circuit Court No. 87-CI-10070.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART/REVERSING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sewage facility owner appealed a decision from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) affirming the dismissal of its tortious interference with business interests and tortious interference with contract claims against defendant metropolitan sewer district and defendant state environmental protection agency on grounds of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The sewage facility owner contended that the metropolitan sewer district was not protected by sovereign immunity, and that, as to the state environmental protection agency, sovereign immunity protection did not apply to intentional torts. The supreme court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the claims against the state environmental protection agency, but reversed the trial court's dismissal of the claims against the metropolitan sewer district. Case law had defined the metropolitan sewer district as a municipal corporation and, therefore, it did not qualify for sovereign immunity under Kentucky law. However, sovereign immunity protection, where applicable, applied to both intentional and unintentional torts.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

Commonwealth v. Foley


No. 89-SC-646-TR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


798 S.W.2d 947; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 121



November 8, 1990, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 27, 1990. Released for Publication December 27, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Garrard Circuit Court; Hon. Robert J. Jackson, Judge; No. 89-CR-28.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth of Kentucky sought review of the decision of the Garrard Circuit Court (Kentucky), which dismissed the indictment against defendants on the grounds that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 119.205 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted for conspiracy to pay money to procure or influence a vote in violation of § 119.205. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the indictment on the grounds that § 119.205 was vague, overbroad, and thus, unconstitutional. The court stated that it would not have been unreasonable to interpret § 119.205 to prohibit the use of any money or thing of value with the intent to influence voters. The court found that such an interpretation was absurd and repugnant to the concept of free elections because the singular purpose of an election campaign was for the influencing of voters. The court articulated the standard for analyzing a statute for unconstitutional vagueness as whether a person disposed to obey the law could have determined with reasonable certainty from the language used whether the contemplated conduct would have amounted to a violation. The court found that the language of § 119.205 was so indefinite that it failed to meet the required standard. The court held that the statute was so broad and subject to such a vast array of interpretations that it failed on due process and equal protection grounds. The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court dismissing defendants' indictment.

Revenue Cabinet, Commonwealth v. Cherry


No. 90-SC-131-I


Supreme Court of Kentucky


803 S.W.2d 570; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 110



November 8, 1990, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Review From Court of Appeals; 89-CA-2651; Jefferson Circuit Court No. 89-CI-7960.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner revenue cabinet brought a motion pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 65.09 to dissolve a protective order issued by the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky). The order quashed a summons commanding respondent taxpayers to produce invoices and various bank financing documents.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers thought a summons issued by the revenue cabinet was oppressive. Instead of responding to the summons, they sought to have declared unconstitutional the revenue cabinet's attempt to assess and collect sales and use taxes from them on various grounds. Their complaint attacked the tax collection effort as unconstitutionally selective, discriminatory, and arbitrary and challenged the use of the administrative summons. As part of their lawsuit they sought a protective order. The trial court granted the order and quashed the summons. The revenue cabinet brought a Ky. R. Civ. P. 65.07 motion in the court of appeals seeking to have the protective order dissolved. The court of appeals denied the motion. The revenue cabinet then brought a motion pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 65.09. The taxpayers stated that the issue was only their right to require the revenue cabinet to seek a court order rather than proceeding by administrative summons. The court denied the motion and held that given this understanding of the trial court's protective order, Rule 65.09 did not apply. Nor did the authority of the trial court transgress the authority under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. 131.130(2).


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion of the revenue cabinet to dissolve a protective order that quashed a summons commanding the taxpayers to produce invoices and various bank financing documents.

Prestonia Area Neighborhood Ass'n v. Abramson


Nos. 90-SC-548-TG, 90-SC-556-I


Supreme Court of Kentucky


797 S.W.2d 708; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 100



October 18, 1990, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from Court of Appeals; No. 90-CA-000423; Jefferson Circuit Court No. 89-CI-004743.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighborhood associations sought review of a judgment in the Jefferson Circuit Court, Twelfth Division (Kentucky), which declared appellee city's ordinances under the Urban Renewal and Community Development Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 99.330 to 99.510, were constitutional. The ordinances declared three neighborhoods to be blighted and approved plans for urban renewal and citizen relocation.


OVERVIEW: Appellees won a declaratory judgment that the ordinances at issue, all identical in form, were constitutional. The ordinances declared the Prestonia, Highland Park and Standiford neighborhoods to be blighted, approved an urban renewal plan for each neighborhood, and approved a relocation plan for families and businesses displaced by the projects in favor of airport expansion. The record showed that only five to fifteen percent of the land in two neighborhoods and none of one neighborhood was necessary for the expansion of the airport's commercial zone. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and found the ordinances unconstitutional because the neighborhoods were already developed for predominantly housing uses, most of which were not substandard, and the neighborhoods were not "predominated" by blight. The court found a lack of substantial evidence to support the declaration of blight in the ordinances, and found those declarations to be violative of the Kentucky Constitution. The case was remanded to the trial court for entry of a judgment based on the court's decision and issuance of an injunction prohibiting any further actions under the ordinances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and declared the ordinances unconstitutional, invalid, and void. The case was remanded to the trial court for entry of a judgment declaring the ordinances unconstitutional and for issuance of a permanent injunction to prevent demolition, destruction or other acts under the voided ordinances.

 

130 of 908 DOCUMENTS


McCollum v. Sisters of Charity of Nazareth Health Corp.


Nos. 89-SC-63-DG, 89-SC-229-TG, 89-SC-234-TG, 89-SC-238-TG, 89-SC-251-TG, 89-SC-293-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


799 S.W.2d 15; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 98



October 18, 1990, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 27, 1990; No. 89-SC-238-TG, Petition for Rehearing Denied, December 27, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from Court of Appeals; No. 87-CA-000984; Fayette Circuit Court No. 86-CI-003485.

Appeal from Laurel Circuit Court; Honorable Charles R. Luker, Judge; Nos. 88-CI-000186, 88-CI-000600, 88-CI-000498, 88-CI-000413, 88-CI-000460.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In six consolidated appeals from two Circuit Courts of Appeals (Kentucky), which involved medical malpractice or wrongful death actions, the lower courts dismissed the actions under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.140(2) because they were time barred. The appeals court affirmed the medical malpractice judgment, and the court granted transfer of the five wrongful death cases for its consolidated review.


OVERVIEW: Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.410(2) provided that a claim against a hospital or medical personnel could not be filed more than five years from the date on which the negligent act or omission occurred. The court held that the provision was a statute of repose, not of limitation, and that it was unconstitutional because it violated the open court provisions of Ky. Const. § 14, Ky. Const. § 54, and Ky. Const. § 241. The constitutional provisions prohibited the diminution of legal remedies, such as the medical malpractice and wrongful death actions, which existed when the Constitution was adopted. The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.410(2) prevented the party with the malpractice action from bringing the action because he could not have not have discovered the injury until after the five year period. Thus, the statutory provision was unconstitutional. In regard to the remaining cases, the estates whose decedents had been murdered by a hospital physician who was later convicted, the court held that the deaths put the estates on notice to investigate, unless the hospital took steps to conceal relevant facts from them. The issue of concealment was held to be a jury question.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court appeals interest in the malpractice action and of the circuit court in the five remaining actions. All cases were referred to their originating courts for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Cummins v. Cox


No. 89-SC-662-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


799 S.W.2d 5; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 94



September 27, 1990, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified December 27, 1990. Rehearing Denied December 27, 1990; Reported at 1990 Ky. LEXIS 148. Released for Publication December 27, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Review from Court of Appeals; No. 87-CA-1317-MR; Franklin Circuit Court No. 86-CI-1438.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant mother, individually and as the administratrix of her son's estate, challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed a judgment of the circuit court denying appellee biological father the right to file an action for wrongful death of his illegitimate son pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.130 or as a surviving parent in an action for loss of affection and companionship under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.135.


OVERVIEW: Several years after the parties' divorce, they had a son. No judicial determination of paternity was sought. The child was killed in a car accident as a teenager. The mother, as administratrix of his estate, brought a wrongful death action under § 411.130 and individually for loss of affection and companionship under § 411.135. The father brought an action under § 411.135. The actions were consolidated and the driver paid the policy limit of his insurance coverage. The mother then sought a declaration of rights claiming that as the surviving mother, she alone was entitled to recover and that the father could not inherit from his illegitimate child. The circuit court granted summary judgment to the mother. The appellate court reversed. On further appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the father had standing to bring a wrongful death action pursuant to §§ 411.130, 411.135 and to inherit from his illegitimate son. The court reasoned that a statute requiring that a child be legitimate in order to inherit had been determined to be violative of equal protection, and that the language of §§ 411.130, 411.135 did not distinguish between legitimate and illegitimate fathers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's reversal of the circuit court's grant of summary judgment to the mother in her action against the father seeking a declaration that she alone was entitled to recover for the son's wrongful death and to inherit from him.

Sanders v. Commonwealth


No. 87-SC-674-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


801 S.W.2d 665; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 93



September 27, 1990, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 14, 1991.
Writ of certiorari denied Sanders v. Kentucky, 502 U.S. 831, 112 S. Ct. 107, 116 L. Ed. 2d 76, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 4767 (1991)
Post-conviction relief denied at Sanders v. Commonwealth, 89 S.W.3d 380, 2002 Ky. LEXIS 136 (Ky., 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Sanders v. Commonwealth, 339 S.W.3d 427, 2011 Ky. LEXIS 82 (Ky., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by Sanders v. White, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20140 (E.D. Ky., Feb. 18, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Madison Circuit Court; Honorable William T. Jennings, Judge; No. 87-CR-018.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the Madison Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted him on two counts each of murder and robbery, and imposed a sentence of incarceration as well as a death sentence. Appellant contended, inter alia, that there were errors in evidentiary rulings, jury instructions were improper, that the prosecutor's comments were improper, and that the death sentence was unconstitutional and disproportionate.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two counts of robbery and two counts of murder, and sentenced to death, as well as to consecutive terms of imprisonment. Appellant raised many issues on appeal, all of which the court deemed meritless, and accordingly, affirmed the judgment and sentence. The court held that jurors who were unsuccessfully challenged by the defense did not deprive appellant of an impartial jury or due process of law, nor did any other procedures followed during jury selection. Further, that evidence of a prior crime was admissible to show appellant's intent, common scheme, or plan, photographs were admissible to prove that the crime occurred where appellant had pled not guilty, and expert testimony was admissible. The court held that comments by the prosecutor and objections to instructions, both at the guilt and sentencing phases of the trial, also lacked merit. The court held that the sentencing was done properly, and that claims as to the unconstitutionality and disproportionality of the sentence were without any basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for robbery and murder, and his sentences of imprisonment and death. The court found that the numerous arguments raised by appellant all lacked merit. The court held that jury selection was done in a manner that allowed a fair trial, that evidentiary rulings were not erroneous, comments by the prosecutor were acceptable, and that sentencing was conducted in a constitutional and fair manner.

Taylor v. Commonwealth


No. 86-SC-481-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


821 S.W.2d 72; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 159

Writ of certiorari denied Taylor v. Kentucky, 502 U.S. 1100, 117 L. Ed. 2d 428, 112 S. Ct. 1185, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 966 (1992)
Writ of certiorari denied Kentucky v. Taylor, 502 U.S. 1121, 117 L. Ed. 2d 475, 112 S. Ct. 1243, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 1196 (1992)
Post-conviction relief denied at Taylor v. Commonwealth, 63 S.W.3d 151, 2001 Ky. LEXIS 182 (Ky., 2001)
Subsequent appeal at Taylor v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 160 (Ky., May 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Fayette Circuit Court; 85-CR-334; on Change of Venue from Jefferson Circuit Court; 84-CR-1549; Hon. William E. McAnulty, Jr., Judge.
Taylor v. Commonwealth, 817 S.W.2d 891, 1990 Ky. LEXIS 81 (Ky., 1990)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state convicted defendant of two counts of murder, kidnapping and first-degree robbery and one count of first-degree sodomy in the Circuit Court for Fayette County (Kentucky). The trial court sentenced defendant to death on the murder and kidnapping convictions and prison terms on the other convictions. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial judge erred by admitting the co-defendant's statement into evidence at the defendant's trial. The court rejected this argument and noted that the statement met the trustworthiness requirement for admission of a statement against penal interest. Co-defendant was also unavailable within the meaning of Fed. R. Evid. 804(A) because he had a pending criminal appeal at the time he was called as a witness. Defendant also argued that the trial judge abused his discretion when he denied the defendant's second motion for a change of venue on the basis that the motion did not give the state reasonable notice. The court rejected the argument that the statute related to venue changes in criminal actions was unconstitutional because the trial judge indicated that it would have considered a second change if he discovered problems seating an impartial jury. The court did agree that the death sentences for the kidnapping convictions had to be vacated because they violated defendant's double jeopardy rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions but vacated the death sentences imposed for the kidnapping convictions and remanded for resentencing on the two kidnapping charges as Class A felonies.

Franklin v. Natural Resources & Environmental Protection Cabinet


Nos. 89-SC-303-DG, 89-SC-583-TG, 89-SC-442-DG, 89-SC-466-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


799 S.W.2d 1; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 75



September 6, 1990, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 27, 1990. Released for Publication December 27, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Review from the Court of Appeals; No. 87-CA-2602; Webster Circuit Court No. 87-CI-143.

Appeal from Franklin Circuit Court; Honorable William L. Graham, Judge; No. 88-CI-388.

On Review from the Court of Appeals; No. 87-CA-2436 and No. 88-CA-605; Franklin Circuit Court No. 87-CI-806.

Appeal from Franklin Circuit Court, Honorable Ray Corns, Judge, No. 86-CI-1661.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING COURT OF APPEALS. REVERSING FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. AFFIRMING COURT OF APPEALS. AFFIRMING FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth sought review of the judgments in favor of appellee mines rendered in several cases in the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which held that the portion of Ky. Admin. Regs. 405 § 7:090(4) that required the prepayment of fines and penalties before a formal appeal to the Natural Resources and Environmental Protection Cabinet of the Commonwealth of Kentucky could be perfected was void.


OVERVIEW: The mines were fined for violations of state law but they could not afford to pay the fines as required to perfect an appeal of the fines. The court held that Ky. Admin. Regs. 405 § 7:090(4) was void pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13A.120(2) because it modified and vitiated Kentucky law in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13A.120(1)(i). No law in Kentucky required the prepayment of fines as a precondition to a hearing. The court held that because the portion of Ky. Admin. Regs. 405 § 7:090(4), which required the prepayment of fines and penalties before a formal appeal could be perfected, was more stringent than the applicable federal law, the Federal Surface Mining Control and Reclamation Act of 1977, 30 U.S.C. S. § 1201 et seq., it was void pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §13A.120(1). The court held that the prepayment requirement of the regulation violated the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the federal and state constitutions because it denied a due process hearing solely on a mine's ability to pay the penalty that was accessed.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the lower court were affirmed.

Vessels v. Brown-Forman Distillers Corp.


Nos. 89-SC-421-D, 89-SC-479-WC, 89-SC-480-WC


Supreme Court of Kentucky


793 S.W.2d 795; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 24



March 15, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 6, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ky. LEXIS 83. As Modified September 6, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Review from Court of Appeals, 88-CA-2433-WC, Workers' Compensation Board No. 81-28724.



DISPOSITION: DENYING MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW (89-SC-421-D) REVERSING ON DIRECT APPEAL (89-SC-479-WC) DISMISSING ON CROSS-APPEAL (89-SC-480-WC)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, as the father and next friend of a deceased worker's grandchildren, sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) entered in favor of appellee employer in a workers' compensation action. The court of appeals reversed an award of the workers' compensation board, which found that the grandchildren were partially dependent upon their grandmother and allowed the grandchildren's claim for the continuation of benefits.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals found that the grandchildren were not dependent on their grandmother, and reversed the award of the board. On appeal, the court reversed the court of appeals' decision. The court held: (1) appellant could seek review of the court of appeals' decision as a matter of right because Ky. Const. § 115 provided that in all cases there shall be allowed as a matter of right at least one appeal to another court; (2) Ky. R. Civ. P. 76.25(12), which provided that review by the supreme court in workers' compensation cases was discretionary, was unconstitutional; and (3) the court of appeals acted in error when it treated the question of dependency as a matter of law contrary to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. 342.075(2) and when it substituted its judgment for the judgment of the board on questions of fact contrary to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.290; and (4) dependency was properly determined at the time of the accident, and not at the time of death.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's motion for discretionary review, dismissed the cross-appeal of the employer, reversed the decision of the court of appeals, and remanded to the board for enforcement of the workers' compensation award.

Harris v. Commonwealth


No. 88-SC-45-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


793 S.W.2d 802; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 25



March 15, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 6, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ky. LEXIS 80. As Modified September 6, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court, Honorable Joseph Eckert, Judge, No. 86-CR-0680.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted defendant of kidnapping, wanton murder, tampering with physical evidence, and abuse of a corpse. He was sentenced to life without the possibility of parole for 25 years for the kidnapping, life imprisonment for murder, 5 years for tampering, and 12 months and $ 500 for abuse of a corpse.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that a capital offense was neither alleged nor proved, with respect to kidnapping. First, defendant argued that the indictment did not specifically allege that the victim was not released alive, as required under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 509.040(2). The court held that, although correct, defendant was not misled by the indictment as to the penalty. The indictment stated that kidnapping was being charged as a capital offense. There was sufficient evidence for the jury to find that the victim was not released alive. Defendant also argued that his aggravated sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole for 25 years for kidnapping was erroneous because the jury did not find one of the aggravated circumstances enumerated in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.025(2)(a). The court held that the murder of the victim sufficed as an aggravated circumstance of the kidnapping. However, double jeopardy principals were not violated because the victim's death was not necessary to establish the offense of kidnapping under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 509.040 and because murder under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 509.020 did not required proof that the victim was restrained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions because the evidence was sufficient. The trial judge properly considered aggravating and mitigating circumstances in imposing the sentence recommended by the jury.

 

137 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Maney v. Mary Chiles Hosp.


No. 89-SC-144-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


785 S.W.2d 480; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 31



March 15, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, No. 87-CA-2305-S, MONTGOMERY CIRCUIT COURT NO. 87-CI-9070.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient brought an action against appellee physician. The physician filed a motion to dismiss based on Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.140(2). The patient alleged the statute was unconstitutional but did not inform the attorney general of the constitutional challenge. The trial court upheld the constitutionality and dismissed the complaint. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) dismissed the appeal. Discretionary review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The physician claimed that the failure of the patient to inform the attorney general that he was challenging the constitutionality of a statute as required in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.075 rendered the trial court's decision on the issue non-reviewable. The patient claimed that § 418.075 did not apply and that the physician waived any objection to the failure to notify the attorney general by failing to raise the issue in the trial court. The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and vacated the judgment of the trial court. There was a strong public policy in favor of notification to the attorney general whenever the constitutionality of a statute was placed in issue and the language of § 418.075 requiring notification was mandatory and required strict enforcement. It was clear that no judgment was to be entered which decided the constitutionality of a statute until the attorney general was given notice and an opportunity to be heard. Judgments entered in violation of the attorney general's notice statute were defective. The court applied the decision to cases currently pending and prospectively to avoid any effect on otherwise settled judgments.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals dismissing the appeal was set aside and the judgment of the trial court was vacated. The case was remanded to the trial court.

Rev. Stat. Ann. § 177.841(2), which regulated the placement of billboards, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The department filed two suits seeking a judgment declaring appellants' violations of § 177.841(2), but appellants challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The trial court struck the statute down as unconstitutional, but the appellate court reversed. Frederick v. Air Pollution Control Dist.


No. 89-SC-000038-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


783 S.W.2d 391; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 10; 20 ELR 20811



January 18, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, Nos. 87-CA-1403-MR, 87-CA-1456-MR, Jefferson Circuit Court No. 85-CI-3743.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county residents challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed a judgment entered by the trial court declaring part of the regulation created by appellees, the Air Pollution Control District of Jefferson County (district) and its director, unconstitutional but which affirmed the judgment that the regulation was not unconstitutional in its entirety.


OVERVIEW: The district promulgated a regulation creating a vehicle exhaust testing program. The trial court held that the regulation was constitutional except for a provision requiring payment of a mandatory testing fee. The district and its director appealed, and the county residents cross-appealed. The appellate court reversed and remanded on the direct appeal of the district and its director and affirmed on the cross-appeal. The court affirmed the finding that pursuant to the extensive power given to the district by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 77 to prevent and reduce air pollution, the district had the authority to create the testing program, and the regulation was a reasonable exercise of the district's power. The county residents' equal protection claims were without merit because the regulation's exemption of certain vehicles was rationally based and did not adversely affect the regulation's overall purpose. Finally, court reversed the finding that the mandatory testing fee was unconstitutional because the record showed that the amount of the fee was not excessive; it was the amount paid by the district for each test and an estimated minimal charge to cover administrative costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court, reversing and remanding the judgment of the trial court declaring that the mandatory fee requirement of the district's regulation was unconstitutional and affirming the judgment of the trial court that the regulation was not unconstitutional in its entirety.

Drumm v. Commonwealth


Nos. 87-SC-848-MR, 87-SC-849-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


783 S.W.2d 380; 1990 Ky. LEXIS 3



January 18, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM BULLITT CIRCUIT COURT, HON. OLGA S. PEERS, SPECIAL JUDGE, INDICTMENT NOS. 86-CR-065, 070 AND 073.

APPEAL FROM BULLITT CIRCUIT COURT, HON. OLGA S. PEERS, SPECIAL JUDGE, INDICTMENT NOS. 86-CR-066, 071 AND 074.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, father and mother, were indicted for sexually abusing their children. The Bullitt Circuit Court (Kentucky) entered judgments convicting and sentencing defendant father of first-degree rape and first-degree sodomy of his daughter, and first-degree sodomy of his son. Defendant mother was convicted and sentenced for the same offenses based on complicity. Both defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The major issue on both appeals was whether the admissibility of various out-of-court statements incriminating the defendants made by both children to various persons involved in their care and treatment after they were removed from defendants' home was proper. The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 421.355 was unconstitutional because it denied defendants fundamental rights of due process and confrontation by permitting their convictions based upon hearsay where no traditionally acceptable and applicable reasons for exceptions applied. The court adopted the application of Fed. R. Evid. 803(4) to cases involving the admissibility of statements made by the children to treating physicians. The court held that there was little doubt, once the commonwealth conceded the evidence regarding the hearsay statements made by the daughter was inadmissible, that the use of such evidence so seriously prejudiced the case involving the offenses charged as to the son, that the trial on these charges was fundamentally unfair, and a retrial was required as to both defendants.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions on all charges were reversed, and the case was remanded to the lower court for further consideration.

Boone v. Commonwealth


No. 88-SC-839-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


780 S.W.2d 615; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 107



November 30, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM McCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE LLOYD C. EMERY, II, JUDGE, No. 87-CR-150.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING AND REMANDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky), which held in favor of the state and convicted defendant of sodomy and sexual abuse. The circuit court denied defendant's motion to present evidence of parole eligibility pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the sentencing procedure of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055, which was followed by the circuit court. The circuit court denied defendant's motion to present evidence of parole eligibility as provided by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055(2)(a)1. The court affirmed the convictions and vacated and remanded the sentence. Kentucky was one of the few states that provided for jury sentencing. The court found that a bifurcated trial was a small price to pay for a better-informed sentencing process. The court endorsed the concept of an enlightened jury in its consideration and assessment of an appropriate penalty. However, the court agreed with defendant that to place the phase of the enlightenment solely in the hands of the prosecutor was a denial of due process to defendant or any other defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and vacated and remanded his sentence. The court held that refusing defendant's motion to introduce evidence of minimum parole eligibility and allowing the commonwealth to have sole control of the evidence was a denial of due process.

 

142 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Board of Trustees v. Hayse


Nos. 88-SC-283-DG, 88-SC-289-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


782 S.W.2d 609; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 99



November 9, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 8, 1990.
Writ of certiorari denied Hayse v. Board of Trustees of University of Kentucky, 497 U.S. 1025, 110 S. Ct. 3273, 111 L. Ed. 2d 783, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 3655 (1990)
Writ of certiorari denied Board of Trustees of University of Kentucky v. Hayse, 498 U.S. 938, 111 S. Ct. 341, 112 L. Ed. 2d 306, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 5568 (1990)
Related proceeding at Hayse v. Wethington, 110 F.3d 18, 1997 U.S. App. LEXIS 6423 (6th Cir.) (6th Cir. Ky., 1997)
Decision reached on appeal by Hayse v. Bd. of Trs. of the Univ. of Ky., 2008 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 732 (Ky. Ct. App., Aug. 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 86-CA-1826, FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 79-CI-437.

ON APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 86-CA-1902, FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT NO. 79-CI-437.
Hayse v. Board of Trustees, 1987 Ky. App. LEXIS 612 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 11, 1987)



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff professor brought an action against defendants, university and dean, for wrongful termination, reinstatement, and award of tenure. The Kentucky Court of Appeals reversed the trial court's grant of judgment notwithstanding the verdict, which was rendered for the professor, and on grounds of sovereign immunity sustained the result that denied monetary damages.


OVERVIEW: In this wrongful termination action the court found that neither the professor's constitutional claims nor his claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 were time barred. The cause began to run on the date the professor received rejection of his second tenure application. The judgment notwithstanding the verdict could not be sustained because the university had the burden of persuading the jury that the professor's termination was not based on consideration of impermissible factors, which the university failed to do. The court found that the doctrine of sovereign immunity was misapplied to shield the dean because he was sued for his personal wrongdoing for violating the professor's constitutionally protected rights, not for acts he did in serving in his official capacity. Although Ky. Const. § 231 could not bar litigants that sought prospective injunctive relief for violations of federally protected rights against state officials, the court found that to correct the procedural error of the administrative body, the appropriate relief was to remand the case to the administrative agency to decide the merits of the controversy. Thus, the professor was not entitled to reinstatement.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment notwithstanding the verdict, and reinstated the judgment for damages. The court vacated the separate judgment that denied injunctive relief against the university, and required the university consider the professor's tenure under the rules and regulations at the time tenure was denied to him.

 

143 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Hubbard


No. 88-SC-938-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


777 S.W.2d 882; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 69



 September 7, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS, 87-CA-2147, Clay Circuit Court #86-CR-107.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) that reversed defendant's conviction for reckless homicide, on the ground that defendant's Fifth Amendment due process rights were violated when the Commonwealth employed private counsel to assist in the prosecution, and reversed the sentence that was imposed by the circuit court, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055(4), after the jury failed to agree on a sentence.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of reckless homicide and the circuit court, after the jury could not agree on a sentence, sentenced defendant pursuant § 532.055(4) in excess of the minimum sentence but less than the maximum prescribed by statute. The appellate court reversed the conviction, ruling that the Commonwealth's employment of private counsel to assist the in the prosecution of a criminal case violated defendant's due process rights under the federal constitution. The appellate court reversed the sentence on the ground that § 532.055(4) also violated defendant's due process rights. On appeal, the court ruled: (1) the employment of private counsel to assist the Commonwealth attorney in the prosecution of a criminal case did not offend due process, because the Commonwealth attorney maintained control over the prosecution of the case, and; (2) § 532.055(4) did not violate due process because the action of the trial judge was the result of and expressly authorized by statute. The federal constitution did not, the court ruled, prohibit judicial sentencing when the jury failed to agree on a sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the sentence imposed by the circuit court and reversed the decision of the court of appeals.

Sweasy v. King's Daughters Memorial Hospital


No. 88-SC-592-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


771 S.W.2d 812; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 54



June 8, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ORIGINAL ACTION FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 88-CA-1061-OA.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband and wife, challenged a writ of prohibition that was granted by the Court of Appeals (Kentucky). The writ prevented the trial court, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 311.377 (1980), from ordering document production from appellee hospital in a medical negligence case. The husband and wife argued that Ky. Const. § 51 rendered the statute invalid.


OVERVIEW: A husband and wife brought a medical malpractice action against a hospital, among others, and sought discovery of peer review documents in its possession. The hospital claimed privilege under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 311.377 (1980). The court on appeal held that there was no privilege excusing production because the statute's enactment violated the single-subject rule for legislation contained in Ky. Const. § 51. The court noted that the only other plausible interpretation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 311.377(2) (1980) was that it was limited to suits against peer review entities themselves by the persons being reviewed. In either case, the court found that the hospital could not claim the benefit of any privilege from discovery. The court noted that the newer 1988 version of the statute was not before the court. The court further held that the trial judge was not an indispensable party to the original action for the requested writ of prohibition because he would be a party in name only, not a real party in interest.


OUTCOME: The court denied the hospital's motion to dismiss, vacated the writ of prohibition, and reinstituted the judgment of the trial court requiring production of the documents from the hospital.

 

145 of 908 DOCUMENTS


F.T.P. v. Courier-Journal


Nos. 89-SC-103-MR, 89-SC-126-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


774 S.W.2d 444; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 48; 16 Media L. Rep. 1921



June 8, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 7, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, NO. 88-CA-2190-OA, Jefferson Circuit Court No. 88XX0051.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING IN PART/REVERSING IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, challenged the order of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) that permitted appellees, a newspaper and its reporters, to attend and report juvenile proceedings at the appellate level. Appellees challenged the order denying them access to his juvenile court records.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth sought to transfer the juvenile's case from the juvenile session to the circuit court for a youthful offender trial. The transfer statute was declared unconstitutional. The newspaper filed a motion to intervene in the Commonwealth's appeal and for access to the record. The newspaper was permitted to intervene but was denied access to the record. Upon the juvenile's motion, the appeal hearings were closed. The court of appeals issued appellees' requested writ prohibiting the closing of the proceedings. The court reversed. Although Ky. Rev. Stat. § 600.020(12) defined "court" to mean only the juvenile session, it did not follow that the statute was inapplicable to juvenile proceedings on appeal to the circuit court. To exclude appellees at the district level, but admit them at the appellate level nullified the intent and purpose to protect the juvenile with a shroud of secrecy. If the case was successfully transferred to the circuit court, the juvenile would be stripped of the protection. The juvenile's right to a fair trial, and the public's interest in fostering opportunities for rehabilitation transcended appellees' right to instantaneous reporting.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that permitted appellees to attend and report juvenile proceedings at the appellate level. The court affirmed the order denying appellees' access to the juvenile's court records.

Carpenter v. Commonwealth


Nos. 87-SC-98-MR, 87-SC-114-TRG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


771 S.W.2d 822; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 56



June 8, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Carpenter v. Commonwealth, 2003 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 83 (Ky. Ct. App., Aug. 15, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM KENTON CIRCUIT COURT, HON. DOUGLAS M. STEPHENS, JUDGE, CRIMINAL ACTION No. 76-CR-163.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of their convictions on two counts of first-degree criminal abuse by the Kenton Circuit Court (Kentucky).


OVERVIEW: The questions presented on appeal were whether the evidence was insufficient, whether Ky. Rev. Stat. § 508.100 was unconstitutionally vague, and whether the instructions were improper. The court ruled that Kentucky's criminal abuse statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. § 508.100, was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness. The court reasoned that the principal question in such an inquiry was whether the statute gave suitable notice of prohibited conduct and the court found that it did. The court further held that defendants were not substantially prejudiced by the introduction of opinion testimony that the injuries to their child were intentionally caused. However, the court held that intent was an essential element in abuse cases and that failure to instruct was prejudicial error. As such, the court reversed and remanded for retrial as to one defendant but affirmed both counts of conviction as to the other defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both counts of conviction of one defendant and reversed and remanded for retrial as to the judgment of conviction of the other defendant in the case concerning first-degree criminal abuse.

Rose v. Council for Better Educ.


No. 88-SC-804-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


790 S.W.2d 186; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 55



June 8, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified September 28, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE RAY CORNS, JUDGE, 85-CI-1759.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING IN PART/REVERSING IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the state general assembly, appealed from the Franklin Circuit Court ( Kentucky) which found in favor of plaintiffs, students and local school districts, on plaintiffs' action for declaratory judgment and held that defendant had failed to comply with its constitutional mandate under Ky. Const. § 183 to provide an efficient system of common schools throughout the state.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, students and local school districts, filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant, the state general assembly in which plaintiffs alleged that defendant's system of school financing resulted in an inefficient system of common school education in violation of Ky. Const. § 183. The trial court agreed and declared the state's common school finance system to be unconstitutional and the system of common schools to be inefficient. On review, the court affirmed the holding that the state common school system was unconstitutional. The court held that when it considered the evidence in the record and applied the constitutional requirement of § 183 to the evidence, it was clear that defendant had fallen short of its duty to enact legislation to provide for an efficient system of common schools throughout the state because the system of common schools was underfunded and inadequate, it remained fraught with inequalities and inequities throughout the various school districts, it was ranked nationally lower in virtually every category that was used to evaluate educational performance, and it was not uniform among the districts in educational opportunities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling in favor of plaintiffs, students and local districts which declared that the state common school finance system of defendant, the state general assembly, was unconstitutional because the evidence clearly demonstrated that defendant had not met its state constitutional mandate to enact legislation that would provide for an efficient system of common schools throughout the state.

Palmore v. Jones


No. 88-SC-557-D


Supreme Court of Kentucky


774 S.W.2d 434; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 32



May 4, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 7, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 87-CA-1218-MR, PIKE CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE CHARLES LOWE, JR., JUDGE, 86-CI-1485.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state secretary of labor, sought review of a decision of the Kentucky Court of Appeals, which awarded a judgment in favor of appellee widow in the widow's action that sought a continuation of her deceased husband's workers' compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: The sole question presented on appeal was whether the widow, who had married a disabled worker, was entitled to a continuation of her deceased husband's disability benefits which were awarded prior to the marriage. The court held that the widow was entitled to a continuation of benefits. The court found that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.730(3) set out classes of persons entitled to a continuation of benefits and that benefits could be paid to persons within the class at the time of a worker's death. The widow was within an appropriate class and was fully entitled to the benefits provided by § 342.730(3). Pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.730(3)(a), the income benefits specified and unpaid at the worker's death, whether or not accrued or due at his death, were required to be paid to and for the benefit of the widow.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court, which awarded a judgment in favor of the widow.

University of Louisville v. O'Bannon


No. 87-SC-604-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


770 S.W.2d 215; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 12



February 9, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 8, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, NO. 87-CA-697-OA



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, university hospital and doctor, pleaded sovereign immunity and moved to dismiss appellee patient's medical malpractice action against them. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) denied appellants' petition seeking to prohibit the trial, and they sought review.


OVERVIEW: The patient and his wife commenced litigation against the university hospital and the doctor claiming improper administration of an antibiotic drug in connection with a puncture wound on the patient's left foot resulted in permanent ringing in his ears. The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44.072 did not provide a defense of sovereign immunity to either the hospital or the doctor, as it would not be applied retroactively. This claim already was pending on the effective date of the statute. The application of the legislative act to the facts in question would produce a retroactive limitation on the right of the patient to recover that did not exist at the time of the alleged negligence or at the time of the commencement of the suit. Consequently it would be an ex post facto act to prohibit the trial in this case. The sentence in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44.073(12) including the words "no action for damages may be maintained" in its entirety was simply a further explanation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44.073(11), which specified that the commonwealth did not intend by this statute to waive sovereign immunity or any other immunity or privilege except as otherwise provided.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed, and the matter was remanded to the circuit court to proceed with trial.

Remote Services, Inc. v. FDR Corp.

Supreme Court of Kentucky


764 S.W.2d 80; 1989 Ky. LEXIS 2; 1989-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P68,394



January 19, 1989, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants gasoline sellers challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals, Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) which reversed a trial court's grant of summary judgment against appellee gasoline seller and classified Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 365.030 as a trade practice measure, not a minimum mark-up law.


OVERVIEW: Appellee filed a complaint alleging that appellants had violated the provisions of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 365.030 by selling gasoline and gasoline products at less than cost for the purpose of injuring competitors and destroying competition. Appellants conceded that the allegation was true. The decision of the appeals court was reversed and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appeals court was reversed and the ruling of the trial court was affirmed because the court found that the statute in question was facially unconstitutional as being violative of the state constitution.

Huff v. Commonwealth


No. 87-SC-664-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


763 S.W.2d 106; 1988 Ky. LEXIS 77



November 17, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 9, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM HARLAN CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE CLARENCE A. CORNELIUS, JUDGE, No. 86-CR-104


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055, which described evidence relevant to sentencing which may have been presented to a jury after a finding of guilty and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 439.3401, which related to parole for violent offenders. After his challenge was denied in Harlan Circuit Court (Kentucky), he entered a conditional plea of guilty to a charge of murder.


OVERVIEW: With respect to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055, the court declared that statute unconstitutional because the United States Supreme Court required that the court at the sentencing state inform the jury of the nature of the sentence of imprisonment that could have been imposed, including its implication with respect to possible release upon parole, if the jury sentence was against sentence of death. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 439.3401 because it allowed for a possible disparity in sentencing in the minimum for parole eligibility. Defendant argued that, under the statutory scheme, one who received a sentence of 25 years or more had a minimum parole eligibility in excess of one who received a life sentence, which the layman considered to be a longer sentence. The court did not find that the minimum imposed by the legislature was arbitrary or capricious and explained that it was the uncertainty in life itself, not a declaration of minimum eligibility, which created the possible disparity. The court noted that the statute provided for a minimum period of parole eligibility and was only one factor to be considered in the granting of parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the lower court which held that the statutes challenged by defendant were not unconstitutional.

Griggs v. Dolan


No. 87-SC-886-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


759 S.W.2d 593; 1988 Ky. LEXIS 69



October 27, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, No. 86-CA-1472-MR, Fayette Circuit Court No. 84-CI-3728



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING AND REMANDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant class of taxpayers appealed from the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which affirmed the trial court's decision in the class's action against respondents, administrators, clerk, sheriff, board of education, and Department of Revenue of the Commonwealth of Kentucky (department) challenging the constitutionality of the method of assessment used by the administrators in determining ad valorem taxes.


OVERVIEW: The class filed a complaint seeking tax refunds and a declaration that their taxes were unconstitutionally assessed and collected. In a prior action, the court determined that the method of assessment for 1981 was unconstitutional. The board, which was not a party to the prior action, intervened. Respondents filed a motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim for relief. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss and the appellate court affirmed. On further appeal, the court reversed. Pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590(6), the class had two years from the finality date of the previous litigation in the case challenging the method of assessment in 1981to file their refund claims. The class members could not obtain refunds for 1981 school taxes because the board was not a party to the prior action and refund claims were not filed within two years pursuant to § 134.590(6). A new lawsuit was necessary before the board was bound by the prior decision as to the unconstitutionality of the 1981 taxes. A new action was also necessary to determine whether the same unconstitutional method of assessment was used in subsequent years.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court affirming the trial court's order that granted the motion to dismiss of respondents in the class's action for declaratory relief and tax refunds. The action was remanded for further proceedings.

Ellis v. Ellis


No. 87-SC-187-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


752 S.W.2d 781; 1988 Ky. LEXIS 47

DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant heirs at law sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals for Whitley Circuit Court (Kentucky) in favor of appellee illegitimate son, in a case where the illegitimate son sought a declaratory judgment that he was the decedent's illegitimate child and sole heir. The lower court reversed the decision of the trial court that dismissed the claim as barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Decedent died intestate and unmarried. Appellee illegitimate son commenced an action that asserted ownership by virtue of inheritance from the decedent. The court found that the claim for inheritance did not arise before the decedent's death. The one year limitations provisions of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 396.025 did not apply, and the failure of the heirs at law to bring the equitable claim that the action was barred by laches prevented that court hearing those claims. The heirs at law argued that as an adult, the illegitimate son had no claim for support and could not have sought to establish paternity in a bastardy proceeding under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 406, et seq. Likewise, he had no claim for inheritance since his putative father was still living, and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 391.090 absolutely prohibited inheritance by illegitimate children from their fathers. To hold, as appellants urged, that the claim was barred after his 21st birthday would result in barring his claim before it ever accrued. Such a result was impermissible.


OUTCOME: The Opinion of the Court of Appeals was affirmed.
