Gillis v. Yount


Nos. 87-SC-286-DG, 87-SC-288-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


748 S.W.2d 357; 1988 Ky. LEXIS 13; 100 Oil & Gas Rep. 645



March 3, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 85-CA-2662 & 2717-MR, Franklin Circuit Court Nos. 84-CI-815, 84-CI-867 & 85-CI-589.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant, Secretary of the Kentucky Revenue Cabinet, appealed the decision of the Kentucky Court of Appeals that affirmed the trial court' s decision that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.020, which classified and taxed unmined coal separately from other property, was not permitted by Ky. Const. § 170 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, property taxpayers and automobile excise taxpayers, filed an action challenging the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.020, which taxed unmined coal at a different rate than other real property. The trial court found the statute bestowed upon unmined coal, a real property interest, a de facto exemption from property taxation that was prohibited under Ky. Const. § 174. The court of appeals affirmed and the court affirmed. The court held that the ownership of unmined coal was classified as an interest in real estate, and as such was subject to real property taxes. Ky. Const. §§ 170-175 made it clear that all property was to be taxed uniformly and at its fair cash value unless exempted from the constitution. Ky. Const. § 170 made void all laws that attempted to exempt or omit other property not specifically exempted in the constitution. The court held that the special classification of unmined coal for special tax treatment that was different than other real estate interests was not permitted under the Kentucky Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals that affirmed the trial court's decision. The classification and taxation of unmined coal at a different rate than other real property interests was not constitutional under the Kentucky Constitution.

 

157 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Ballard v. Commonwealth


No. 87-SC-11-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


743 S.W.2d 21; 1988 Ky. LEXIS 6



January 21, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM BATH CIRCUIT COURT, HON. J. M. RICHARDSON, JUDGE, 85-CR-017.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a decision of the Bath Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted appellant of sexual abuse in the first degree, attempted rape in the first degree, and sodomy in the first degree, and sentenced appellant to 50 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court convicted appellant of sexual abuse in the first degree, attempted rape in the first degree, and sodomy in the first degree, and sentenced appellant to 50 years imprisonment. On appeal, the court held that the circuit court erred by prohibiting a defense witness from testifying without making the required determination under Ky. R. Crim. P. 9.48. Rule 9.48 required the circuit court to determine whether the violation of the rule was prejudicial under the facts and circumstances of the case. Automatic prohibition of testimony without such a determination amounted to an abuse of discretion. Further, the court, citing a prior decision, held that the trial court erred by allowing into evidence a videotape interview of the 10-year old complaining witness. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 421.350(2) unconstitutionally infringed on the inherent powers of the judiciary since it permitted testimony from a child who had not been determined competent as a witness by the trial court. In the case at bar, videotape testimony was heard without a determination of witness competency and without the taking of an oath. The court reversed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction with directions that he be granted a new trial.

Kirschner v. Louisville Gas & Electric Co.


No. 86-SC-1001-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


743 S.W.2d 840; 1988 Ky. LEXIS 10



January 21, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 85-CA-2129-MR, Jefferson Circuit Court - 83-CI-09667.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) affirmed the decision of the trial court, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant utility company in plaintiff injured party's action for injuries he received when he climbed a tower owned by the utility company. The injured party appealed.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was 15 years old, and although several children regularly played in the field where the tower was located, there was no evidence that other children had climbed the tower or that the utility company had notice of such activity. The trial court held that the injured party was a trespasser, and therefore, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 381.232, the utility company was not liable. The court held that § 381.232 did not violate Ky. Const. § 54 and that summary judgment was proper. The court held that the idea that the tower was an attractive nuisance because the utility company knew that children played in the field was not tenable. There was not an implied invitation, and their presence in the field under the tower was irrelevant. The court also held that the there was sufficient warning of the danger, and arcing was not considered to be a concealed dangerous condition under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals.

 

159 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Reneer


No. 85-SC-780-CL


Supreme Court of Kentucky


734 S.W.2d 794; 1987 Ky. LEXIS 232



August 6, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]


PRIOR HISTORY: ON MOTION FOR CERTIFICATION OF THE LAW, HONORABLE ROBERT M. SHORT, JUDGE, DAVIESS CIRCUIT COURT, No. 85-CR-221.



DISPOSITION:  CERTIFYING THE LAW


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: During defendant's criminal trial, the trial court found that provisions of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055 (1986) relating to bifurcated trials in felony cases unconstitutionally infringed on the court's power to prescribe rules of procedure. After defendant was found not guilty, the commonwealth sought certification from the court on the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055 (1986).


OVERVIEW: During defendant's criminal trial, the trial court found that provisions of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055 (1986) relating to bifurcated trials in felony cases unconstitutionally infringed on the court's power to prescribe rules of procedure. Although defendant was found not guilty, the court granted the commonwealth's request to certify the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055 (1986). The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055 (1986) was procedural in nature and that principles of comity allowed the court to tolerate a minor legislative intrusion on its power to regulate court procedure. Because the statute did not unreasonably interfere with judicial function, the court held that the unconstitutional intrusion was tolerable under comity principles. The court also held that it retained the paramount power to prescribe rules of judicial procedure, and could supersede the statute at any time if it became necessary.


OUTCOME: The court granted the commonwealth's request to certify the constitutionality of a criminal procedure statute. Under principles of comity, the unconstitutional legislative intrusion into the judicial power to regulate court procedure was tolerable because it was not an unreasonable intrusion and the court retained the power to override the statute at any time.

Akers v. Baldwin


Nos. 85-SC-392-CL, 85-SC-422-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


736 S.W.2d 294; 1987 Ky. LEXIS 230; 98 Oil & Gas Rep. 33; 26 ERC (BNA) 1643



July 2, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Corrected July 2, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: U.S. DISTRICT COURT EASTERN DISTRICT OF KENTUCKY NO. 84-88.

Appeal from Perry Circuit Court Honorable Calvin N. Manis, Judge 83-CI-429.



DISPOSITION:  Reversing and Remanding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Secretary of Natural Resources (secretary) and coal companies, sought review of the grant of an injunction by the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Kentucky which prevented the issuance of strip mine permits. In a second action, appellants, strip miners, sought review of a judgment from the Perry Circuit Court (Kentucky) that prevented them from strip mining on appellee surface owners' property.


OVERVIEW: In the first of two consolidated actions, surface owners' sought an injunction to prevent the secretary from issuing strip mining permits to strip miners who claimed the rights under a broad form deed. Several coal companies intervened and challenged the applicability of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 381.930-945 (1984). The lower court entered a preliminary injunction and certified the challenge of the statute for the court's review. The court certified the law and declared unconstitutional that portion of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 381.940 which created a presumption and precluded strip mining claimed by broad form deeds. The statute violated the separation of powers because it was the judiciary's function to determine the rights of parties to past transactions. In the second action, strip miners filed an action against the surface owners and sought a declaration of rights to strip mine on the subject property by terms of a broad form deed. The lower court denied the relief sought and the court reversed. The court determined that strip mining could occur, however, the court held that the strip miners were required to pay damages to the surface owners for all damages caused to the property.


OUTCOME: The court certified the constitutional challenge to the applicable statute in the first action and declared a portion of the statute that created a presumption that broad form deeds precluded strip mining to be unconstitutional. In the second action, the court reversed the lower court's decision that denied strip mining and held that the strip miners would have to pay damages to the surface owners for all damages caused on the property.

 

161 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Hayes v. State Property & Bldgs. Com.


Nos. 86-SC-918-TG, 86-SC-1041-TG, 86-SC-1042-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


731 S.W.2d 797; 1987 Ky. LEXIS 217



June 11, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion amended June 15, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT, HON. RAY CORNS, JUDGE, 86-CI-0884.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state budget director and citizens, challenged a judgment from Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which determined in a declaratory judgment action that Senate Bill 361 adopted by the Kentucky General Assembly and the actions taken by appellee State Property and Buildings Commission were constitutional relating to certain incentives granted to an automobile manufacturer in building a new plant.


OVERVIEW: Attempting to alleviate state unemployment, the legislature passed a bill granting incentives to an automobile manufacturer to build a new plant and create jobs, opening opportunity for other projects. Appellants, state budget director and citizens, challenged the bill's constitutionality, bringing a declaratory judgment action against appellee State Property and Buildings Commission. The trial court found the bill constitutional, and on review, the court affirmed, finding that no conveyance of publicly financed property without receiving fair market value would occur and that appellee made the required statutory findings. The court found that the legislation did not commit future funds to the project and that no appropriation was guaranteed in the next biennial budget. The court found that the manufacturer's tax obligation was significantly more than any other taxpayer, that the new taxes were incremental and would not exist but for the project, and that conveyance of the site was not a donation to a private corporation. The court found that new taxes would enhance state revenue and provide citizen benefits, but that no debt was created and no vote of the people was required.


OUTCOME: The court held that the bill passed by the legislature was constitutional and affirmed the trial court's decision in favor of appellee State Property and Buildings Commission and against appellants, state budget director and citizens. The project had a proper public purpose of alleviating unemployment. No state donation was made to a private corporation and the manufacturer received no special treatment.

Smith v. Commonwealth


No. 83-SC-799-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


734 S.W.2d 437; 1987 Ky. LEXIS 200



April 2, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM PIKE CIRCUIT COURT HON. REED ANDERSON, JUDGE, Criminal No. 80-CR-166.



DISPOSITION:  Considering the case as a whole we find no unfairness in the trial situation. Therefore the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Pike Circuit Court (Kentucky) convicting him of one count of intentional murder and three counts of transferred intentional murder pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 507.020(1)(a), and imposing a death sentence upon him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his constitutional rights were violated because of an alleged underrepresentation of women and young adults in the grand and petit jury pools, that the trial court erred in excusing for cause a juror whose wife was his second cousin, and that he was improperly sentenced to death. The supreme court affirmed defendant's convictions and death sentence. Defendant, a 32-year-old white male, lacked standing under the equal protection clause to challenge the grand jury pool on the grounds that young people and women were underrepresented. As to the petit jury, defendant's argument failed because he failed to show that any underrepresentation of women was due to their systematic exclusion in the jury selection process. The trial judge's exclusion of the juror because of the possibility of kinship rendering the juror less than a fair and impartial juror was reasonable and was not reversible error. Also, defendant was properly sentenced to death based on the existence of the aggravating factor that his act or acts of killing were intentional and resulted in multiple deaths.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and death sentence were affirmed.

Gaines v. Commonwealth

DISPOSITION:  Reversing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Campbell Circuit Court (Kentucky) convicting him for first-degree sodomy and sentencing him to 20 years imprisonment. He was also challenged his conviction for first-degree sexual abuse and sentence to five years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree sodomy and first-degree sexual abuse. Hawkins v. Sunmark Industries, Inc.


No. 85-SC-1006-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


727 S.W.2d 397; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 323



December 18, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied April 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS, No. 84-CA-1952-MR, Jefferson Circuit Court No. 79-CI-11039.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING IN PART/REVERSING IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant firemen were injured by an explosion at a fire caused by appellee motorist who backed into a gasoline dispenser at appellee service station. Appellees included the property owners and the dispenser manufacturer. The trial court dismissed all claims on the grounds that they were barred by the fireman's rule. The Kentucky Court of Appeals affirmed the trial court, and the firemen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motorist accidentally bumped against a gasoline dispenser located at the service station. Although the collision was relatively minor, the gasoline dispenser was knocked loose and a short circuit occurred initiating a small fire. The fire department responded almost immediately. Within seconds after their arrival, as one of the firemen was approaching the dispenser, the small fire exploded into a firebomb causing serious injuries to all three firemen. Disputed evidence indicated that the cause of the explosion was a build-up of pressure due to a failure of a relief valve caused by either defective design or construction of the gasoline dispenser. The firemen claimed that the fireman's rule was unconstitutional because it limited their access to the courts. The court decided that there was a public policy reason for the continued viability of the rule, an ancient, longstanding rule of law and thus would apply to appellees who were owners or occupiers of the premises. However, because the manufacturer was neither an owner nor occupant of the premises the Fireman's Rule would have no application to this claim if it could be substantiated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower courts' grant of summary judgment to appellees who were owners or occupiers of the premises and reversed and remanded as to the gasoline dispenser manufacturer.

Reda Pump Co., Div. of TRW, Inc. v. Finck


No. 85-SC-553-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


713 S.W.2d 818; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 283



July 3, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON TRANSFER FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS (Jefferson Circuit Court No. 79-CI-05833)



DISPOSITION:  The judgment is reversed with direction that the complaint and the intervening complaint be dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant manufacturer sought review of an order from the Court of Appeals, Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which submitted the products liability action to a jury under a comparative negligence instruction. The jury found that both appellant and appellee were negligent.


OVERVIEW: Appellee brought suit when he was injured by a pump, produced by appellant manufacturer, exploded. Appellee claimed damages based upon negligence, breach of warranty, and strict liability, and the trial court submitted the case under a comparative negligence instruction. The jury prorated liability 34.25 percent to appellee and 65.75 percent to appellant. Appellant sought review, and the court granted transfer of the appeal. The court held that the matter was deemed to be a products liability action and fell under the Products Liability Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 411.300 -- 411.350. Moreover, under the plain meaning of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.320(3), the contributory negligence of appellant was an absolute bar to recovery of damages. The judgment was reversed, and the complaint was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed with direction that the complaint and the intervening complaint be dismissed because appellee's contributory negligence was an absolute bar to recovery against appellant manufacture.

Commonwealth v. Willis


No. 85-SC-218-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


716 S.W.2d 224; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 281



July 3, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied October 16, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT, HON. GEORGE BARKER, JUDGE, 84-CR-346



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of the decision of the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky), which denied the State's request to take the testimony of a five-year-old sexual abuse victim, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 421.350(3), (4), (5), and held the sections were unconstitutional because they denied defendant the right to confrontation and violated the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for first-degree sexual abuse. He filed a motion to exclude the testimony of the child victim and claimed that she was incompetent to testify. A competency hearing was held, and the trial court was unable to rule on whether the victim was competent because her answers were unresponsive. The State then pursued a motion to permit the use of television cameras to present the victim's testimony. The trial court sustained defendant's motion to exclude the testimony of the child witness and ruled that §§ (3), (4), (5) were unconstitutional and violated the separation of powers doctrine under the state constitution. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case. The court held that defendant's rights were to be balanced with the legitimate concern for the victim. Defendant's right of confrontation was fully protected as required by the state constitution, the Sixth Amendment, and Ky. R. Crim. P. 7.12. There was no constitutional right to face-to-face confrontation, and the right to be present at trial and the right to confrontation were to be applied in such a way as to produce a fair result and enhance the truth-determining process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court, which denied the State's request to take the testimony of a five-year-old sexual abuse victim.

Thompson v. Kentucky Reinsurance Asso.


No. 85-SC-17-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


710 S.W.2d 854; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 266



May 22, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE RAY CORNS, JUDGE, 84-CI-0661



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the General Assembly of the Commonwealth and the Secretary of Finance, sought review of a decision of the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee Kentucky Reinsurance Association (KRA) in its action for declaratory and injunctive relief pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 342.122, 342.123 related to appellants' attempted appropriation of KRA funds.


OVERVIEW: The KRA operated to fund payments of the Special Fund, from which workers compensation payments were made. The KRA was a statutorily created nonprofit corporation and was given all "general corporate powers" under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.123(1). Appellants sought the transfer of funds held by the KRA to the State's general fund pursuant to 1984 Ky. Acts 410, 418 which provided for transfer of funds from trust and agency accounts to the State's general fund and conferred upon the General Assembly the right to suspend operation of existing statutes if the State's financial condition required such action. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the funds collected by the KRA were private, as opposed to public funds, and were not subject to the authority of the General Assembly. The attempt by appellants to divert the KRA's private funds pursuant to 1984 Ky. Acts 410, 418 was invalid. Under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 342.122, 342.123, the sole corporate purpose of the KRA was to independently fund the liabilities of the Special Fund through private sources, and not to meet the needs for general administration of the State's government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Commonwealth ex rel. Armstrong v. Collins


No. 85-SC-155-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


709 S.W.2d 437; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 262



May 1, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE WILLIAM L. GRAHAM, JUDGE, NO. 84-CI-0787



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART, REVERSING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the judgment for appellees, a governor, a state finance secretary, and a state treasurer, by the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky). The trial court ruled that H.B. 474, ch. 418, 1984 Reg. Session (Ky. 1984) (budget law), permitting the transfer of funds from trust and agency accounts to the General Fund, and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 446.085 did not offend Ky. Const. §§ 15 and 51.


OVERVIEW: Faced with an emergency financial situation, the General Assembly passed a budget that included the budget law and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 446.085 (modification law) that gave the assembly the authority in a budget bill to suspend or modify the operation of an existing statute if the financial condition of the state required such action. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in part and reversed it in part. The court held that the assembly had the constitutional power to suspend or modify the operation of existing statutes and that it clearly had the power to enact legislation regarding the budget. Moreover, the court ruled that both the budget law and the modification law satisfied the title requirements in Ky. Const. § 51, because both titles gave a "clue" as to the content of the legislation and were not deceitful. The court also ruled that the budget enactments did not constitute a repeal or an amendment of previous laws with regard to most specific appropriations. But the trust and agency fund transfers involving the transfer of money from agencies in which public funds and private employee contributions were commingled were found to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in part and reversed it in part. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling that found that two recently enacted laws were not outside the scope of the legislature authority, but it reversed the trial court's ruling that permitted the legislature to transfer private funds to the general fund because such a transfer of private funds was unconstitutional.

Bevins v. Commonwealth


No. 83-SC-805-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


712 S.W.2d 932; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 252



March 20, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 7, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM GREENUP CIRCUIT COURT, HON. JAMES D. ATKINSON, JUDGE (Indictment Nos. 82-CR-016 and 023)



DISPOSITION:  The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Greenup Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted defendant of five murders pursuant to a plea of guilty and sentenced him to death. Upon entry of his plea, defendant waived sentencing by jury and submitted the issue of aggravating, mitigating, or extenuating circumstances to the trial judge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised, inter alia, assignments of error as to the trial judge's conduct of the penalty phase of the proceedings and the constitutionality and administration of the death penalty statute. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of five murders and imposing a capital sentence.

Fireman's Fund Ins. Co. v. Sherman & Fletcher


NO. 84-SC-279-DG, NO, 84-SC-274-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


705 S.W.2d 459; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 239



February 27, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS NO. 83-CA-859-MR (Jefferson Circuit Court NO. 79-CI-03064); ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, NOS. 83-CA-852-MR and 83-CA-1435-MR (Jefferson Circuit Court NO. 79-CI-03064)



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Review of order from the Kentucky Court of Appeals, which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of all claims against respondent contractors in suit by movant insurer who sought to indemnify itself against the contractors for any damages it might be required to pay to the estate administratrix because of a subcontractor employee's wrongful death.


OVERVIEW: An employee of a subcontractor was killed at the construction site. His employer paid worker's compensation benefits to the estate. The estate sought wrongful death recovery against the contractors. The insurer sought indemnity. The court affirmed the summary judgment grant to the contractors on the estate's claim because the worker's compensation statutes precluded such recovery. The contractor would have had to pay worker's compensation benefits to the estate if the subcontractor had not and that potential liability relieved the contractors from tort liability. The court declined to consider the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 342.690 because the issue was not raised in the Court of Appeals. Because the deceased employer secured the worker's compensation benefits, the actual dollar amount that the contractors became obligated to pay as compensation benefits to the deceased was zero. The statute thus limits the liability of the contractors to zero dollars. The court held that the statute limited the liability of the contractors to another who paid benefits on account of injury or death of an employee to the amount of compensation for which the contractor was liable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

173 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Musselman v. Commonwealth


No. 85-SC-28-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


705 S.W.2d 476; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 242



February 27, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 83-CA-1726-DG (Jefferson Circuit Court No. 82-XX-0122)



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky) that reversed a decision of the circuit court and held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 525.070(1)(b) was constitutional and found him guilty of violating the harassment statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding, and he used profane language towards the police officer. The district court found him guilty of a violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 525.070(1)(b), the harassment statute. He appealed to the circuit court, which held that the statute was impermissibly broad and that it imposed an undue restriction on constitutional guarantees of free speech under U.S. Const. amend. I and Ky. Const. § 8. The court of appeals reversed, holding that the statute could be construed as limited in its application to situations where the offensively coarse utterance or abusive language amounted to fighting words that had a direct tendency to cause acts of violence by the person to whom, individually, the remark was addressed. The court of appeals held that so construed the statute was constitutional. On further appeal, the court reversed. The court held that, as written, the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The statute itself had no measuring stick, so that, consistent with its terms, in a broad range of cases, persons could be found guilty of its violation in circumstances that would infringe constitutional guarantees of free speech.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that set aside defendant's conviction under the harassment statute.

Board of Education v. Taulbee


Nos. 85-SC-435-TG, 85-SC-488-TRG, 85-SC-489-TRG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


706 S.W.2d 827; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 245



February 27, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 1, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 85-CA-1474-P (Fayette Circuit Court #84-CI-3394); ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 85-CA-236-I (Fayette Circuit Court #81-CI-3113); ON TRANSFER FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 85-CA-1393-P (Fayette Circuit Court #84-CI-3394)



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Board of Education and Department of Revenue, challenged judgments of the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky), which dismissed the board's complaint seeking a permanent injunction to restrain the sheriff from refunding to appellee class of taxpayers a portion of their 1981 school taxes from current school taxes in his possession and that required the sheriff to make the refunds. The actions were transferred from the court of appeals.


OVERVIEW: After the property owners brought an action successfully challenging the constitutionality of assessments on agricultural land, the board filed an action seeking a permanent injunction to restrain the sheriff from making refunds, and the property owners filed an action seeking to require the sheriff to make the refunds. The court reversed the judgments requiring the sheriff to make the refunds, holding that the property owners were not entitled to automatic refunds. Instead, individual applications pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590(6) had to be made in order to obtain a refund. The court also held that the board was never properly a party in the original lawsuit challenging the assessments; thus, the board was never able to contest the refund of school taxes, and the judgment was not enforceable against the board. Accordingly, refunds could only have been obtained from the Department of Revenue assessment of the tax liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments dismissing the board's action and requiring the sheriff to make requested tax refunds.

Smith v. Rogers


No. 84-SC-797-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


702 S.W.2d 425; 1986 Ky. LEXIS 227; 88 Oil & Gas Rep. 474



January 16, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, No. 83-CA-2447-MR (Warren Circuit Court 83-CI-278)



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lessors sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which reversed a decision from the Warren Circuit Court (Kentucky), which entered a declaratory judgment that oil leases from the lessors to appellee lessees had expired.


OVERVIEW: The lessors brought a declaratory judgment action against the lessees whereby the lessors sought a declaration that oil leases from the lessors to the lessees had expired. The trial court entered a judgment in favor of the lessors. The court of appeals reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that: (1) the provisions of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 353.630, 353.640, which stated that pooling had to be approved on an application to the oil and gas commission and that proper notice had to be given to interested surface owners and that a hearing had to be held, did not apply to voluntary pooling, where as provided in the instant leases, it could only be done in furtherance of conservation; (2) the trial court erred when it held that the permit issued to commence drilling was ineffective because Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 353.570(3) was unconstitutional inasmuch as it was vague and uncertain; (3) the statute was not uncertain and because the attorney general was not notified of the constitutional attack, it could not be raised; and (4) the record did not show that the authorization to begin drilling was arbitrary or contravened the statutory or lease requirement of conservation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals.

Yonts v. Commonwealth


No. 85-SC-303-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


700 S.W.2d 407; 1985 Ky. LEXIS 285



November 21, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [**1] AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Education member challenged the judgment of the Muhlenberg Circuit Court (Kentucky), which upheld the validity of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 160.180, in appellee attorney general's action seeking to declare forfeited the office of the member.


OVERVIEW: The board member was elected as a board member for the school district. In 1981, he became a candidate for the office of state representative. He was unsuccessful in the primary election. When the election to the office of state representative next came around, he again ran for the nomination and was not successful. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court determined that it was the law of the commonwealth that when the board member became a candidate for state representative, there were clear grounds for his removal as a board member. The court explained that such removal could have only been accomplished by the attorney general. The court concluded that the board member's contention that § 160.180 violated the Kentucky constitution was not subject to appellate review because it was not presented in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which upheld the validity of statute, in the attorney general's action seeking to declare forfeited the office of the board member.

 

177 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Tabler v. Wallace


Nos. 84-SC-844-DG, 85-SC-63-TRG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


704 S.W.2d 179; 1985 Ky. LEXIS 291



November 21, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing February 27, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, #83-CA-2160-MR (Fayette Circuit Court #81-CI-0166); APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT, HON. BENJAMIN F. SHOBE, JUDGE, NO. 79-CI-01275



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING IN PART/REVERSING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured parties filed separate actions for personal injuries against defendants, architects and builders, when an elevator malfunctioned and a warehouse roof collapsed. The trial courts granted summary judgments in favor of the architects and builders under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.135. The Court of Appeals (Kentucky) reversed one judgment, held § 413.135 unconstitutional, and transferred the consolidated cases for review.


OVERVIEW: The trial courts granted summary judgment on grounds that the claims were not filed within five years of completion of construction, pursuant to § 413.135. The appeals court concluded that § 413.135 was nothing more than an arbitrary grant of immunity to architects and builders with no reasonable basis for a separate classification. The court affirmed the appeals court and reversed the trial court because § 413.135 violated Ky. Const. § 59(5). No substantial reason for special immunity was presented. The only apparent basis for the present legislation was that a special class, builders, architects, and engineers involved in construction, faced with a growing exposure to litigation, lobbied for a statute limiting their liability. There was no social or economic basis presented to justify a special class, only their own self-interest. Their subjective reasons could not withstand public policy analysis. The arbitrariness of providing immunity to those engaged in design and construction of a real estate improvement which did not extend to others similarly situated was the essence of the constitutional evil addressed by the prohibition against local and special legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appeals court decision which reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the architect and builder. The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the architect and builder.

Commonwealth v. Grimes


No. 85-SC-72-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


698 S.W.2d 836; 1985 Ky. LEXIS 281



October 31, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, No. 85-CA-2634-MR (Jefferson Circuit Court No. 82-CR-0777)



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), holding that a conviction pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.990(2) could not be enhanced pursuant to the general persistent felony offender statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was originally convicted of trafficking in a controlled substance second offense. In the second part of the bifurcated proceedings, defendant was found guilty of being a persistent felony offender (PFO) in the second degree. On the first appeal, the court reversed the decision relating to the propriety of the search and seizure of the drugs, which was subsequently vacated and remanded by the appellate court because the use of defendant's subsequent offender convictions under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.990(2) as a springboard in obtaining a PFO status was improper. On discretionary review, the court reversed the appellate court because the trial court did not commit reversible error by allowing the second offense trafficking conviction to be enhanced by the PFO statute. A conviction of a second offense of trafficking in a Schedule III controlled substance under § 218A.990(2), was permitted to be further enhanced by a persistent felony offender second degree charge pursuant to the general PFO statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.080, where the PFO charge was grounded on a prior, unrelated conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision.

 

179 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Transit Authority of Lexington-Fayette Urban County Government v. Amalgamated Transit Union, Local 639


No. 84-SC-1124-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


698 S.W.2d 520; 1985 Ky. LEXIS 266



September 5, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 21, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE N. MITCHELL MEADE, JUDGE (NO. 84-CI-1625)



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant transit authority, which was created as a political subdivision and a public body corporate pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 96A.020, filed an appeal from the judgment of the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky), which found in favor of appellee union in its suit to compel arbitration of the proposed changes to the parties' collective bargaining agreement pursuant to the arbitration provisions of that agreement.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the trial court's judgment. Ky. Const. § 162 provided that no municipality was authorized to pay any claim created against it under any agreement made without express authority of law, and all such unauthorized agreements were null and void. The court held that the transit authority fell within the classification of a municipal corporation whose policy-making function could not be delegated. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 96A.020 provided that a transit authority constituted an agency and instrumentality for accomplishing essential governmental functions of the public body creating it. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 96A.040 and 96A.070(6) provided that the transit agency was to be managed and controlled by a board and the board was to fix the salaries of its agents and employees. The duties imposed by statute upon the members of the transit agency's board could not be delegated. Thus, the arbitration clause, which purported to delegate to an arbitrator the management function of the transit agency's board, was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for the union.

 

180 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Howard v. Salyer


No. 84-SC-258-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


695 S.W.2d 420; 1985 Ky. LEXIS 247



July 3, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 26, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 83-CA-360-MR (Magoffin Circuit Court 81-CI-255)



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant prohibitionists appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals of Kentucky upholding a lower court's decision favoring respondent anti-prohibitionists in the latters' effort to repeal a county sub-division's prohibition law.


OVERVIEW: Movant prohibitionists and respondent anti-prohibitionists lived in a dry magisterial district i.e., a county subdivision in which the sale or consumption of alcohol was prohibited. The anti-prohibitionists succeeded in having the question of the repeal of prohibition in the district placed on the ballot for a referendum. A majority of the district's voters approved of the repeal of prohibition in the district. When the anti-prohibitionists sought to have that repeal implemented, however, the prohibitionists moved to block that enforcement, claiming a violation of the county unit rule (a statutory rule requiring, on prohibition matters, the county to vote wet or dry as a unit). Both the judge to whom the matter was originally assigned and three intermediate appellate judges rejected the prohibitionists' argument, and they appealed. On appeal, the court reversed. It held that although there was indeed another statute also dealing with prohibition referendums, that statute did not modify, expressly or implicitly, the county unit rule statute. That statute controlled, and under it the sub-county referendum held in this case was void. Judgment was ordered entered in movants' favor.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and entered in favor of the prohibitionists.

 

181 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. Motorists Ins. Cos.


No. 84-SC-895-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


695 S.W.2d 415; 1985 Ky. LEXIS 234



June 13, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing September 5, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, NO. 83-CA-2635-MR (Jefferson Circuit Court - No. 83-CI-03538)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the decision by the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which held that he was not entitled to a statutory attorney's fee from appellee client's insurance company. The attorney sought the fee, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. § 304.39-070 (5), for his work in settling his client's claim with the liability insurance carrier of the tortfeasor whose car struck the vehicle of the attorney's client.


OVERVIEW: The client's motorist insurance policy included basic reparations benefits. The attorney claimed he was owed a statutory fee from his client's insurance company for having settled his client's claim with the tortfeasor's insurance carrier. The trial court ruled the attorney was not entitled to the fee and dismissed the case. The appellate court affirmed the trial court. On appeal, the court determined the question was whether the mandatory language of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 304.39-070 (5) meant that his client's insurance company, as reparations obligor, was required to pay the attorney a statutory fee. The court held the statute did not require payment. The court ruled that where liability was conceded in the case, where the reparations obligor had notified the tortfeasor's insurer of its subrogation, where its right to payment was not in dispute, and where there was no proof that the attorney's work conferred any benefits on the reparations obligor, directly or indirectly, then a reasonable fee was no fee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court and the judgment of the trial court that the attorney was not entitled to a fee because there was no proof his work had conferred any benefits on the reparations obligor.

Graham v. Mills


No. 85-SC-181-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


694 S.W.2d 698; 1985 Ky. LEXIS 236



June 13, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 5, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEALS, No. 84-CA-2712-OA



DISPOSITION:  REVERSING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial judge and the Commonwealth challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which granted defendant a writ of prohibition restraining the trial judge from conducting further criminal proceedings against defendant while the Attorney General acted as prosecutor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, the State Treasurer, was indicted for offenses related to her office. The Attorney General acted as prosecutor and defendant objected, asserting that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15.715(4) was unconstitutional as special legislation. The court disagreed and reversed, allowing the prosecution to go forward. The court found that defendant had an adequate remedy at law, just as all defendants do who raise a constitutional question. Therefore, prohibition was inappropriate. In addition, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15.715(4) was constitutional and was not special legislation. Instead, it granted the Attorney General authority to prosecute all crimes against the State Treasury, regardless of the occupation or location of a defendant. Allowing venue to be had in Franklin County was similarly reasonable and proper, considering the crimes involved and considering the fact that Franklin County was the seat of government.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the granting of a writ of prohibition. The writ was dissolved. The prosecution of defendant was allowed to continue with the Attorney General as prosecutor.

Delta Air Lines, Inc. v. Commonwealth, Revenue Cabinet


No. 84-SC-44-DG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


689 S.W.2d 14; 1985 Ky. LEXIS 225



May 2, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REVIEW FROM COURT OF APPEALS, 82-CA-2560-MR & 82-CA-2591-MR (Franklin Circuit Court Nos. 81-CI-1347 & 81-CI-1126)



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which determined that respondent Commonwealth of Kentucky Revenue Cabinet (revenue cabinet) was entitled to tax jet fuel used by the taxpayer pursuant to KY. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 139.480(16) and that a remand was required for findings of fact as to the taxability of food.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the taxpayer challenged the constitutionality of KY. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 139.200, which imposed state taxes on intrastate food and fuel purchases. The tax, circuit, and appellate courts upheld the assessment against the taxpayer as to fuel purchases. The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment and concluded that a remand was necessary to determine issues of fact as to the taxation of food. Nevertheless, § 139.200 unambiguously imposed a uniform, non-discriminatory sales tax that applied to local fuel transactions without offending the Commerce Clause. The taxpayer did not meet its burden of showing that it was entitled to an exemption or that the classification subjecting it to taxation was hostile and oppressive in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment. Rather, the presumption of legislative regularity was not rebutted. Neither the doctrine of contemporaneous construction nor a contrary agency interpretation altered that result because § 139.200 was unambiguous, and the court owed little deference to an erroneous interpretation of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's determination that jet fuel was subject to state sales tax, and it determined that findings of fact were necessary to assess the taxability of food.

Commonwealth v. Hollingsworth


NO. 83-SC-497-TRG


SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY


685 S.W.2d 546; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 278



December 20, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 21, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON CERTIFICATION FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT, #82-CR-10342, HONORABLE RICHARD A. REVELL, JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commonwealth of Kentucky, sought review of a decision of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which ordered a verdict of acquittal be entered on behalf of defendant, who was indicted for trafficking in a Schedule III controlled substance, pentazocine, contrary to Ky. Rev. Stat. § 218 A.140.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the guidelines set out for classification of substances in Ky. Rev. Stat. § 218A.020 were not mandatory, and therefore, the statute was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power. Defendant alleged that even if the statute was constitutional, the regulation adding pentazocine to Schedule III, 902 Ky. Admin. Regs. 55:025, was constitutionally defective because it did not state that the cabinet had considered the eight items listed in Ky. Rev. Stat. § 218A.020 in addition to the standards stated in Ky. Rev. Stat. § 212A.080 when it determined pentazocine in pill form should be controlled. The court ruled that § 218A.020 and the statutes that followed it were constitutional because the individual statutes listing the criteria for a particular classification read in combination with § 218A.020 set out specific mandatory standards to be used by the cabinet of human resources in classifying substances. The regulation was constitutional because the eight factors merged into any consideration of the potential for abuse. Thus, § 218A.080 itself set forth adequate standards for the cabinet to use in classifying a substance under 902 Ky. Admin. Regs. 55:025.


OUTCOME: The court certified as constitutional the law regarding the classification of pentazocine as a Schedule III controlled substance.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant alcoholic beverage control board sought review of a judgment from the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted summary judgment to appellee liquor store on its action that challenged appellant's decision that denied appellee's application for a retail beer license pursuant to Ky. OVERVIEW: The alcoholic beverage control board (Board) had denied the liquor store's application for a retail beer license pursuant to § 243.220(3)(a) because it was located approximately 91 feet from a church. Commonwealth v. Littrell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Kentucky


677 S.W.2d 881; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 285



October 4, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22A.020(4), the Commonwealth of Kentucky challenged a judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted defendant's motion for a new trial based upon newly discovered evidence and set aside the jury's verdict finding defendant guilty of robbery. In a second trial, defendant was acquitted. The Commonwealth sought to vacate the acquittal and the grant of a new trial and to reinstate the conviction.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of robbery, but before formal sentencing, the trial court granted his motion for a new trial. In a prior appeal filed by the Commonwealth before the second trial in which defendant was acquitted, the court held that there was no appeal from an interlocutory decree granting a new trial. After defendant was acquitted in the second trial, the Commonwealth filed the subject appeal, arguing that the granting of the new trial was erroneous and that the second trial was a nullity. The court held that under § 22A.020(4) in the prior appeal, the Kentucky Court of Appeals had no authority to set aside the order granting a new trial, which the court had overturned in a prior opinion, and was limited to certifying the law. The court further held that once defendant was placed on trial by the swearing of a legally impaneled jury and the reception of evidence, he was in jeopardy. The court further found that the jury had the power and the authority to find defendant guilty and to assess a severe punishment against him. Additionally, the court explained that the acquittal served as a complete and final bar as to any further proceedings against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the Commonwealth's motion to vacate the judgment of acquittal, its motion to vacate the order granting a new trial, and its motion to reinstate the jury's verdict. The court affirmed the final judgment acquitting defendant.

American Trucking Asso. v. Commonwealth, Transp. Cabinet


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Kentucky


676 S.W.2d 785; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 268



September 13, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a trucking association, a transport association, and several trucking companies, sought review of judgments from the trial court (Kentucky), which granted partial summary judgment to appellees, the transportation cabinet, the department of vehicle regulation, and members of both agencies, on their challenge to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 138.660 and upheld the validity of 601 Ky. Admin. Regs. 9.072E(15)(7).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, appellants contended that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 138.660, the weight-distance tax, denied them equal protection of law because the tax was imposed on an arbitrary basis without relation to any proper or reasonable classification. Appellants also contended that 601 Ky. Admin. Regs. 9.072E(15)(7) exceeded the statutory authority granted to the cabinet and that the regulation violated the privileges and immunities clause because it discriminated against out-of-state carriers. Upon review, the court held that the regulation went beyond the scope of the regulatory authority granted for the transportation cabinet by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 138.661.There was no indication of the intent of the General Assembly that auditing fees were to be assessed against the carriers for whom the audit was to be performed. To the contrary, it appeared that in making provision for the expenses of auditing from allotment from the transportation fund, the General Assembly expressed an intent that the necessary expenses of audit be born by the cabinet and not the individual carriers. For that reason the regulation in question was inconsistent with § 138.661 and was invalid.


OUTCOME: The partial summary judgment that upheld the constitutionality of the statute imposing a weight-distance tax was affirmed. The judgment that upheld the validity of the regulation concerning assessment of audit fees against carriers whose books required auditing outside the Commonwealth of Kentucky was reversed.

 

192 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Perry County Fiscal Court v. Commonwealth


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Kentucky


674 S.W.2d 954; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 243



July 5, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified September 13, 1984.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a county fiscal court (county), appealed a decision from the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which, in part, affirmed an order of appellee, a trial court judge, who ordered the county to pay for certain experts requested by an indigent prisoner as part of his defense to a capital crime.


OVERVIEW: The trial court initially ordered the fiscal court to pay for certain experts for defendant's use in his homicide trial. The fiscal court alleged that it had no funds with which to comply with the order, and the trial court then excluded the death penalty from defendant's trial because the fiscal court could not provide the funds. The commonwealth filed a petition in the court of appeals to prohibit the trial court from enforcing the order that excluded the death penalty, and the court of appeals required that the fiscal court provide the funds and obey the trial court's order. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 31.185 already provided that any defending attorney operating under the provisions of the public advocacy system was entitled to use the same state facilities for evaluation of evidence as were available to the attorney representing the commonwealth. If it considered their use impractical, the court concerned could authorize the use of private facilities to be paid for by the county. Therefore, the county was directed and ordered to pay the reasonable fees of such expert witnesses as were reasonably necessary for the defendant's defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order and held that the county was directed and ordered to pay the reasonable fees of such expert witnesses as were reasonably necessary for defendant in the homicide trial.

 

193 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Smothers v. Lewis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Kentucky


672 S.W.2d 62; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 256; 42 A.L.R.4th 509



July 5, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner licensee challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kentucky), which granted respondent board's request for relief from the trial court's temporary restraining order to stay the board's order revoking the licensee's retail beer license, upheld the board's order of revocation, and upheld the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 243.580.


OVERVIEW: The licensee's retail beer license was revoked by the board. The licensee appealed seeking a temporary restraining order to stay the order, and the trial court granted the licensee's request. The appellate court issued an order staying the temporary restraining order and upholding the board's revocation order and upholding the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 243.580, which in effect prohibited all courts from interfering with an order of revocation of an alcoholic beverage license during an appeal. The court reversed concluding that § 243.580 was unconstitutional as being in violation of Ky. Const. §§ 109, 116, 27, and 28. The court concluded that the statutes were unconstitutional because its prohibitions against injunctive relief pending appeals were legislative encroachments upon the powers of the judicial branch of government. The court found that the legislature attempted to limit the court's power to stay a possibly unjustly imposed punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's order staying the injunction and held that the statute prohibiting the licensee from appealing the board's order revoking his retail beer license was unconstitutional.

 

194 of 908 DOCUMENTS


In re Beverly Hills Fire Litigation


No. 84-SC-33-CL


Supreme Court of Kentucky


672 S.W.2d 922; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 239



May 31, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] AS TO ALL CASES CIVIL NO. 77-79


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action tort suit involving a fire that destroyed a building and resulted in deaths and injuries, the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Kentucky certified to the court for decision a question of Kentucky law as it applied to the litigation. The question certified was whether Ky. Rev. Stat. § 413.135 was unconstitutional as applied to facts of the case by virtue of Ky. Const. §§ 14, 54 and/or 241.


OVERVIEW: Ky. Rev. Stat. § 413.135 was the "no action" statute that limited the period in which actions could be brought against architects and builders for any deficiencies in their work. The federal district court had originally expressed the opinion that § 413.135 was not applicable to the facts of the case, but the federal appeals court designated the defendant manufacturers in the case as materialmen who designed products for construction projects, and as such, within the contemplation of § 413.135. The court concluded that: (1) properly construed, § 413.135 had no application to what was essentially a products liability case because its language did not express coverage for materialmen or cover construction projects unless they were an improvement to real property;and (2) otherwise construed, § 413.135 would be special legislation in violation of Ky. Const. § 59 because if Ky. Rev. Stat. § 413.135 was interpreted to include in its protection the manufacturer of a product simply because the product was used as a component part in construction of a building, it would discriminate in favor of such person arbitrarily and beyond reasonable justification in violation of Ky. Const. § 59.


OUTCOME: The court did not address the underlying question of the constitutionality of a "no action" statute as to those persons who were within its purview. In response to the question certified, the court answered that the statute was not applicable to the case.

 

195 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Farris v. Shoppers Village Liquors, Inc.


No. 83-SC-116-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


669 S.W.2d 213; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 236



May 10, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT, #82-CI-1158, HONORABLE SQUIRE N. WILLIAMS, JUDGE



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, members of the Alcoholic Beverage Board of Kentucky, appealed a decision of the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) holding that Ky. Rev. Stat. § 243.892 was unconstitutional and issuing an injunction permanently enjoining the members from enforcing the statute. After the notice of appeal was filed, a joint motion for transfer was granted.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, a corporation and others, brought an action seeking a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. § 243.892. The trial court ruled the statute was a violation of Ky. Const. §§ 47 and 51 and issued an injunction permanently enjoining the members from enforcing the same. The members appealed, and a joint motion for transfer was granted by the court. Upon review, the court affirmed the unconstitutionality of the statute. First, the statute was not germane to the subject matter suggested by the title, "An Act Relating to Revenue and Taxation," so that it did not satisfy the notice requirement of Ky. Const. § 51. Furthermore, since the statute did not relate to the subject matter of revenue and taxation, it violated Ky. Const. § 47, which prohibited the Senate from attaching amendments that did not relate to the subject matter. However, the permanent injunction was dissolved so that the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control could enforce those statutes not affected by the instant ruling.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the injunction was dissolved.

 

196 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Basham v. Commonwealth


Nos. 82-SC-689-MR, 82-SC-391-TG, 82-SC-674-TRG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


675 S.W.2d 376; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 229



April 19, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 4, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM BOYLE CIRCUIT COURT, HON HENRY V. PENNINGTON, JUDGE, (Indictment Nos. 82-CR-003, 82-CR-007 and 82-CR-020); APPEAL FROM BOYLE CIRCUIT COURT, HON. HENRY V. PENNINGTON, JUDGE, (Indictment Nos. 82-CR-003, 82-CR-004, 82-CR-007, 82-CR-008 and 82-CR-017); APPEAL FROM BOYLE CIRCUIT COURT, HON. HENRY V. PENNINGTON, JUDGE, (Indictment Nos. 82-CR-005, 82-CR-006 and 82-CR-022)



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Boyle Circuit Court (Kentucky) convicted defendants of various crimes, including knowingly receiving stolen property, counterfeiting, and possession or trafficking in controlled substances. Defendants appealed, arguing that the evidence seized pursuant to a federal wiretap order was improperly admitted because Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 526 et seq. prohibited evidence obtained by electronic surveillance.


OVERVIEW: Evidence against the defendants was obtained during a federal wiretap operation conducted pursuant to a federal wiretap order. The evidence was turned over to the state police who used it to obtain state search warrants. The wiretap evidence was also admitted during trial. However, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 526 et seq. made any electronic surveillance unlawful. The court held that the statute did not prohibit federal officers from conducting a wiretap operation pursuant to a valid federal wiretap order. The statute likewise did not prohibit all use of evidence obtained by electronic surveillance. If the evidence was illegally seized by federal officers, state officers could not use it. If there was collusion between federal and state authorities attempting to avoid the prohibitions of the statute, the evidence would be inadmissible. The court determined that there was a separate federal investigation of defendants in progress and that the federal officers substantially complied with the procedural steps to obtain and carry out the wiretap order; though the parties shared information and combined their efforts in investigating defendants, they did not collude to avoid the statute.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions were affirmed.

 

197 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Kling v. Geary


No. 83-SC-610-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


667 S.W.2d 379; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 216



March 8, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE SQUIRE N. WILLIAMS, JR., JUDGE, No. 83-CI-0039



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county clerks challenged a decision of the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which upheld the constitutionality of Ky. H.R. 807 (1982) in favor of appellee Kentucky Secretary of Revenue.


OVERVIEW: H.R. 807 created a new system for collecting the ad valorem tax on motor vehicles, a part of which system involved collection by the county clerks at the time of registration or renewal of registration of the vehicle. Under the new method, motor vehicle taxes were to have been collected on the date of renewal of registration, which was determined by the birth month of the owner. On appeal, the clerks argued that the trial court erred in finding the legislation constitutional. The court disagree and affirmed the judgment. In doing so, the court held that (1) Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.487(3) did exclude motor vehicles from the compensating tax rate and the maximum tax rate, (2) the act itself did not become special legislation in contravention of Ky. Const. § 59(15), and (3) the legislature's classification of motor vehicles was upheld because the legislation established a classification made upon a reasonable and natural distinction that related logically to the purpose of the act. Further, the court held that the exemption for dealers was immaterial because the purchaser, whether from a dealer or an individual, was treated in exactly the same manner in both instances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Jackson v. Commonwealth


No. 82-SC-465-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


670 S.W.2d 828; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 205



February 16, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 5, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM WARREN CIRCUIT COURT, Honorable J. David Francis, Judge, No. 81-CR-645; NO. 82-SC-466-MR; APPEAL FROM WARREN CIRCUIT COURT, Honorable J. David Francis, Judge, NO. 81-CR-654; NO. 82-SC-464-MR; APPEAL FROM WARREN CIRCUIT COURT, Honorable J. David Francis, Judge, No. 81-CR-650



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an order of the Warren Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted them of various counts of burglary, theft by unlawful taking, and knowingly receiving stolen property, for their involvement in a series of burglaries after which they were found to have sold a number of items that had been stolen.


OVERVIEW: After a series of burglaries in neighboring counties, appellants were found to have sold property that had been stolen in the burglaries. Appellants were indicted separately, but were tried together. One appellant was convicted of three counts of burglary, ten counts of theft by unlawful taking, and ten counts of knowingly receiving stolen property and was sentenced to three life sentences and 10 10-year sentences. Another appellant was convicted of four counts of burglary, 13 counts of theft by unlawful taking, and 13 counts of knowingly receiving stolen property and was sentences as a persistent felony offender to three life sentences and 13 20-year sentences. The final appellant was convicted of one count of theft by unlawful taking and one count of knowingly receiving stolen property and was sentenced as a persistent felony offender to 2 20-year sentences. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that the first and second appellants were improperly convicted of theft of a scanner radio and of knowingly receiving stolen property. The final appellant was granted a separate trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that the first appellant was improperly convicted of theft of a scanner radio and of knowingly receiving stolen property. The second appellant also was improperly convicted of theft by unlawful taking of a radio scanner and of knowingly receiving stolen property. The final appellant was granted a separate trial from the other appellants.

McQueen v. Commonwealth


No. 81-SC-566-MR


Supreme Court of Kentucky


669 S.W.2d 519; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 210



February 16, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 14, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MADISON CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE JAMES S. CHENAULT, JUDGE, No. 80-CR-020



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Madison Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted defendant of first-degree robbery and murder and sentenced him to 20 years imprisonment for the robbery and death for the murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree robbery and murder for shooting a store clerk during the robbery. On appeal, defendant raised several errors regarding the jury, the guilt phase, and the sentencing phase of the trial. In affirming defendant's conviction and sentence, the court found that there was no abuse of discretion or errors. A juror was properly dismissed on the appearance of impropriety and for discussing the case with another person in violation of Ky. R. Crim. P. 9.70. Defendant was not denied a fair cross-section of the community on the jury panel because "young people" was not an identifiable group that could not be excluded. Employment of statisticians and mathematicians during jury venires was not statutorily authorized and the experts were not reasonably necessary. The mere mention of the words "polygraph" or "polygraph examiner" did not constitute a prejudicial error. Defendant's live-in girlfriend had the common authority and relationship to consent to a search of the resident. The sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor, and the evidence supported the findings of an aggravating circumstance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for armed robbery and murder.

 

200 of 908 DOCUMENTS


Dolan v. Land


No. 82-SC-997-TG


Supreme Court of Kentucky


667 S.W.2d 684; 1984 Ky. LEXIS 211



February 16, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified on Denial of Petition for Extention of Opinion May 10, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE L. T. GRANT, JUDGE, CIVIL ACTION NO. 81-CI-3113



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART AND REVERSING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property valuation administrator (PVA), Kentucky Department of Revenue (department), and others, challenged the judgment of the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky), which was entered in favor of appellee taxpayers and that determined that the PVA's method of assessment for agricultural and horticultural land was unconstitutional, and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 132.101(9), (10), 132.450(2)(a) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers owned farm land on which the PVA assessed taxes based on a method that resulted in the land being assigned a value based on general averages rather than on a value that was related to its agricultural purpose. The taxpayers brought an action that challenged the assessment. The circuit court entered a judgment in their favor, which the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the PVA's method was not constitutionally sound because the valuation of the land was based on a mathematical formula that was applied mechanically and failed to consider the individual characteristics of specific farm property. The method that was used failed to value the property on the basis of uniform standards and did not result in a tax that was equally burdensome on all farm taxpayers. The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 132.010(9), (10), 132.450(2)(a) did not violate the Kentucky Constitution because the qualifying standards for "agricultural land" or "horticultural land" were not unreasonable. The department was not required to prove that tax assessments imposed the same tax burdens on the farm owners in one county as opposed to another.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment that was entered in favor of the taxpayers on their challenge of the assessment process employed by defendants.
